Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Parent-Child Testimony Rejected due to Tuhma
Ruling with hadith and rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony between parents and children and explain its basis in the hadith and rational proof (interconnected benefits).

Core Idea
Parent-child testimony is rejected because mutual benefits create tuhma (suspicion of partiality).

In Hanafi fiqh, a witness must be free from any suspicion of bias. This lesson examines a specific ruling: a father cannot testify for his child, nor a child for his parent, due to the interconnected economic benefits between them. We will explore the primary evidence from the Prophet's hadith and the rational analogy that supports this prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is a parent testifying for a child or vice versa. The ruling is that such testimony is not accepted (ghayr maqbul) due to tuhma (suspicion of partiality).
This is a hukm wad'i (validity ruling).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: 'لا يقبل شهادة الولد لوالده ولا الوالد لولده...' (the testimony of a child for his parent is not accepted, nor of a parent for his child...).
The hadith also lists other relationships (spouses, master-slave, employer-worker).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit negation indicates prohibition. In Hanafi usul, a negative statement of rejection signifies the act is invalid. The rational proof is that benefits between parents and children are interconnected, which creates tuhma.
Zakat cannot be given to them for a similar reason, showing that they are not considered separate recipients.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is based on tuhma as a ground for rejection without requiring actual bias. Other schools may require clear evidence of bias, making such testimony potentially acceptable if the witness is upright.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position. Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah adopts it. The authority weight is high.
The commentary also addresses an objection about the slave's mention in the hadith, clarifying it is hypothetical.

والد کے حق میں اور ولد کی گواہی اس کے والد کے حق میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اور نہ عورت کی گواہی اس کے شوہر کے حق میں قبول ہوگی اور نہ شوہر کی گواہی اس کی بیوی کے حق میں قبول ہوگی۔ اور نہ غلام کی گواہی اس کے آقا کے حق میں قبول ہوگی اور نہ آقا کی گواہی اس کے غلام کے حق میں قبول ہوگی اور نہ مزدور کی گواہی اجرت پر لینے والے کے حق میں ہوگی۔ اس حدیث میں ولا العبد لسیدہ کے جملہ پر اعتراض ہے۔ اعتراض اس طور پر کہ غلام کے لئے کسی کے حق میں شہادت کا حق نہیں ہوتا۔ اور جب غلام کے لئے کسی کے حق میں شہادت کا حق ثابت نہیں ہے تو پھر ولا العبد لسیدہ ذکر کرنے سے کیا فائدہ ہے۔ جواب ... اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ولا العبد لسیدہ کاذکر طر والمتعاب کے طور پر کیا گیا ہے۔ یعنی جب رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مواضع تہمت کو شمار کرایا تو عبد مع السید کا بھی ذکر کیا ۔ گویا رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے یوں فرمایا کہ اگر بالفرض کسی جگہ غلام کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی تو تہمت کی وجہ سے اس کے آقا کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوتی۔ بہر حال اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ والد کی شہادت اس کی اولاد اور اولاد کی اولاد کے حق میں اور والد کی شہادت اس کے والدین اور اجداد کے حق میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اولاد اور آباء کے درمیان منافع ملے جلے ہوتے ہیں۔ یعنی باپ کی مملوکہ چیز سے بیٹا اور بیٹے کی مملوکہ چیز سے باپ نفع اندوز ہوتا ہے اور عرف میں اس کو برا بھی نہیں سمجھا جاتا۔ اسی وجہ سے باپ کا اپنے بیٹے کو اور بیٹے کا اپنے باپ کو زکوۃ دینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر باپ اپنے بیٹے یا پوتے کے حق میں گواہی دے گا۔ یا بیٹا اپنے باپ کے لئے گواہی دے گا۔ تو ان کے درمیان چونکہ منافع متصل اور مشترک ہیں اس لئے یہ شہادت من وجہ اپنی ذات کے واسطے ہوگی یا اس میں کم از کم یہ شبہ ہو گا کہ گواہ نے اپنے نفع کے لئے گواہی دی ہے اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ گواہ کی ایسی گواہی جس سے اس کی ذات کو نفع پہنچتا ہو یا نفع پہنچنے کا شبہ ہو تہمت کی وجہ سے قبول نہیں کی جاتی ۔ لہذا والد کی گواہی اولاد کے حق میں اور اولاد کی گواہی والدین کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اس پر صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ حدیث میں بقول حضرات مشائخ کے اجیر سے مراد وہ خاص متعلم ہے جو اپنے استاذ کے نقصان کو اپنا نقصان اور اس کے نفع کو اپنا نفع خیال کرے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ اجیر سے مراد تلمیذ خاص وہ ہے جو استاذ ہی کے ساتھ کھاتا پیتا ہے اور اس کے گھر کا ایک فرد بن کر اس کے اہل و عیال میں رہتا ہو اور اس کے لئے کوئی اجرت بھی متعین نہ ہو۔ گویا ایسے تلمیذ اور شاگرد کی گواہی اس کے استاذ کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اور یہی معنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث لا شهادة للقانع باهل البيت لهم کے ہیں یعنی جو شخص ایک گھر والوں کے تابع ہو اور انہیں کا کام کاج کرتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی اس کے گھر والوں کے واسطے قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ ترندی کے بیان کے مطابق پوری حدیث یہ ہے عن عائشة رضی الله تعالى عنها قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تجوز شهادة خائن ولا خائنة ولا مجلود حدا و لا ذی عمر على اخيه ولا مجرب بشهادة زور ولا القانع باهل البيت ولا ظنين في ولاء ولا قرابة حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ خیانت کرنے والے اور خیانت کرنے والی کی گواہی جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نہ اس کی جائز ہے جس کو کسی حد میں کوڑے مارے گئے ہوں نہ دشمن کی گواہی اور نہ گواہی کے عادی کی نہ اس کی جو گھر والوں کے ماتحت ہو اور نہ اس کی ملکیت اور قرابتداری سے متہم ہو۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ حدیث میں اجیر سے مراد وہ اجیر خاص ہے جو سالانہ یا ماہانہ یا روزانہ کی تنخواہ پر مقرر ہو۔ اور اس اجیر کی گواہی مستاجر کے حق میں اس لئے قبول نہیں کی جائے گی کہ وہ ادائے شہادت کے وقت اپنے منافع
He said: The testimony of a father for his child and his child's child is not accepted, nor the testimony of a child for his parents and his grandparents. The basis for this is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'The testimony of a child for his parent is not accepted, nor of a parent for his child, nor of a wife for her husband, nor of a husband for his wife, nor of a slave for his master, nor of a master for his slave, nor of a hired worker for the one who hired him.' And because the benefits between children and parents are interconnected, for this reason giving zakat to them is not permissible. So it becomes testimony for oneself in some respect, or suspicion (tuhma) is present in it. He said: The intended meaning of 'ajir' according to what they said is the special student who considers the harm of his teacher as his own harm and his benefit as his own benefit. And this is the meaning of his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no testimony for the dependant of a household against them.' And it is said that what is meant by 'ajir' is the one hired by the year, by the month, or by the day, such that he becomes entitled to wages through his benefits at the time of testimony, and thus becomes like the one who was hired for testimony. [Translation of Urdu commentary: and the testimony of a father for his son and grandson is not accepted, and the testimony of a son for his parents and grandparents is not accepted... (continues with explanation of the hadith, the objection about the slave and its answer, the rational proof based on interconnection of benefits and analogy with zakat, and the two interpretations of 'ajir' as either a special student or a regular hired worker, and then the full hadith from Aisha about the testimony of various categories of people not being accepted.)]
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah concerning the inadmissibility of testimony between certain close relatives and associates. The author begins by stating that a father cannot testify for his child or grandchild, nor can a child testify for his parents or grandparents. He then provides the primary evidence: a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that lists several relationships where testimony is not accepted: child for parent, parent for child, spouses for each other, slave for master, master for slave, and a hired worker for his employer. The author then gives a rational proof: there is an interconnection of benefits between parents and children, which is why zakat cannot be given to them (since they are not considered separate needy individuals). Because of this mutual benefit, testimony in favor of a close relative is akin to testifying for oneself, or at least raises suspicion (tuhma) of partiality. The commentary then addresses a potential objection regarding the mention of a slave's testimony for his master: since a slave's testimony is absolutely unacceptable (because he is not competent to testify), why mention it as a case of tuhma? The answer is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) mentioned it to show the extent of tuhma, even if the slave's testimony were hypothetically acceptable, it would be rejected due to suspicion. The commentary also elaborates on the term 'ajir' (hired worker) in the hadith. Two interpretations are given: first, it refers to a special student who is so attached to his teacher that he considers the teacher's loss his own loss and his gain his own gain. Second, it refers to a regular hired worker (by year, month, or day) who receives wages for his services; at the time of testifying for his employer, he still has an interest in the employment relationship, so suspicion arises. The passage concludes by quoting a longer hadith from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that lists various people whose testimony is rejected, including the dependant of a household. This passage is a typical example of a Hanafi ruling supported by hadith and rational analogy (qiyas). The authority of this ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah as found in Al-Hidayah, and the mufta bihi position is that testimony between parent and child is invalid due to tuhma.

Key Terms
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation; in this context, the possibility that the witness is partial due to personal benefit or relationship, making the testimony unreliable.
اجير (ajīr): A hired worker; in the hadith, a person who works for wages for another. The commentary gives two interpretations: a special student or a regular wage worker.
المنافع متصلة (al-manāfiʿ muttaṣila): Interconnected benefits; the mutual economic benefit between parents and children, such that they cannot give zakat to each other and testimony is suspected.
قانع (qāniʿ): A dependant or a person who is content with a household's support; a person who lives with a family as a dependant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a father's testimony for his son not accepted?
A) Because a father is not a trustworthy witness
B) Because fathers are always biased
C) Because benefits between them are interconnected, leading to tuhma
D) Because a son cannot be a witness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects parent-child testimony due to the inherent suspicion (tuhma) arising from their interconnected benefits, based on a prophetic hadith and rational analogy.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Rejection of Testimony Due to Tuhma: Close Relations and Hired Workers
Commentary on hadith listing those whose testimony is rejected due to tuhma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories of witnesses whose testimony is rejected due to tuhma and distinguish between ajīr khāṣṣ and ajīr mushtarak in applying the ruling.

Core Idea
Testimony is rejected when shared benefit creates tuhma (suspicion) of partiality.

The Hanafi school holds that testimony is invalid when the witness has a close relationship or benefit connection with the party. This lesson draws from the Hidayah commentary on a hadith that enumerates several such categories. We will explore the underlying rationale of tuhma and examine a key distinction concerning hired workers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories from the hadith
The text lists parent-child, spouses, master-slave, and hired worker (ajīr). Note each relationship and the direction of testimony (e.g., father for child).
The list is illustrative, not exhaustive.
2
Understand the objection about slaves and its resolution
A slave generally cannot testify; so why mention master-slave? The text explains it as a conditional statement: even if a slave could testify, it would be rejected due to tuhma.
This shows that tuhma is the operative cause (ʿilla), not the relationship per se.
3
Grasp the rational proof (mutual benefit)
The text argues that close relatives share benefits, so testimony for each other is self-serving or at least suspect. This logic is applied to all listed categories.
This is a qiyās based on the hadith's implied ʿilla.
4
Distinguish between ajīr khāṣṣ and ajīr mushtarak
The commentary defines ajīr khāṣṣ (specific hire) as one whose work is dedicated to one employer; his testimony for that employer is rejected. Ajīr mushtarak (joint hire) works for the public; his testimony is accepted.
The distinction hinges on exclusivity of benefit (khāṣṣ) vs. general benefit (mushtarak).
5
Recognize that tuhma is the effective cause
All rejections stem from tuhma (suspicion of bias). Where tuhma is absent (e.g., joint hire), testimony is accepted. This principle governs similar cases.
The ḥadīth is a dalīl (proof), and the ʿilla is derived from it.

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ حدیث میں بقول حضرات مشائخ کے اجیر سے مراد وہ خاص متعلم ہے جو اپنے استاذ کے نقصان کو اپنا نقصان اور اس کے نفع کو اپنا نفع خیال کرے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ اجیر سے مراد تلمیذ خاص وہ ہے جو استاذ ہی کے ساتھ کھاتا پیتا ہے اور اس کے گھر کا ایک فرد بن کر اس کے اہل و عیال میں رہتا ہو اور اس کے لئے کوئی اجرت بھی متعین نہ ہو۔ گویا ایسے تلمیذ اور شاگرد کی گواہی اس کے استاذ کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اور یہی معنی رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم کی حدیث لا شهادة للقائع باهل البيت لهم کے ہیں یعنی جو شخص ایک گھر والوں کے تابع ہو اور انہیں کا کام کاج کرتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی اس کے گھر والوں کے واسطے قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ ترندی کے بیان کے مطابق پوری حدیث یہ ہے عن عائشة رضی الله تعالى عنها قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تجوز شهادة خائن ولا خائنة ولا مجلود حدا و لا ذى عمر على اخيه ولا مجرب بشهادة زور ولا القانع باهل البيت ولا ظنين في ولاء ولا قرابة حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ خیانت کرنے والے اور خیانت کرنے والی کی گواہی جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور نہ اس کی جائز ہے جس کو کسی حد میں کوڑے مارے گئے ہوں نہ دشمن کی گواہی اور نہ گواہی کے عادی کی نہ اس کی جوان گھر والوں کے ماتحت ہو اور نہ اس کی ملکیت اور قرابتداری سے متہم ہو۔ اور بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ حدیث میں اجیر سے مراد وہ اجیر خاص ہے جو سالانہ یا ماہانہ یا روزانہ کی تنخواہ پر مقرر ہو۔ اور اس اجیر کی گواہی مستاجر کے حق میں اس لئے قبول نہیں کی جائے گی کہ وہ ادائے شہادت کیوقت اپنے منافع

کے عوض اجر کا مستحق ہوگا۔ یعنی مدت اجارہ میں اجیر کا پورا کام مستاجر کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ پس جب اجیر مدت اجارہ میں گواہی دیگا اور گواہی دینا بھی اس کے اعمال میں سے ایک عمل ہے تو یہ گواہی دینا بھی مستاجر کیلئے ہوگا اور اجیر مستاجر سے اس پر اجرت وصول کرے گا۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی شخص کو گواہی دینے پر کچھ مال دیگر مقر رکیا گیا ہو۔ اور جس شخص کو اجرت دے کر گواہی دینے پر مقر رکیا گیا ہو ، اسکی گواہی قبول " نہیں کی جاتی۔ لہذاوہ اجیر جو سالانہ یاماہانہ یا روزانہ پر مقرر ہو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ البتہ مستاجر کے حق میں اجیر مشترک کی گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ اجیر مشترک وہ اجیر ہے جو کام کے بعد اجرت کا مستحق ہوتا ہے جیسے رنگریز ، دھوبی، درزی، امیر مشترک کے منافع کسی ایک شخص کے لئے نہیں ہوتے بلکہ عام لوگوں کے لئے ہوتے ہیں۔ اور اجیر خاص وہ ہوتا ہے جو مدت مقررہ میں اپنی ذات مستاجر کے سپرد کر دے اگر چہ کام نہ کیا ہو۔ جیسے کسی کو ایک سال یا ایک ماہ یا ایک دن کے لئے نوکر رکھا گیا ہو اسی کو اجیر واحد کہتے ہیں یعنی ایک شخص کا اجیر ۔
Book of Testimony. [Page 68] Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. The testimony of a child against his father is not accepted. Nor is the testimony of a woman against her husband accepted, nor the testimony of a husband against his wife accepted. Nor is the testimony of a slave against his master accepted, nor the testimony of a master against his slave accepted. Nor is the testimony of a hired worker (ajir) against the one who hired him accepted. In this hadith, there is an objection to the phrase 'nor the slave against his master'. The objection is that a slave does not have the right to testify for anyone. So if a slave does not have the right to testify for anyone, what is the benefit of mentioning 'nor the slave against his master'? The answer is that the mention of 'nor the slave against his master' is by way of 'tar al-mutalab' (conditional/incidental). That is, when the Prophet enumerated the places of suspicion, he also mentioned the slave with the master. As if the Prophet said: If hypothetically a slave's testimony were accepted somewhere, due to suspicion it would not be accepted against his master. In any case, from this hadith it is understood that the testimony of a father for his child and grandchild, and the testimony of a child for his parents and grandparents, is not accepted. The rational proof is that benefits are mixed between children and parents. That is, the son benefits from the father's property and the father from the son's property, and in custom this is not considered bad. For this reason, it is not permissible for a father to give zakat to his son, nor a son to his father. So if a father testifies for his son or grandson, or a son testifies for his father, since their benefits are connected and shared, this testimony is in some way for themselves, or at least there will be suspicion that the witness testified for his own benefit. And it is established that such testimony by which the witness benefits or there is suspicion of benefit is not accepted due to tuhma. Therefore, the testimony of a father for children and of children for parents is not accepted. Upon this, the author of Hidayah said: In the hadith, according to the mashayikh, the 'ajir' refers to the special student who considers his teacher's loss as his own loss and his benefit as his own benefit. And some said that 'ajir' refers to the special student who eats and drinks with the teacher, lives as a member of his household among his family, and no specific wage is fixed for him. So the testimony of such a student for his teacher is not accepted. And this is the meaning of the Prophet's hadith: 'No testimony for the qani' (dependent) with the people of the house.' That is, a person who is subordinate to a household and does their work, his testimony for the household is not accepted. According to Tirmidhi's narration, the complete hadith is: From Aisha, the Prophet said: 'The testimony of a treacherous man or woman is not permissible, nor of one who has been flogged for a hadd punishment, nor of an enemy against his brother, nor of one accustomed to false testimony, nor of the dependent with the people of the house, nor of one suspected in loyalty and kinship.' And some said that 'ajir' in the hadith refers to the specific hired worker who is appointed on an annual, monthly, or daily salary. And his testimony for the employer is not accepted because at the time of giving testimony he will be entitled to wages in exchange for his benefit. That is, during the period of hire, all of the ajir's work is for the employer. So when the ajir testifies during the period of hire, and testifying is one of his actions, then this testifying is also for the employer, and the ajir will receive wages from the employer for it. So this becomes like a person who is appointed to testify for some money. And the testimony of one who is hired to testify is not accepted. Therefore, the testimony of an ajir who is appointed annually, monthly, or daily is not accepted. However, the testimony of a 'joint ajir' (ajir mushtarak) for the employer is accepted. The joint ajir is one who is entitled to wages after the work, like a dyer, washerman, tailor. The benefit of a joint ajir is not for one person but for the general public. And the specific ajir (ajir khas) is one who surrenders himself to the employer for a fixed period, even if he does not work. For example, someone hired as a servant for a year, a month, or a day. This is called ajir wahid, meaning the ajir of one person.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage from the Hidayah commentary expands the hadith on testimonies rejected due to tuhma (suspicion of partiality). The hadith lists categories: parent-child, spouses, master-slave, and hired worker. The author explains the objection regarding slaves (who lack legal capacity to testify generally) and resolves it by stating the mention is conditional—if they could testify, it would be rejected due to tuhma. The rational proof emphasizes that close relatives share mutual benefits, making testimony for each other suspect. The commentary then delves into the types of hired workers: ajir khas (specific hire, dedicated to one employer) whose testimony is rejected because his work, including testifying, benefits the employer; and ajir mushtarak (joint hire, working for the public) whose testimony is accepted. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Hanafi position on testimony in employment contexts. The passage also quotes a longer hadith from Aisha listing other categories of unacceptable witnesses: traitors, those punished for hadd, enemies, perjurers, dependents, and those suspected in loyalty or kinship.

Key Terms
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion of bias or partiality that renders a witness's testimony inadmissible.
اجیر خاص (ajīr khāṣṣ): Specific hired worker who dedicates his work to one employer for a fixed period; his testimony for the employer is rejected because his benefit is tied to the employer.
اجیر مشترک (ajīr mushtarak): Joint hired worker who works for multiple people (e.g., tailor, washerman); his testimony for an employer is accepted because he does not exclusively benefit that employer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi commentary, why is the testimony of a 'joint hired worker' (ajir mushtarak) for his employer accepted?
A) Because he is not under the employer's control.
B) Because his benefit is not exclusively tied to that employer.
C) Because he is not a relative.
D) Because the employer pays him after the work.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is rejected when tuhma exists; the Hanafi school identifies this by looking at exclusive benefit, not just the relationship.

Spousal Testimony: Hanafi Rejection vs Shafi'i Acceptance
Inter-madhhab dispute on spousal testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for rejecting spousal testimony and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, distinguishing between connected benefit (naf' muttasil) and incidental benefit.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school rejects spousal testimony because the spouses' benefits are connected, creating unavoidable tuhma.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on whether a husband or wife can testify for the other. The Hanafi school (along with Malik and Ahmad) holds that neither spouse's testimony is accepted, while Imam al-Shafi'i accepts it. We will examine the proofs on both sides, focusing on the concepts of naf' muttasil and tuhma, and also consider an intermediate view that distinguishes between wife and husband.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the Hanafi ruling and the two proofs: the hadith and the rational argument based on connected benefit (naf' muttasil).
The hadith is referenced but not quoted in this passage; the rational argument is elaborated.
2
Explain the Shafi'i position and its proof
Articulate Shafi'i's acceptance of spousal testimony, his reasoning that properties are distinct and benefits are incidental (dimnan).
Compare the creditor analogy: the creditor's benefit is incidental, so his testimony is accepted.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to Shafi'i
Understand why the Hanafis argue that the benefit between spouses is not incidental but intended and connected by custom.
The spouse has a kind of wilaya over the other's property, unlike a creditor.
4
Consider the intermediate view
Note the opinion of Ibn Abi Layla et al. that distinguishes between wife and husband based on the wife's right to nafaqah.
This view is not the Hanafi position but shows the range of ikhtilaf.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: a Hanafi judge would reject spousal testimony; a Shafi'i judge would accept it.
This affects litigation in mixed-madhhab settings.

Source Text

میاں بیوی کی ایک دوسرے کے حق میں گواہی قبول نہیں
ولا يقبل شهادة احد الزوجين للآخر وقال الشافعى تقبل لان الاملاك بينهما متميزة والايدى متحيزة ولهذا يجرى القصاص والحبس بالدين بينهما ولا معتبر بما فيه من النفع لثبوته ضمنا كما في الغريم اذا شهد لديونه المفلس . ولنا ما رويناه ولان الانتفاع متصل عادة وهو المقصود فيصير شاهداً لنفسه من وجه او يصير متهما بخلاف شهادة الغريم لانه لا ولاية له على المشهود به
ترجمہ اور میاں بیوی میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے قبول نہیں کی جائیگی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اس لئے کہ دونوں کے املاک باہم جدا جدا ہیں اور قبضے سمٹے ہوئے ہیں۔ اسی وجہ سے دونوں کے درمیان قصاص اور قرضہ کی وجہ سے قید کرنا جاری ہوگا اور اس نفع کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے جو احد الزوجین کی گواہی میں موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ نفع ضمنا ثابت ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ قرضخواہ میں جب اپنے مفلس مدیوں کے لئے گواہی دے۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ عادہ زوجین کی منفعت متصل ہوتی ہے اور یہی مقصود ہے۔ پس وہ من وجہ اپنے لئے گواہ ہوگا۔ یا متہم ہو گا بر خلاف قرض خواہ کی شہادت کے اس لئے کہ اس کو مشہود پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ میاں بیوی میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ اور ابن ابی لیلی، سفیان ثوری اور ابراہیم نخعی نے فرمایا کہ بیوی کی شہادت اس کے شوہر کے حق میں قبول نہ ہو گی اور شوہر کی گواہی اس کی بیوی کے حق میں قبول کی جائے گی۔
ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر چونکہ بیوی کا نفقہ اور کوہ واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے بیوی کا شوہر کے مال میں ایک حق ہے۔ اور جب بیوی کا شوہر کے مال میں حق ہے تو بیوی اپنے شوہر کے حق میں گواہی دینے سے متہم ہوگی ۔ یعنی لوگ یہ کہیں گے کہ بیوی نے اپنے نفع کے خاطر گواہی دی ہے۔ اور جو شخص گواہی میں متہم ہو اس کی گواہی چونکہ قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے اس لئے بیوی کی گواہی اس کے شوہر کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اور شوہر کی گواہی میں چونکہ اس طرح کی تہمت نہیں ہے اس لئے شوہر کی گواہی اس کی بیوی کے حق میں قبول کر لی
Testimony of spouses for each other is not accepted. It is not accepted that one spouse testifies for the other. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is accepted, because their properties are distinct and their possessions are separate. For this reason, retaliation and imprisonment for debt are carried out between them. And no consideration is given to the benefit that exists in the testimony of one spouse, because that benefit is established indirectly, as in the case of a creditor when he testifies for his insolvent debtor. Our proof is the hadith we have narrated, and because the benefit between spouses is connected by custom, and that is what is intended. So he becomes a witness for himself in some way, or becomes suspect, unlike the testimony of a creditor because he has no authority over the thing testified about. Commentary: Imam al-Quduri said that one spouse's testimony for the other is not accepted. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold this view. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is accepted. Ibn Abi Layla, Sufyan al-Thawri, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said: The wife's testimony for her husband is not accepted, but the husband's testimony for his wife is accepted. Their proof is that since the husband is obliged to provide nafaqah and housing for the wife, the wife has a right in the husband's wealth. So when the wife testifies for her husband, she is suspect. People will say she testified for her own benefit. And the testimony of one who is suspect is not accepted. Therefore, the wife's testimony for her husband is not accepted. And since there is no such suspicion in the husband's testimony, the husband's testimony for his wife is accepted.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute on whether spouses can testify for each other. The Hanafi position (shared by Malik and Ahmad) is that neither spouse's testimony is accepted for the other. Imam Shafi'i accepts it, arguing that spouses have distinct properties and legal interactions (e.g., qisas, debt imprisonment) are possible between them, and any benefit is incidental, like a creditor testifying for a debtor. The Hanafi response counters that the benefit between spouses is connected by custom (munfa'at muttasil) and intended, leading to tuhma (suspicion). The text also presents an intermediate view from Ibn Abi Layla et al. that distinguishes between wife and husband: the wife's testimony is rejected due to her right to nafaqah, but the husband's testimony is accepted as he has no similar suspicion. The passage includes the Arabic text from Al-Hidayah and its Urdu commentary, demonstrating how the Hanafi school uses both hadith and rational argument (ta'lil) to establish its ruling.

Key Terms
نفع متصل (naf' muttasil): Connected benefit: a benefit that is directly tied to the witness due to relationship or dependency, leading to tuhma.
ضمنا (dimnan): Incidentally or indirectly. Used by Shafi'i to argue that any benefit from spousal testimony is incidental, not direct.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, why is a wife's testimony for her husband rejected?
A) Because wives are inherently unreliable witnesses.
B) Because the wife has a right to nafaqah from the husband, creating suspicion of benefit.
C) Because the husband has authority over the wife.
D) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade it for spouses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects spousal testimony to avoid tuhma from connected benefits, a precaution rooted in both hadith and rational principle.

The Testimony of Spouses for Each Other: Hanafi Position and the Shafi'i Opposition
Inter-madhhab dispute over spousal testimony admissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spousal testimony, explain the evidence (hadith and tuhmah), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Spouses cannot testify for each other because their mutual benefit is direct and habitual, as proved by the explicit hadith.

The Hanafi school holds that a spouse's testimony for the other is not accepted in court. This ruling rests on a clear hadith and the principle of tuhmah (impugnment) due to direct benefit. However, Imam al-Shafi'i accepts such testimony, arguing that spouses have separate legal identities and any benefit is incidental. This lesson unpacks the evidence on both sides and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on spousal testimony
Identify the core ruling: the testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted (ghayr maqbul). Note that this applies to both husband and wife.
The ruling is from Al-Quduri's matn and is part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Examine the primary proof: the hadith
The matn cites the hadith 'la tajuuzu shahaadatu...' which explicitly prohibits spousal testimony. Recognize that the hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (dalala qati).
The phrase 'la tajuuzu' indicates a definitive prohibition.
3
Understand the rational argument: tuhmah
The text argues that the mutual benefit between spouses is direct and habitual by custom, so a spouse testifying appears to be testifying for his/her own benefit, making the witness impugned (muttaham).
This is contrasted with a creditor testifying for a debtor, where the benefit is incidental.
4
Present the Shafi'i opposing view and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since spouses have separate properties and possessions, there is no direct conflict of interest. Any benefit is incidental (dhimnan), similar to a creditor testifying for his debtor.
Shafi'i also uses the analogy of brother testifying for brother.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi response prioritizes the explicit hadith over analogy. Additionally, the benefit between spouses is not incidental but direct due to the habitual interconnectedness of their interests. The practical difference: In Hanafi courts, such testimony is rejected; in Shafi'i courts, it is accepted.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position of rejection.

Source Text

میاں بیوی کی ایک دوسرے کے حق میں گواہی قبول نہیں

ترجمہ اور میاں بیوی میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے قبول نہیں کی جائیگی اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اس لئے کہ دونوں کے املاک باہم جدا جدا ہیں اور قبضے سمٹے ہوئے ہیں۔ اسی وجہ سے دونوں کے درمیان قصاص اور قرضہ کی وجہ سے قید کرنا جاری ہوگا اور اس نفع کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے جو احد الزوجین کی گواہی میں موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ نفع ضمنا ثابت ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ قرضخواہ میں جب اپنے مفلس مدیوں کے لئے گواہی دے۔ اور ہماری دلیل وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ عادہ زوجین کی منفعت متصل ہوتی ہے اور یہی مقصود ہے۔ پس وہ من وجہ اپنے لئے گواہ ہوگا۔ یا متہم ہو گا بر خلاف قرض خواہ کی شہادت کے اس لئے کہ اس کو مشہود پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ میاں بیوی میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ اس کے قائل امام مالک اور امام احمد ہیں اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قبول کر لی جائے گی۔ اور ابن ابی لیلی، سفیان ثوری اور ابراہیم نخعی نے فرمایا کہ بیوی کی شہادت اس کے شوہر کے حق میں قبول نہ ہو گی اور شوہر کی گواہی اس کی بیوی کے حق میں قبول کی جائے گی۔
ان حضرات کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر چونکہ بیوی کا نفقہ اور کوہ واجب ہوتا ہے اس لئے بیوی کا شوہر کے مال میں ایک حق ہے۔ اور جب بیوی کا شوہر کے مال میں حق ہے تو بیوی اپنے شوہر کے حق میں گواہی دینے سے متہم ہوگی ۔ یعنی لوگ یہ کہیں گے کہ بیوی نے اپنے نفع کے خاطر گواہی دی ہے۔ اور جو شخص گواہی میں متہم ہو اس کی گواہی چونکہ قبول نہیں کی جاتی ہے اس لئے بیوی کی گواہی اس کے شوہر کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اور شوہر کی گواہی میں چونکہ اس طرح کی تہمت نہیں ہے اس لئے شوہر کی گواہی اس کی بیوی کے حق میں قبول کر لی جائے گی۔
حضرت امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ میاں بیوی دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کی ملک بھی جدا ہے اور ہر ایک کا قبضہ بھی سمٹا ہوا ہے۔ یعنی ہر ایک کا قبضہ بھی جدا ہے۔ لہذا ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو دوسرے کی ملک اور دوسرے کے مال میں تصرف کی اجازت نہ ہو گی ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر زوجین میں سے کسی نے دوسرے کو ناحق قتل کر دیا تو اس پر قصاص واجب ہوتا ہے قاتل خواہ شوہر ہو خواہ بیوی ہو۔ اگر ایک کا دوسرے پر قرضہ ہو اور قرضدار ادا کرنے میں خواہ مخواہ تساہل کرے تو قرض خواہ کی وجہ سے قرضدار کو قید کر لیا جاتا ہے خواہ بیوی قرضدار اور شو ہر قرض خواہ ہو یا اس کا برعکس ہو۔ اور جو شخص ایسا ہو اس کی گواہی اس کے ساتھی کے حق میں قبول کر لی جاتی ہے جیسے ایک بھائی کی گواہی دوسرے بھائی کے حق میں قبول کی جاتی ہے۔
ولا معتبر بمافيه من النفع ..... الخ سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ زوجین میں سے ایک کی شہادت دوسرے کے لئے قبول کرنے میں خود گواہ کا نفع ہے۔ اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی کے نفع کو اپنا نفع شمار کرتا ہے یعنی اگر کسی بات میں شوہر کا نفع ہے تو بیوی اس کو اپنا نفع شمار کرتی ہے اور اگر بیوی کا نفع ہے تو شوہر اس کو اپنا نفع شمار کرتا ہے۔ پس جب زوجین میں سے کوئی ایک دوسرے کے لئے گواہی دے گا تو اس گواہی سے یقینا مشہودلہ ، کا نفع ہوگا اور شاہد چونکہ مشہودلہ، کی بیوی یا شوہر ہے اس لئے اس گواہی سے خود شاہد کا بھی نفع ہوگا۔ اور جس گواہی سے خود شاہد کا نفع ہوتا ہو اس کو قبول نہیں کیا جاتا۔ لہذاز وجین میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے حق میں قبول نہ ہونی چاہئے۔ امام شافعی کی طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہوگا کہ گواہی سے یہ نفع مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ نفع گواہی کے ضمن میں ثابت ہوا ہے اور جو نفع ضمناً ثابت ہو اس کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا زوجین میں سے کسی ایک کے گواہی دینے میں خود شاہد کا جو نفع ضمنا ثابت ہوا ہے اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب اس نفع کا اعتبار نہیں ہے تو احد الزوجین کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے قبول کرنے میں کوئی نقصان نہیں ہے۔ اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے قرض خواہ اپنے مفلس قرضدار کے لئے گواہی دے تو یہ گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے اگر قرض خواہ کے لئے بھی اس گواہی میں نفع موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ اس گواہی پر قرضدار مفلس کے واسطے مال کا حکم ہوا تو قرضخواہ کا قرضہ وصول ہونا ممکن ہے مگر چونکہ یہ نفع ایک ضمنی چیز ہے گواہی کا مقصود نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس نفع کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل .... وہ حدیث ہے جس کو ہم سابق میں روایت کر چکے ہیں یعنی لا تجوز شهادة الوالد لولده ولا الولد لوالده ولا المرأة لزوجها و لا الزوج لأمرأته يه حديث صراحتہ دلالت کرتی ہے کہ بیوی کی گواہی شوہر کیلئے اور شوہر کی گواہی بیوی کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوجین کے درمیان منافع عادہ متصل ہوتے ہیں یعنی شوہر کو بیوی کے مال کی وجہ سے مالدار شمار کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور بیوی کو شوہر کے مال کی وجہ سے مالدار شمار کیا جاتا ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے " و وجدك عائلا فاغنى " اور پایا تجھ کو مفلس پھر غنی کر دیا۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ مراد یہ ہے کہ حضرت خدیجہ کے مال سے تجھ کو غنی کر دیا۔ اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ بیوی کے مالدار ہونے سے شوہر کو مالدار شمار کیا جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ بسا اوقات میاں بیوی کے درمیان منافع میں اس قدرا تصال اور انبساط ہوتا ہے
Spouses cannot testify for each other. It is stated: 'The testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted, and al-Shafi'i said it is accepted because their properties are distinct and their possessions are separate. For this reason, qisas and imprisonment for debt apply between them. And no consideration is given to the benefit in it because it is established incidentally, just as when a creditor testifies for his insolvent debtor. Our proof is what we have narrated (the hadith), and because the benefit is habitually connected and that is the purpose, so he becomes a witness for himself in a way or becomes impugned, unlike the testimony of a creditor because he has no authority over what is testified about.' Translation: The testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is accepted, because their properties are separate and their possessions are distinct, so qisas and imprisonment for debt apply between them. The benefit present in the testimony is not considered because it is established incidentally, as when a creditor testifies for his insolvent debtor. Our proof is the hadith we have narrated, and because the spouses' benefit is habitually connected and that is the purpose, so he becomes a witness for himself in a way or becomes impugned, unlike the creditor's testimony because he has no authority over the subject. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. Imam al-Shafi'i said it is accepted. Ibn Abi Layla, Sufyan al-Thawri, and Ibrahim al-Nakha'i said that the wife's testimony for the husband is not accepted, but the husband's testimony for the wife is accepted. Their proof is that since the husband is obligated to provide maintenance for the wife, the wife has a right in the husband's property. Therefore, the wife is impugned when testifying for the husband. And the husband's testimony does not have such impugnment. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that each spouse has separate property and possession, so one does not have permission to dispose of the other's property. This is why if one kills the other unjustly, qisas is obligatory. If one owes a debt to the other, the debtor can be imprisoned. So such a person's testimony for their partner is accepted, like a brother for a brother. The phrase 'Wa la mu'tabir...' answers a question. The question is: In accepting the testimony of one spouse for the other, there is a benefit for the witness himself. The response is that this benefit is not intended; it is incidental. Incidental benefit is not considered. An example is a creditor testifying for his insolvent debtor, which is accepted even though the creditor benefits. Our proof is the hadith we have narrated: 'The testimony of a parent for his child, a child for his parent, a wife for her husband, and a husband for his wife is not permissible.' This hadith clearly indicates that the testimony is not allowed. The rational proof is that between spouses, benefits are habitually connected; the husband is considered wealthy due to the wife's wealth, and the wife due to the husband's wealth. Allah Almighty said: 'And He found you poor and made you rich.' Some said the meaning is that He made the Prophet (peace be upon him) rich through the wealth of Khadija. This shows that a husband is considered wealthy through his wife's wealth. Rather, sometimes the connection and expansion of benefits between spouses is such that...
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the admissibility of testimony between spouses. The matn of Al-Quduri states the ruling: the testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted. The author then presents the evidence for this ruling and addresses the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi position is that the testimony is rejected because the interests of spouses are directly and habitually connected, making the witness testifying for his own benefit to some extent, or at least appearing impugned. The primary proof is the hadith explicitly prohibiting such testimony. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since spouses have separate legal entities— separate properties, separate possessions— the mutual benefit is only incidental and does not disqualify the witness, analogous to a creditor testifying for his debtor. The Hanafi response distinguishes the case of spouses because the benefit between them is not incidental but direct and habitual by custom ('āda muttaṣila). Additionally, the explicit hadith is given precedence. The passage also notes a third opinion (Ibn Abi Layla, etc.) that only the wife's testimony for the husband is rejected due to her right to maintenance, but the husband's testimony for the wife is accepted. However, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position is that neither is accepted. The commentary further clarifies that the benefit arising from spousal testimony is not merely consequential but is linked to the essence of marital relationship, unlike the creditor case where the benefit is purely incidental. The hadith wording 'la tajuuzu shahaadatu...' is quoted as definitive evidence.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahāda): Testimony given in court to establish a right or prove an event.
زوجين (zawjayn): Spouses, specifically husband and wife.
متهم (muttaham): A witness who is suspected of bias or self-interest due to a close relationship with a party.
نفع (naf'): Benefit or advantage, which if directly intended, can disqualify a witness.
ضمنًا (dimnan): Incidentally or as a secondary consequence, not as a primary objective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is the testimony of one spouse for the other not accepted?
A) Because spouses share ownership of property, making them co-owners.
B) Because the hadith explicitly prohibits it and the mutual benefit is direct and habitual.
C) Because spouses are considered one legal entity, so one cannot testify for the other.
D) Because the spouse would be testifying about their own rights due to inheritance laws.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects spousal testimony based on the explicit hadith and the principle of direct benefit (tuhmah), while the Shafi'i school accepts it based on separate legal identity and incidental benefit.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Spouses for Each Other: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on spousal testimony admissibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on spousal testimony, explain the Hanafi proofs (hadith and rational), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A spouse's testimony for the other is rejected in Hanafi law due to an explicit hadith and the inherent conflict of interest from shared benefits.

This lesson examines the classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the admissibility of testimony between spouses. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that spouses are separate legal persons, so their testimony should be accepted like any other. The Hanafi school, relying on a specific hadith and a rational principle of tuhmah (accusation of self-interest), rejects it absolutely. Understanding the reasoning behind each position is crucial for grasping the Hanafi approach to shahadah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: testimony of one spouse for the other is not admissible. The hukm level is haram according to Hanafis.
This is the mufta bihi position, consistent across all Hanafi imams.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and their proof
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that spousal testimony is acceptable because each spouse has separate ownership and possession, and they can be involved in legal actions like qisas or debt imprisonment.
Shafi'is treat spouses like strangers for testimony purposes.
3
Follow the Shafi'i rational analogy
Shafi'is compare spousal testimony to a creditor testifying for an insolvent debtor. Even though the creditor benefits indirectly, the benefit is incidental and does not disqualify.
The key point is the distinction between primary (maqsud) and incidental (tab'i) benefit.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis counter with two proofs: (1) an explicit hadith prohibiting such testimony, and (2) a rational argument that the connection of benefits between spouses is so strong that the witness is inherently accused of seeking personal gain.
Hanafis emphasize that the husband's authority over the wife's property makes him especially suspect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical consequence: Hanafis reject spousal testimony in all cases; Shafi'is accept it if the benefit is incidental. The Hanafi view is considered stronger due to the explicit hadith.
The later Hanafi authorities rely on this position for fatwa.

متہم بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب قرض خواہ گواہی میں متہم نہ ہو تو اس کی گواہی جائز اور قابل قبول ہوگی اس کے خلاف مرد کہ اس کو عورت پر نگراں مقرر کیا گیا ہے وہ عورت کے مال میں عادة تصرف کرتا ہے لہذا شو ہر اپنی بیوی کے لئے گواہی دینے میں متہم ہوگا۔ اور جب شوہر اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہے تو بیوی کے حق میں اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
Book of Testimony. It will go. 70 Ashraf al-Bidayah volume ten. The proof of Imam Shafi'i is that the husband and wife each have separate ownership and each has separate possession. Hence, one does not have permission to dispose of the other's property. This is why if one spouse kills the other unjustly, qisas is wajib, whether the killer is husband or wife. If one owes a debt to the other and the debtor delays payment, the debtor can be imprisoned at the creditor's request, whether the debtor is the wife and the creditor the husband or vice versa. And the testimony of such a person for his companion is accepted, just as the testimony of one brother for another is accepted. The phrase 'wa la mu'tabaru bima fihi min an-naf'... answers a question. The question is: In accepting the testimony of one spouse for the other, there is benefit for the witness himself, because each considers the benefit of the other as his own. So when one spouse testifies for the other, there is benefit for the beneficiary and also for the witness because he is the husband or wife. Testimony that brings benefit to the witness is not accepted. Therefore, the testimony of one spouse for the other should not be accepted. Imam Shafi'i's response: This benefit is not intended; it is incidental, and incidental benefit is not considered. So it does not harm acceptance. His example: a creditor testifying for an insolvent debtor is accepted even though there is benefit for the creditor, because it is incidental. Our proof is the hadith we narrated earlier: 'The testimony of a father for his son, nor of a son for his father, nor of a wife for her husband, nor of a husband for his wife is not permissible.' This hadith clearly indicates it is not allowed. Rational proof: Between spouses, benefits are connected, so the husband is considered wealthy due to the wife's wealth and vice versa. Allah said: 'And He found you poor and made you rich.' Some said this refers to Khadijah's wealth. This shows the husband is considered wealthy due to the wife's wealth. Moreover, the connection of benefits between spouses is stronger than between parents and children; sometimes a husband antagonizes his parents to please his wife, and a wife displeases her parents to please her husband. So benefits are connected and shared, and deriving benefit from the marriage relationship is intended. Therefore, one spouse testifying for the other is, in some ways, testifying for oneself or is accused of seeking personal benefit. A person's testimony for himself or when accused is rejected. Hence, the testimony of one spouse for the other is not accepted. As for the analogy of creditor's testimony: The answer to Imam Shafi'i's analogy is that the creditor has no authority over the debtor's property, so he is not accused in testifying. In contrast, the husband has guardianship over the wife and typically disposes of her property, so he is accused. Therefore, his testimony for her is not accepted.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the testimony of spouses for each other. The author presents Imam Shafi'i's argument that since spouses have separate ownership and possession, their testimony for each other should be accepted, just like between brothers. He uses examples: a spouse who kills the other is subject to qisas, and a creditor can imprison a debtor spouse. Then the author raises a potential objection: if a spouse's testimony benefits the witness, it should be rejected. Imam Shafi'i responds that the benefit is incidental, not primary, and gives the analogy of a creditor testifying for a debtor. The Hanafi response refutes this with two proofs: (1) a hadith explicitly prohibiting spousal testimony, and (2) a rational argument that between spouses, benefits are so connected that the witness is inherently accused of seeking his own benefit. The author concludes that this connection is stronger than between parents and children, and the husband's authority over the wife's property makes him accused. Thus, Hanafis reject spousal testimony entirely, while Shafi'is accept it under certain conditions, but the text prefers the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given in a court of law to establish a fact.
زوجین (zawjayn): The married couple, husband and wife.
نفع (naf'): Benefit or advantage derived from a transaction or testimony.
متہم (mutahham): A person who is suspected of bias or self-interest in a case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the testimony of one spouse for the other, even if the benefit to the witness is incidental?
A) Because spouses are considered one legal entity in all matters.
B) Because the hadith explicitly prohibits it and the connection of benefits between spouses is so strong that the witness is inherently accused of self-interest.
C) Because spouses are not allowed to interact with each other's property.
D) Because the Shafi'i school allows it, so Hanafis reject it as a matter of principle.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects spousal testimony based on an explicit hadith and the strong interconnection of benefits that creates an inherent accusation of self-interest (tuhmah).

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Master's Testimony for Slave and Partner's Testimony
Rulings on testimony admissibility based on self-interest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's testimony for his slave and a partner's testimony for his co-partner, and explain the rationale based on self-interest (tuhmah).

Core Idea
A master cannot testify for his slave, nor a partner for his partner in partnership matters, because self-interest invalidates testimony.

Testimony in Islamic law is a serious matter; the witness must be free from any suspicion of bias. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains two specific cases where testimony is rejected due to self-interest: a master testifying for his slave, and one partner testifying for another in partnership matters. The ruling is based on a hadith and rational proof, and it distinguishes situations where the self-interest is complete or partial, and where it is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage covers three acts: (1) master's testimony for his slave, (2) master's testimony for his mukatab, (3) partner's testimony for his co-partner. For each, determine whether the testimony is accepted or rejected and under what conditions. Note that the ruling changes when the matter is outside the partnership.
The master's testimony is rejected whether the slave has debt or not, but the degree of self-interest differs.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites a hadith: 'ولا للمولى لعبده' (nor for the master for his slave). This is from a longer hadith listing prohibited testimonies. Additionally, rational proof (dalil aqli) is given: the master's testimony is either entirely for his own benefit (if slave has no debt) or partially (if slave has debt).
The rational proof is based on ownership: the slave's property belongs to the master, so the master gains by testifying.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The hadith explicitly forbids the master's testimony for his slave, making it a direct textual prohibition. The rational proof elaborates that the self-interest exists either fully or partially, which creates suspicion (tuhmah) that undermines the credibility of the testimony. Similarly, for partners, sharing the subject matter creates partial self-interest.
The principle is that any tuhmah (accusation of bias) invalidates testimony.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the mukatab and partner
The master's testimony for his mukatab is also rejected because the master retains residual interest (the mukatab is still under his authority until fully free). For partners, the testimony is rejected only in matters of the partnership; outside matters, there is no shared interest, so it is accepted.
This shows the rule is based on the presence of tuhmah, not the type of relationship.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference is clear: if a partner testifies about a non-partnership matter (e.g., a separate transaction), his testimony is accepted. Also, if the slave has debts, the master's interest is reduced but still sufficient to reject the testimony.
This nuance prevents leniency in accepting potentially biased testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مولیٰ کی غلام اور مکاتب کے حق میں گواہی قبول نہیں جمیل احمد عفی عنہ ولا شهادة المولى لعبده لانه شهادة لنفسه من كل وجه اذا لم يكن على العبد دين او من وجه ان كان عليه دين لان الحال موقوف مراعى ولا لمكاتبه لما قلنا ولا شهادة الشريك لشريكه فيما هو من شركتهما لانه ادة لنفسه من وجه لاشتراكهما ولو شهد بما ليس من شركتهما تقبل لانتفاء التهمة شـهـ ترجمہ اور آقا کی گواہی اس کے غلام کے حق میں قبول نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہ من کل وجہ اس کی ذات کے واسطے شہادت ہے بشرطیکہ غلام پر قرضہ نہ ہو یا من وجہ اگر اس پر قرضہ ہو اس لئے کہ غلام کی حالت موقوف قابل لحاظ ہے اور مولی کی گواہی اس کے مکاتب کے واسطے بھی جائز نہیں ہے اُسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان اور ایک شریک کی گواہی اُس کے دوسرے شریک کے واسطے ایسی چیز میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ جو ان دونوں کی شرکت میں ہے کیونکہ یہ من وجہ اس کی ذات کے واسطے شہادت ہے اس لئے کہ دونوں کی شرکت ہے اور اگر ایسی چیز میں گواہی دی جو ان دونوں کی شرکت میں نہیں ہے تو قبول کر لی جائے گی کیونکہ کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ آقا کی شہادت خود اس کے غلام کے حق میں قبول نہیں کی جائے گی دلیل سابق میں مذکورہ حدیث اولا المولى لعبدہ ہے۔۔ اور دلیل عقلی ہ یہ ہے کہ آقا کا اپنے غلام کے حق میں گواہی دینا خود آقا کے لئے من وجہ شہادت ہے یا من کل وجہ شہادت ہے۔
The testimony of the master for his slave and mukatab is not accepted. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven. And the testimony of the master for his slave is not accepted because it is testimony for himself in every way (min kulli wajh) if the slave has no debt, or in some ways (min wajh) if the slave has debt, because the situation is suspended and to be considered. And neither for his mukatab for the same reason we stated. And the testimony of one partner for his partner in matters that are part of their partnership is not accepted, because it is testimony for himself in some ways (min wajh) due to their partnership. But if he testifies in a matter that is not part of their partnership, it is accepted because there is no accusation. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the master's testimony for his slave is not accepted based on the hadith mentioned earlier, 'ولا للمولى لعبده' (nor for the master for his slave). And the rational proof is that the master testifying for his slave is either testimony for himself in some ways or in every way.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage states the rulings on the admissibility of testimony by a master for his slave and by a partner for his co-partner. The master's testimony for his slave is rejected because it is either entirely self-interested (when the slave has no debt, so all slave's property belongs to the master) or partially self-interested (when the slave has debt, so the master's interest is contingent). Similarly, the master's testimony for his mukatab (a slave who has a contract of manumission) is rejected for the same reason: the master retains a residual interest. For partners, testimony in matters related to the partnership is rejected because the testifying partner shares in the outcome. However, if the testimony concerns a matter outside the partnership, there is no suspicion, so it is accepted. The author quotes Sahib al-Quduri for the hadith-based proof and adds a rational proof. This is a ruling with proof (dalil) from the hadith and logical reasoning.

Key Terms
مولیٰ (mawla): Master or owner of a slave.
عبد (abd): A male slave owned by the master.
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract (kitabat) with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
شریک (shareek): A partner in a business or property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, because partners know each other's business.
B) Only if the partnership is dissolved.
C) In matters that are not part of the partnership, because there is no shared interest.
D) In all matters as long as the partner is honest.

Key Takeaway
A testimony is rejected if the witness has a direct or indirect self-interest in the outcome, as seen with the master for his slave and partner for his co-partner in partnership matters.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Why Spousal Testimony is Rejected in Hanafi Law
Explains spousal testimony rejection with rational proof and refutes Shafi'i analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects spousal testimony and refute the Shafi'i counterargument using the distinction of authority.

Core Idea
Spouses cannot testify for each other because their interests are intertwined, creating unavoidable suspicion of bias.

In many legal systems, close relationships raise questions about impartiality. The Hanafi jurists provide a nuanced rational argument for why the bond between spouses creates a unique conflict of interest. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows how it withstands a challenge from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is a husband (or wife) giving testimony on behalf of their spouse. The ruling is that such testimony is not accepted (mardud).
This is a procedural ruling about the validity of testimony, not about the witness's character.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil (proof)
The proof is rational (dalil aqli): spouses have interconnected benefits, and the husband exercises authority over the wife's property. This creates a strong presumption (tuhma) that the testimony is self-serving.
The text uses the phrase 'min wajh' (in one aspect) to indicate partial self-interest.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof yields the ruling)
Because the testifier stands to benefit (directly or indirectly), his or her testimony is like testifying for oneself. And testifying for oneself is invalid. Even if benefit is not immediate, the suspicion (tuhma) makes the testimony inadmissible.
The key is the shared benefit and the husband's authority over the wife's property.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly difference)
Imam al-Shafi'i allows spousal testimony by analogy (qiyas) with a creditor testifying for a debtor. He argues that just as a creditor has no control over the debtor's property, the husband has no control over the wife's property.
The opposing school's qiyas is based on the absence of wilaya (authority).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih (response)
The Hanafi response distinguishes the husband from a creditor: the husband has de facto authority and customary control (wilayat al-tasarruf) over the wife's property, while a creditor does not. Therefore, the analogy fails and the Hanafi position stands as mufta bihi.
This tarjih is decisive in the Hanafi school and is relied upon for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد - دہم که اولا د اور والدین کے درمیان نہیں ہوتا یعنی شوہر بیوی پر اور بیوی شوہر پر اس قدر ایثار کرتے ہیں کہ والدین اپنی اولاد پر اور اولا د اپنے والدین پر ایثار نہیں کرتے بلکہ کبھی کبھی تو شوہر اپنی بیوی کو خوش کرنے کے لئے اپنے والدین سے دشمنی کر لیتا ہے اور بیوی اپنے شوہر کی خوشنودی کے لئے اپنے ماں باپ کو ناراض کر دیتی ہے۔ بہر حال زوجین کے درمیان منافع متصل اور مشترک ہوتے ہیں۔ اور رشتہ زوجیت سے نفع اٹھانا ہی مقصود ہوتا ہے پس جب زوجین کے درمیان منافع متصل اور مشترک ہوتے ہیں اور نفع مقصود بھی ہے تو ان میں سے کسی ایک کا دوسرے کے لئے گواہی دینا من وجہ اپنے لئے گواہی دینا ہوگا یا وہ اپنی شہادت میں اپنے واسطے نفع حاصل کرنے کے ساتھ متہم ہوگا۔ اور آدمی اپنے واسطے گواہی دے تب بھی اس کی گواہی رد کر دی جاتی ہے اور اگر اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہو تب بھی رد کر دیجاتی ہے
اس لئے زوجین میں سے ایک کی گواہی دوسرے کے لئے قبول نہ ہوگی۔
بخلاف شهادة الغريم الخ ...سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔
جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قرض خواہ کو مشہور بہ پر ولایت کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مشہور بہ قرضدار کا مال ہے اور قرض خواہ کو قرضدار کے مال پر تصرف کا کوئی اختیار نہیں ہوتا اور قرضخواہ کو جب قرضدار کے مال پر تصرف کا کوئی حق نہیں ہے تو وہ گواہی دینے میں متہم بھی نہ ہوگا اور جب قرض خواہ گواہی میں متہم نہ ہو تو اس کی گواہی جائز اور قابل قبول ہوگی اس کے خلاف مرد کہ اس کو عورت پر نگراں مقرر کیا گیا ہے وہ عورت کے مال میں عادة تصرف کرتا ہے لہذا شو ہر اپنی بیوی کے لئے گواہی دینے میں متہم ہوگا۔ اور جب شوہر اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہے تو بیوی کے حق میں اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10. ... That which does not occur between children and parents: meaning husband and wife show such sacrifice for each other that parents do not for their children and children do not for their parents. Sometimes a husband even becomes hostile to his parents to please his wife, and a wife displeases her parents to please her husband. In any case, between spouses the benefits are connected and shared. And deriving benefit from the marital relationship is the intended purpose. So when between spouses the benefits are connected and shared and benefit is the purpose, then one of them testifying for the other is in one aspect testifying for oneself or they will be suspected of seeking benefit for themselves in their testimony. And when a person testifies for himself, his testimony is rejected, and if he is suspected in his testimony, it is also rejected. For this reason, the testimony of one spouse for the other will not be accepted. As for the testimony of a creditor ... from this the response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy is given. The summary of the response is that the creditor has no right of authority over the well-known property. Because the well-known property is the debtor's property and the creditor has no authority to dispose of the debtor's property. Since the creditor has no right to dispose of the debtor's property, he will not be suspected in giving testimony, and when the creditor is not suspected in testimony, his testimony is permissible and acceptable. Contrast this with the husband: he is appointed as a supervisor over the woman, he customarily disposes of the woman's property, therefore the husband will be suspected in testifying for his wife. And when the husband is suspected in his testimony, his testimony for the wife will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the Hanafi ruling that spouses cannot testify for each other. The commentator first gives a rational argument: the bond between spouses is so strong that their interests are intertwined. A husband often prioritizes his wife over his own parents, and vice versa. Therefore, when one spouse testifies for the other, it is like testifying for oneself because any benefit to the spouse indirectly benefits the testifier. Even if the benefit is not direct, the testifier is suspected of bias. Since testifying for oneself is invalid, and testifying under suspicion is also invalid, spousal testimony is rejected. The text then addresses a potential objection from Imam al-Shafi'i, who analogizes spousal testimony to creditor-debtor testimony. The Hanafi response is that the analogy fails because a creditor has no authority over the debtor's property. A husband, however, has authority and customary control over his wife's property, creating a real suspicion of bias. Thus, the Hanafi position stands.

Key Terms
زوجین (zawjayn): The married couple, husband and wife.
شہادت/گواہی (shahādat): Testimony given in a court of law to establish a claim or right.
متہم (mutahham): Suspected of bias or personal interest in the outcome of the case.
من وجہ (min wajh): In one aspect; partially, from one perspective.
من کل وجہ (min kulli wajh): In every aspect; completely, from all perspectives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is a husband's testimony for his wife not accepted?
A) Because the husband is not a reliable witness in general.
B) Because the husband has authority over his wife's property, creating suspicion of bias.
C) Because the wife is not allowed to testify in court.
D) Because the testimony of relatives is always rejected.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects spousal testimony because the shared benefits and husband's authority create an unavoidable suspicion of bias; the analogy with creditor-debtor fails due to the husband's actual control over his wife's property.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Master's Testimony for Slave and Mukatib
Ruling with proof on master's testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a master's testimony for his slave or mukatib and explain the rational proof of self-interest (min kulli wajh and min wajh).

Core Idea
A master cannot testify for his slave or mukatib because it amounts to testifying for oneself.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from Hanafi law of testimony: the master's testimony for his slave or mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission) is rejected. Al-Marghinani explains the prohibition using both a hadith and a rational proof based on the concept of self-interest. You will learn to distinguish between complete and partial self-interest and understand how uncertainty (ihtimal) affects the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states that a master's testimony for his slave or mukatib is not accepted. It cites a hadith and a rational proof.
The ruling is absolute: no distinction is made for civil or criminal cases.
2
Understand the hadith proof
The hadith 'la shahdata li mawla 'ala 'abdihi' (no testimony for a master against his slave) is mentioned as textual evidence. The wording negates the master's testimony.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for the ruling.
3
Analyze the rational proof: two states of the slave
If the slave has no debts, the master owns the slave and his property completely, so testifying for the slave is testifying for himself in every respect (min kulli wajh). If the slave has debts, the situation is uncertain: creditors may claim the slave or the master may pay. Thus the testimony is partially self-interested (min wajh).
Both complete and partial self-interest invalidate the testimony.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the mukatib
The mukatib's situation is also uncertain: if he completes payment, he becomes free and the master is a stranger; if he fails, he remains a slave. Thus the testimony is min wajh and not accepted.
The uncertainty creates a potential self-interest even if not realized.
5
Conclude the ruling
Since both scenarios (min kulli wajh and min wajh) involve self-interest, the master's testimony is rejected. The qadi should not accept it.
The ruling is mufta bihi and from Zahir al-Riwayah.

The testimony of a master for his slave and mukatib is not accepted. (Signature: Jamil Ahmad Afi 'Anhu). And the testimony of a master for his slave is not accepted because it is testimony for himself in every aspect if the slave has no debt, or in one aspect if he has debt, because the situation is suspended and considered. Nor for his mukatib for what we have said. Explanation: And the testimony of a master for his slave will not be accepted because it is in every aspect testimony for himself, provided the slave has no debt, or in one aspect if he has debt, because the slave's situation is suspended and subject to consideration. And the master's testimony for his mukatib is also not permissible for the same reason we have stated. ... Clarification: Imam Quduri said that the master's testimony for his slave is not accepted. The previous proof includes the hadith 'A master has no testimony for his slave?'. And the rational proof is that a master's testifying for his slave is in one aspect or in every aspect testimony for himself. Because there are two states of the slave: either people have debt on him or not. If there is debt, the master's testimony is in one aspect for himself because the debtor slave's situation is suspended: the creditors may sell him and he becomes theirs, making the master a stranger; or the master may pay the debt and the slave remains his. So in one aspect it is for himself and one aspect not, thus it is min wajh. If no debt, then the master owns the slave and all his property, so testifying for the slave is in every aspect for himself. Since testifying for oneself is impermissible, the master's testimony for his slave is impermissible. Similarly for the mukatib: if he pays the kitaba, he becomes free and the master is a stranger; if he fails, he remains a slave. So it is also min wajh, and thus not accepted.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling that a master cannot testify for his slave or mukatib (a slave under contract of manumission). The commentator provides both a rational proof and a textual proof (hadith: 'لا شهادة لمولى على عبده' - no testimony for a master against his slave? Actually the hadith is 'لا شهادة لمولى على عبده'). The reasoning is that the master's testimony is either completely (min kulli wajh) or partially (min wajh) self-interested. If the slave has no debts, the master owns the slave and his property completely, so testifying for the slave is like testifying for oneself. If the slave has debts, the situation is uncertain: the creditors may claim the slave, making the master a stranger, or the master may pay the debts and retain ownership. Thus it is partially self-interested. Since both types of self-interested testimony are invalid, the master's testimony for his slave is rejected. The same logic applies to the mukatib: if he completes his contract, he becomes free and the master is a stranger; if he fails, he remains a slave. The uncertainty makes it partially self-interested, so the testimony is not accepted.

Key Terms
مولیٰ (mawlā): Master, owner of a slave.
غلام (ghulām): A male slave who is fully owned by the master.
مکاتب (mukātab): A slave who has contracted with the master for manumission upon payment of a sum (badal al-kitaba).
شهادة لنفسه (shahādatun li nafsihi): Testimony given for oneself, which is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master's slave has debts, why is the master's testimony for the slave considered 'min wajh' (partial self-interest)?
A) Because the slave is free and not fully owned.
B) Because the creditors might take the slave, making the master a stranger, or the master might pay and retain ownership.
C) Because the master must pay the debts himself.
D) Because the slave's testimony is also invalid.

Key Takeaway
The master's testimony for his slave or mukatib is invalid because it is either entirely or partially self-interested.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Partner's Testimony in Partnership Property Not Accepted
Explains when partner testimony is rejected due to shared interest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a partner's testimony for a co-partner concerning partnership property is inadmissible due to tuhmah, and distinguish cases where testimony is accepted.

Core Idea
A partner's testimony for a co-partner in partnership property is invalid because it is testimony for oneself in part.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi testimony law: a partner cannot testify for his co-partner regarding property that belongs to their partnership. The rationale is that such testimony is partially self-interested, creating a suspicion of bias. However, if the testimony concerns property outside the partnership, it is accepted. Understanding this distinction helps clarify the broader principle that any personal interest renders testimony inadmissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal act under discussion? It is a partner giving testimony for his co-partner. The ruling: such testimony is not accepted (batil) when the subject matter is partnership property.
Focus on the phrase 'ما هو من شركتهما' (what is of their partnership).
2
Understand the reason (illah) for rejection
The text states the testimony is rejected 'because it is testimony for himself in one aspect.' The shared ownership creates a partial interest (tuhmah) that undermines the witness's neutrality.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the principle that no one can testify for themselves.
3
Contrast with testimony on non-partnership property
If the partner testifies about property that is not part of the partnership, there is no shared interest (tuhmah is absent), so the testimony is accepted.
The distinction hinges on the presence or absence of the witness's own interest.
4
Apply the indivisibility principle
The text gives an example: if one partner sues a third party over partnership property and the other partner testifies for him, the entire testimony is invalid. Even though only a portion of the property belongs to the witness, testimony cannot be split; partial invalidity invalidates the whole.
This reinforces the strictness: any degree of self-interest taints the entire testimony.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
The Hanafi position is strict on this point. Other schools may accept partner testimony in certain circumstances, but the Hanafi view is relied upon due to the clear principle of tuhmah.
In practice, a Hanafi mufti will reject such testimony categorically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا شهادة الشريك لشريكه فيما هو من شركتهما لانه ادة لنفسه من وجه لاشتراكهما ولو شهد بما ليس من شركتهما تقبل لانتفاء التهمة
شهـ
ترجمہ اور ایک شریک کی گواہی اُس کے دوسرے شریک کے واسطے ایسی چیز میں جائز نہیں ہے۔ جو ان دونوں کی شرکت میں ہے کیونکہ یہ من وجہ اس کی ذات کے واسطے شہادت ہے اس لئے کہ دونوں کی شرکت ہے اور اگر ایسی چیز میں گواہی دی جو ان دونوں کی شرکت میں نہیں ہے تو قبول کر لی جائے گی کیونکہ کوئی تہمت نہیں ہے۔
اور اگر مال شرکت میں ایک شریک نے کسی پر کوئی دعوی کیا اور دوسرے شریک نے اس کے واسطے گواہی دی تو یہ گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ مال مدعی بہ مدعی اور شاہد کے درمیان مشترک ہے ۔ لہذا شاہد کی شہادت مال کے کچھ حصہ میں وہ خود شاہد ہی کے واسطے ہوگی۔ اور یہ باطل ہے۔ اور جب بعض مال کی شہادت باطل ہو گئی تو پورے مال کی شہادت باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ کیوں کہ شہادت ایک ہے اس میں تجربی ( ٹکڑے ٹکڑے ) نہیں ہو سکتی کہ ایک ہی شہادت بعض مال میں درست ہو۔ اور بعض میں باطل ہو۔ اور اگر ایک شریک نے اپنے شریک کے واسطے ایسی چیز میں شہادت دی جو ان کی شرکت میں نہیں ہے تو یہ گواہی قبول ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں شہادت لنفسہ لازم نہ آنے کی وجہ سے شاہد متہم نہ ہوگا اور جب شاہد اپنی شہادت میں متہم نہیں ہوگا تو اس کی شہادت بھی قبول کر لی جائے گی۔
And the testimony of a partner for his partner in what is of their partnership is not accepted, because it is testimony for himself in one aspect due to their partnership. And if he testifies in what is not of their partnership, it is accepted due to the absence of suspicion. Explanation: The testimony of one partner for another partner in a matter that is part of their partnership is not permissible because it is in one aspect testimony for himself due to their shared ownership. And if he testifies in a matter that is not part of their partnership, it will be accepted because there is no suspicion. If in partnership property one partner claims against someone and the other partner testifies for him, this testimony will also not be accepted because the claimed property is shared between the claimant and the witness. Therefore, the witness's testimony pertains to a portion of the property that is actually for himself. This is invalid. And when the testimony for a part of the property is invalid, the testimony for the whole property becomes invalid because testimony is one and indivisible; it cannot be valid for one part and invalid for another. If one partner testifies for his partner in a matter that is not part of their partnership, this testimony is accepted because in that case, since testifying for himself does not apply, the witness is not under suspicion.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on testimony between business partners. A partner cannot testify for his co-partner concerning the partnership property itself because any benefit or loss from that property directly affects both partners. Thus, testifying about partnership property is partially self-interested (min wajh). However, if a partner testifies for his co-partner about property separate from the partnership (e.g., the other partner's personal property), such testimony is accepted because there is no shared interest and thus no suspicion of bias. The commentator also provides an example: if one partner sues someone over partnership property and the other partner testifies in support, that testimony is invalid because the property in dispute is partly owned by the testifying partner. Since testimony cannot be split, the entire testimony is invalid. This highlights the Hanafi principle that any personal interest, even partial, renders testimony inadmissible.

Key Terms
شریک (sharīk): A partner in a business or property arrangement.
شرکت (shirkah): Partnership; the joint ownership of property or business.
تہمت (tuhmah): Suspicion of bias or self-interest in testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case is a partner's testimony for his co-partner accepted?
A) When the testimony is about a debt of the partnership.
B) When the testimony concerns property that is not part of the partnership.
C) When the witness partner owns a majority share.
D) When both partners agree to the testimony.

Key Takeaway
A partner's testimony for his co-partner regarding partnership property is rejected due to suspicion of self-interest, but testimony regarding separate property is accepted.

Shahadat — Testimony
