بعض حضرات نے ان سات پر سود کھانے اور یتیم کا مال ناحق طور پر کھانے کا بھی اضافہ کیا ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے فرمایا کہ جو کام حرام لعینہ ہے وہ گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ ہر وہ گناہ جس پر حد وارد ہوئی ہو وہ کبیرہ گناہ کہلاتا ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ جو کام مسلمانوں کے نزدیک شفیع اور معیوب ہو اور اس میں اللہ اور اس کے دین کی ہتک حرمت ہوتی ہو وہ کبیرہ گناہ ہے اور بعض نے کہا کہ کسی گناہ پر اصرار کرنا کبیرہ ہے صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ گناہ ایک اضافی چیز ہے یعنی ہر گناہ ایسا ہے جس کے اوپر بھی گناہ ہے اور نیچے بھی گناہ ہے۔ پس نیچے کے گناہ کے اعتبار سے اس کو کبیرہ کہا جائے اور اوپر کے اعتبار سے صغیرہ کہا جائے گا۔
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص بغیر ازار کے برہنہ حمام میں داخل ہو یعنی ستر عورت کھول کر جائے اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ شرمگاہ اور واجب الستر بدن کا کھولنا حرام ہے اور حرام کا مرتکب فاسق ہوتا ہے۔ اور فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ نیز رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے لعن الله الناظر والمنظور الیہ یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ شرمگاہ کو دیکھنے والے اور جس کی شرمگاہ کو دیکھا گیا دونوں پر لعنت کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ شرمگاہ کھولنے والا لعنت کا مستحق ہے اور شہادت ایک کرامت ہے۔ پس جو شخص لعنت کا مستحق ہے وہ شہادت کا مستحق نہیں ہوتا۔ حمام سے غسل کرنے کی وہ جگہ مراد ہے جو ہوٹل میں تیار کر دی جاتی ہے اور پھر مردو عورت ہر طرح کا آدمی آ کر اس میں غسل کرتا ہے۔ صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ سود کھانے والے کی گواہی بھی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی اور نر دیا شطرنج کے ساتھ جوا کھیلنے والے کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ سود خوری اور قمار بازی دونوں کبیرہ گناہ ہیں اور سابق میں گزر چکا ہے کہ کبیرہ گناہ کے مرتکب کی گواہی قبول ۔ انہیں کی جاتی۔ لہذا ہود خور اور قمار باز کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ لیکن مبسوط میں یہ شرط مذکور ہے کہ سود خور اگر سودخوری میں مشہور بین الناس ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر سود خوری میں مشہور نہ ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ انسان بالعموم عقود فاسدہ کا مرتکب ہوتا ہے اور بہت کم لوگ ایسے ہیں جو عقود فاسدہ سے بچ جاتے ہیں اور عقود فاسدہ بھی رہا اور سود کے معنی میں ہے۔ پس اگر مطلقاً سود خوری کے ساتھ مبتلا شخص کی گواہی کو رد کر دیا گیا تو دنیا میں بہت کم لوگ مقبول الشبادت رہ جائیں گے۔ اور اس صورت میں دقت کا
besturdubooks.wordpress.com
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Volume 10, page 75. The testimony of a singer (male or female) and a committer of a major sin is not acceptable. Kitab al-Shahadah. He said: 'And not (acceptable is) one who sings for people, because he gathers people upon committing a major sin.' He said: 'And not (acceptable is) one who commits any of the major sins that entail a hadd penalty, due to fisq.' He said: 'And not (acceptable is) one who enters the bathhouse without a waistcloth, because uncovering the private parts is haram, or consumes riba, or gambles with backgammon and chess, because all of that is among the major sins. And likewise, one whose prayer is missed due to preoccupation with these two. As for mere playing of chess, it is not a disqualifying transgression preventing testimony, because there is scope for ijtihad in it. And in al-Asl, the condition is that the consumer of riba be well-known for it, because a person rarely escapes entering into invalid contracts, and all of that is riba.' And he said: 'And not (acceptable is) one who does contemptible acts such as urinating on the road and eating on the road, because he abandons chivalry (muruwah). And when he is not ashamed of such things, he will not refrain from lying, so he is accused. And the testimony of one who openly reviles the Salaf is not accepted, due to the manifestation of his fisq, unlike one who conceals it.' Commentary: The translator says: The testimony of one who makes people listen to singing is not accepted, because he gathers people upon committing a major sin. And the testimony of one who commits a major sin that entails a hadd penalty is not accepted, because such a person is a fasiq. And the testimony of one who enters the bathhouse without a waistcloth is not accepted, because uncovering the private parts is haram. Or one who consumes riba or gambles with backgammon and chess, because each is among the major sins. And likewise, the testimony of one whose prayer is missed due to these two is not accepted. As for mere playing of chess, it is not such fisq that prevents testimony, because there is scope for ijtihad in it. And in al-Mabsut, there is a condition that the consumer of riba be well-known for consuming riba, because a person rarely escapes from committing invalid contracts, and each of them is riba. And the testimony of one who does contemptible acts like urinating on the road and eating on the road is not accepted, because he abandons muruwah; and when he is not ashamed of such things, he will not refrain from lying, hence he is accused. And the testimony of one who openly reviles the Salaf is not accepted because his fisq is apparent, unlike one who conceals it. Elaboration: Sayyid al-Quduri said: The testimony of a person who makes others listen to singing is not accepted, just as the testimony of listeners is not accepted, because this person gathers people upon a major sin, and gathering people upon a major sin is itself a major sin, and the testimony of a committer of a major sin is not accepted. Hence, the testimony of one who makes others listen to singing will not be accepted. However, if a person sings alone to amuse himself, according to Imam Sarakhsi, such singing is not makruh, because it is narrated from Anas that he went to his brother Bara' ibn Malik, who was an ascetic Companion, yet Bara' was singing. Shaykh al-Islam Khwaharzadah said that singing is absolutely makruh, both for making others listen and for alone amusement. And they interpret the hadith of Anas to mean that Bara' was reciting permissible poems containing admonition and wisdom, and reciting permissible poems is not objectionable. Sayyid al-Quduri said: If a person has committed a major sin for which a hadd penalty is prescribed, such as theft or adultery, his testimony is not accepted, because committing such a sin makes him a fasiq, and the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted. Therefore, his testimony is not accepted. Scholars differ in the interpretation of major sins. Some said: Major sins are seven, which the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) mentioned in a well-known hadith: associating partners with Allah; fleeing from the battlefield; disobedience to parents; wrongfully killing a believer; slandering a believer; drinking wine; and adultery. Some added to these seven: consuming riba and wrongfully devouring the orphan's property. Some said: Whatever act is inherently haram is a major sin. Some said: Every sin for which a hadd penalty is prescribed is called a major sin. Some said: Whatever act is considered vile and disgraceful among Muslims and involves contempt for Allah and His religion is a major sin. Some said: Persistence in a sin makes it major. The correct view is that sin is a relative matter; that is, every sin has a sin greater and a sin lesser. So relative to the sin below, it is called major; relative to the sin above, it is called minor. Sayyid al-Quduri said: A person who enters the bathhouse naked without a waistcloth, i.e., exposing the private parts, his testimony is not accepted because uncovering the private parts and the body that must be covered is haram, and the committer of haram is a fasiq. And the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted. Therefore, his testimony is not accepted. Also, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'May Allah curse the one who looks and the one whose privates are looked at,' meaning Allah curses both the one who looks at the private parts and the one whose private parts are looked at. The conclusion is that the one who exposes his private parts deserves curse, and testimony is an honor. So one who deserves curse does not deserve testimony. Bathhouse here means the place prepared for bathing in a hotel, where all sorts of men and women come to bathe. Sayyid al-Quduri said: The testimony of a consumer of riba is not accepted, nor of one who gambles with backgammon and chess. The evidence is that riba and gambling are both major sins, and it has passed earlier that the testimony of a committer of a major sin is not accepted. Hence, the testimony of a riba consumer and a gambler is not accepted. But in al-Mabsut, it is mentioned that if the riba consumer is well-known among the people for consuming riba, his testimony is not accepted. If he is not well-known for consuming riba, his testimony is accepted. Because a person generally commits invalid contracts, and very few people avoid invalid contracts, and invalid contracts are also riba in meaning. Therefore, if the testimony of anyone involved in riba were rejected absolutely, very few people would be of accepted testimony in the world, and that would cause difficulty.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary (sharh) on al-Quduri's matn regarding the qualifications of witnesses. It lists several categories of people whose testimony is rejected due to fisq (moral depravity) or lack of muruwah (chivalry/dignity). The primary ruling is that a witness must be 'adl (just, upright), and committing major sins destroys that uprightness.

The first category is the mughanni (singer) who sings for people. The reasoning is that he gathers people upon a major sin (singing itself being considered a major sin by many scholars). The commentary notes an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Sarakhsi considers singing alone for amusement not makruh, citing the practice of Bara' ibn Malik. Khwaharzadah says singing is absolutely makruh. The commentary reconciles by saying Bara' was reciting permissible poems, not singing.

The second category is those who commit any major sin (kabirah) that entails a hadd punishment, such as theft or adultery. Such a person is a fasiq and rejected. The commentary then provides a rich discussion on the definition of kabirah, noting multiple scholarly views: the seven great sins from a hadith, sins with prescribed hadd, sins that are inherently haram, sins that are contemptible in Muslim society, and persistence in sin. The preferred view is that kabirah is relative: a sin is major compared to a smaller one, minor compared to a greater one.

The third category is entering a public bathhouse (hammam) without a waistcloth (izar), exposing the private parts. This is haram, and the committer is a fasiq. The commentary adds a hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) cursed both the one who looks and the one whose private parts are exposed.

The fourth category is consuming riba (usury/interest). The matn states it is a major sin, disqualifying the witness. However, the commentary from al-Mabsut adds a critical condition: the consumer must be well-known (mashhur) for it. This is because many people engage in invalid contracts that technically involve riba, and if all were rejected, few would remain as acceptable witnesses. So only notorious riba consumers are rejected.

The fifth category is gambling (qimar) with backgammon (nard) and chess (shatranj). These are major sins. However, a nuance: mere play of chess without gambling is not disqualifying, as there is room for ijtihad on its permissibility. But if it causes one to miss prayers, it becomes disqualifying.

The sixth category is those who perform contemptible acts (af'ala mustahqara) like urinating or eating on the public road. Such acts show lack of muruwah (dignity). Such a person is not ashamed of vile acts, so he may not refrain from lying, thus is suspect.

The seventh category is those who openly revile the Salaf (the early Muslims, including the Companions). This manifests fisq. However, if one merely conceals such views (without expressing them), his testimony is not rejected based on mere private belief.

Throughout, the key principle is that testimony is an honor (karamah) and requires moral uprightness. The mukhalif (opposing views) are not presented here; it is a Hanafi text. The authority weight is from the mutun and sharh of the Hanafi school; the condition about mashhur riba is from al-Mabsut (a Zahir al-Riwayah source).

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given in court; it is an honor that requires uprightness.
فسق (fisq): Departure from obedience to Allah and moral uprightness.
كبيرة (kabirah): Major sin; the definition is disputed among scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn in this lesson, why is the testimony of a singer who sings for people rejected?
A) Because singing is always haram.
B) Because he gathers people upon committing a major sin.
C) Because he wastes time.
D) Because he is not a reliable narrator of hadith.

Key Takeaway
A singer who performs for an audience is a fasiq and his testimony is rejected; solitary singing is subject to ikhtilaf.

Testimony of One Who Enters Bathhouse Naked
Ruling: testimony is rejected due to nakedness in bathhouse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the testimony of a person who enters the bathhouse naked is rejected, explain the reasoning based on the prohibition of exposing private parts and the status of fasiq, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Exposing private parts is haram, making one a fasiq; a fasiq's testimony is rejected.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on the testimony of a person who enters a bathhouse naked. The Hanafi school holds that such an act is haram, rendering the person a fasiq (transgressor). Since the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted, his testimony is rejected. We will explore the reasoning, the hadith cited, and the implications for witness integrity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering the bathhouse naked, i.e., exposing the private parts. According to the text, this is haram (unlawful).
2
Understand the legal consequence
Committing a haram act makes the person a fasiq (transgressor). A fasiq's testimony is not accepted in Islamic court.
3
Analyze the hadith proof
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'May Allah curse the one who looks and the one who is looked at.' This hadith emphasizes the sinfulness, showing that exposing private parts invites the curse of Allah, and a cursed person is not deserving of the honor of testimony.
4
Apply the ruling to real scenarios
The bathhouse refers to public bathing facilities like hotel pools. Anyone who exposes their private parts in such places becomes fasiq and loses testimonial capacity until repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص بغیر ازار کے برہنہ حمام میں داخل ہو یعنی ستر عورت کھول کر جائے اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ شرمگاہ اور واجب الستر بدن کا کھولنا حرام ہے اور حرام کا مرتکب فاسق ہوتا ہے۔ اور فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی ۔ لہذا اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ نیز رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے لعن الله الناظر والمنظور الیہ یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ شرمگاہ کو دیکھنے والے اور جس کی شرمگاہ کو دیکھا گیا دونوں پر لعنت کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ شرمگاہ کھولنے والا لعنت کا مستحق ہے اور شہادت ایک کرامت ہے۔ پس جو شخص لعنت کا مستحق ہے وہ شہادت کا مستحق نہیں ہوتا۔ حمام سے غسل کرنے کی وہ جگہ مراد ہے جو ہوٹل میں تیار کر دی جاتی ہے اور پھر مردو عورت ہر طرح کا آدمی آ کر اس میں غسل کرتا ہے۔
Sahib al-Quduri said: The person who enters the bathhouse naked without a waist-wrapper, i.e., exposing his private parts, his testimony will not be accepted. Because exposing the private parts and the body that must be covered is unlawful (haram), and the committer of haram is a transgressor (fasiq). And the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted. Therefore, his testimony will not be accepted. Also, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'May Allah curse the one who looks and the one who is looked at,' meaning Allah curses both the one who looks at the private parts and the one whose private parts are seen. The conclusion is that the one who exposes his private parts deserves curse, and testimony is a honor. So the one who deserves curse is not deserving of testimony. By bathhouse is meant the place prepared for bathing in hotels, where every kind of person, men and women, come and bathe.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This is a ruling from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author explains that entering the bathhouse naked is haram because it exposes the private parts. The person is thus a fasiq, and a fasiq's testimony is rejected. The hadith reinforces this: both the looker and the one looked at are cursed. Since testimony is a honor, a cursed person cannot be a witness. The bathhouse here refers to public bathing facilities.

Key Terms
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits a major sin or persists in minor sins, thereby losing moral integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it is a waste of water
B) Because it is a major sin, making the person a fasiq
C) Because the person is considered insane
D) Because the Prophet cursed only the one who looks

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a person who exposes his private parts in a bathhouse is rejected because the act is haram and makes him a fasiq.

Testimony of a Backgammon Player
Ruling: backgammon player's testimony is rejected without any condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a backgammon player and explain the dalil from the hadith of curse.

Core Idea
Playing backgammon makes one unreliable as a witness — the curse renders adala impossible.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hidayah: the testimony of a backgammon (nard) player is rejected unconditionally. The Hanafi school bases this on a hadith that curses the player, which directly impacts the witness's uprightness (adala). Understanding this ruling helps clarify how the school links moral character to legal capacity to testify.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled on? Playing backgammon (nard). What is the ruling? The player's testimony is rejected (mardud al-shahada) without any condition, even if no betting is involved.
The ruling is absolute, not contingent on gambling.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith: 'Cursed is the one who plays with backgammon' (ملعون من لعب بالنرد). This is a Sunnah ahad, transmitted through one chain.
The hadith is the primary evidence; no Quranic verse is cited.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The curse (la'na) indicates that the act is haram and the person is sinful. A sinful person lacks adala (uprightness), and testimony is only accepted from an adil person. The explicit curse removes adala, so the testimony is rejected.
The curse is treated as a decisive indicator (qati' al-dalala) of sinfulness.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? The Hanafi position is unconditional rejection. Other madhhabs may differentiate: some consider nard only makruh if not for gambling, or accept testimony if the player repents. The Hanafi school holds that the curse makes the act inherently haram, thus the player is always non-adil.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is the Hanafi position mufta bihi? The hadith is strong (though ahad in thubut, qati in dalala). The Hanafi principle that a cursed person cannot be adil is logically sound. Later authorities like al-Marghinani uphold this as the relied-upon view.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is consistently followed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور نرد کے ساتھ کھیلنے والا بغیر شرط کے مردود الشہادت ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے ملعون من لعب بالنرد يعنى نرد کے ساتھ کھیلنے والا شخص ملعون ہے۔ اور ملعون شخص عادل کیسے ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس جب نرد کے ساتھ کھیلنے والا ملعون اور غیر عادل ہے تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ گواہی عادل کی قبول ہوتی ہے نہ غیر عادل کی۔ نرد ایک قسم کا کھیل جس کو اردشیر بن بابک شاہ ایران نے ایجاد کیا تھا۔
And the one who plays with backgammon is rejected of testimony without any condition (of betting). Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Cursed is the one who plays with backgammon.' So how can a cursed person be upright (adil)? So when the one who plays with backgammon is cursed and not upright, his testimony will not be accepted. Because testimony is accepted from an upright person, not from a non-upright person. Backgammon is a type of game invented by Ardashir bin Babak, the king of Iran.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a ruling that a backgammon player's testimony is rejected unconditionally, even without betting. The proof is a hadith declaring the player cursed. The author argues that a cursed person cannot be considered upright (adil), and since testimony requires uprightness, it is rejected. The text also defines backgammon (nard) as a game invented by the Persian king Ardashir.

Key Terms
نرد (nard): A game of backgammon, considered haram even without betting.
ملعون (mal'un): Cursed; one who is removed from divine mercy. Used in the hadith to describe the backgammon player.
عادل (adil): Upright, just; a necessary quality for a witness. The opposite is ghayr adil (non-upright) or fasiq (sinner).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Accepted, because there is no gambling
B) Rejected, because the player is cursed
C) Accepted if he repents
D) Rejected only if he is addicted

Key Takeaway
A backgammon player's testimony is rejected unconditionally because the hadith curse makes him non-adil.

Testimony of a Chess Player in Hanafi Fiqh
Inter-madhhab dispute: Hanafi conditions for rejecting testimony of a chess player.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that disqualify a chess player's testimony in the Hanafi school and explain why mere chess playing does not invalidate adala.

Core Idea
Mere play does not break your moral shield — only gambling, missing prayer, or false oaths do.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a chess player. While playing chess is sometimes considered sinful, the Hanafi school distinguishes between mere play and play accompanied by major sins. The key is that scholarly disagreement on chess itself prevents it from being fisq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on chess testimony
State the Hanafi position: testimony of a chess player is accepted unless one of three specific conditions is present.
The default is acceptance; rejection is exceptional.
2
List the three rejecting conditions
The passage lists gambling with chess, missing prayer due to chess, and frequent false oaths during play. All three are major sins.
The third condition is rarely mentioned because the first two are more common.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof for mere chess
The text argues that mere chess without those conditions is not fisq because there is a legitimate ikhtilaf among scholars — Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i consider it halal. A person cannot be fasiq for doing what some recognized mujtahids permit.
This is a classic example of ikhtilaf removing the charge of fisq.
4
Explore the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Hanafi law, a mere chess player's testimony is accepted; under schools that consider chess haram unconditionally, it would be rejected.
The practical effect is on the acceptability of testimony in court.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شطرنج کے ساتھ کھیلنے والے کی گواہی اس وقت مردود ہوگی جبکہ تین باتوں میں سے ایک بات پائی جائے یا تو شطرنج کے ساتھ جوا کھیلتا ہو۔ یا شطرنج میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے نماز فوت ہوتی ہے۔ یا شطرنج کھیلنے میں جھوٹی قسمیں زیادہ کھاتا ہو۔ کیونکہ تینوں چیزیں کبائر میں سے ہیں۔ مصنف نے تیسری بات کا ذکر نہیں فرمایا ہے کیونکہ اول کی دو باتوں کا وقوع غالب ہے رہا محض شطرنج کھیلنا تو وہ فسق نہیں ہے اور جب فسق نہیں ہے تو مانع شہادت بھی نہ ہوگا اور بغیر مذکورہ تین باتوں کے محض شطرنج کھیلنا اس لئے فسق نہیں کہ علماء کا اس میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک شطرنج کھیلنا حلال اور جائز ہے پس جو چیز دو جلیل القدر علماء کے نزدیک حلال اور جائز ہو اس کا مرتکب فاسق کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اور جس چیز کا مرتکب فاسق نہ ہو اس کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے لہذا محض شطرنج کھیلنے والے کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔
The testimony of the one who plays chess will be rejected only when one of three things is found: either he gambles with chess, or due to being occupied with chess he misses prayer, or he frequently takes false oaths while playing chess. Because these three things are among major sins. The author did not mention the third thing because the occurrence of the first two is predominant. As for merely playing chess, that is not fisq. And when it is not fisq, it will not prevent testimony. Merely playing chess without the mentioned three things is not fisq because there is disagreement among scholars about it. Indeed, according to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, playing chess is lawful (halal) and permissible (ja'iz). So how can a person be fasiq for doing something that two great imams consider halal and permissible? And the one who is not fasiq, his testimony is accepted. Therefore, the testimony of one who merely plays chess will be accepted.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This ruling discusses chess player's testimony. The Hanafi position conditions rejection on three scenarios: gambling, missing prayer, or frequent false oaths. Mere chess playing is not fisq due to ikhtilaf among the imams; Malik and Shafi'i consider it halal. So a mere chess player retains uprightness and testimony is accepted. This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafis consider chess potentially sinful only in certain contexts, while others consider it inherently permissible.

Key Terms
شطرنج (shatranj): Chess; the text distinguishes between mere play and play involving gambling, missing prayer, or oath-breaking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, when is the testimony of a chess player rejected?
A) Always, because chess is a form of gambling
B) Only if he gambles, misses prayer, or takes false oaths
C) Only if he plays for money
D) Never, because chess is halal

Key Takeaway
A chess player's testimony is only rejected in Hanafi law if he gambles, misses prayer, or takes false oaths; mere play is not fisq due to scholarly disagreement.

Testimony of a Person with Low Mura'ah (Dignity)
Ruling: testimony rejected due to lack of muru'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a person lacking muru'ah and explain the legal reasoning based on the link between public shame and truthfulness.

Core Idea
Lack of muru'ah in public acts indicates a lack of shame that makes a witness suspect in testimony.

The reliability of a witness in Islamic law is not only about factual honesty but also about public dignity (muru'ah). A person who openly commits shameful acts is presumed to lack the moral restraint that prevents lying. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on such a witness and the underlying reasoning that connects public behavior to legal credibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly that the testimony of a person who performs acts lacking muru'ah is rejected (ghayr maqbul).
The ruling is from Sahib al-Quduri.
2
List the examples of shameful acts
Identify the specific acts mentioned: urinating on the road, eating on the road, eating publicly in the market, and (according to al-Karkhi) walking in the road wearing only a loincloth.
These acts are considered violations of muru'ah.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning
Trace the logic: such a person abandons muru'ah -> not ashamed of these acts -> will not be ashamed of lying -> therefore his testimony is suspected -> rejected.
This is a qiyas (analogy) linking public shamelessness to potential dishonesty.
4
Note the consensus
Observe that the text states all four imams (Hanafi, Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) agree on this ruling, making it a strong legal position.
Ijma strengthens the ruling's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص خفیف و حقیر حرکات کرتا ہو اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی جیسے راستہ پر پیشاب کرنا، راستہ پر کھانا ، اور بازار میں برسر عام کھانا اور بقول امام کرخی کے صرف تہبند یا پائجامہ پہن کر راستہ میں چلنا۔ کیونکہ ایسا آدمی مروت اور انسانیت کو ترک کر دیتا ہے اور جب وہ ایسے کاموں سے شرم نہیں کرتا تو جھوٹ بولنے سے بھی شرم نہیں کرے گا اور جو شخص جھوٹ بولنے سے نہ شرماتا ہو وہ اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہوگا اور جو شخص اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہو اس کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ اس مسئلہ میں چاروں ائمہ کا اتفاق ہے۔
Sahib al-Quduri said: The person who performs trivial and contemptible acts, his testimony will not be accepted. For example, urinating on the road, eating on the road, and eating publicly in the market. And according to Imam al-Karkhi, walking on the road wearing only a loincloth or pajama. Because such a person abandons dignity (muru'ah) and humanity. And when he is not ashamed of such acts, he will not be ashamed of lying. And the person who is not ashamed of lying will be suspected in his testimony. And the person who is suspected in his testimony, his testimony is not accepted. Therefore, his testimony will not be accepted. On this issue, all four imams are in agreement.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This ruling addresses testimony of a person lacking mura'ah (dignity). The acts listed are considered shameful in society. The reasoning is that such lack of shame indicates a tendency to lie, making the witness unreliable. The passage notes consensus (ijma) of the four imams on this point.

Key Terms
مروت (muru'ah): Dignity; a trait that prevents a person from doing shameful acts in public.
خفیف حرکات (khafif harakat): Trivial or contemptible acts; actions that are considered lowly and lacking in dignity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi madhhab reject the testimony of a person who urinates on the road?
A) It is a physical impurity
B) It indicates lack of shame and dignity, making him suspect in testimony
C) It is a health hazard
D) It is only a sin if done intentionally

Key Takeaway
Lack of muru'ah in public acts makes a witness suspect in testimony, leading to rejection, and this is agreed upon by all four imams.

Testimony of One Who Reviles the Companions and Scholars
Ruling: rejected if he verbally abuses, but not if he merely holds bad beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the testimony of a person who verbally abuses the Companions, Tabi'un, or imams, and distinguish it from the case of internal belief without expression.

Core Idea
Verbal abuse disqualifies testimony; internal belief does not — fisq requires outward action.

This ruling from Al-Quduri addresses a critical distinction: when does a person's attitude toward the righteous predecessors affect their legal capacity to testify? The Hanafi position carefully separates internal belief from public expression, ensuring that people are judged by their actions, not their private thoughts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what specific behavior is under discussion: reviling the Companions, Tabi'un, and mujtahid imams. The ruling is that testimony is rejected if the person verbally abuses them.
2
Identify the basis for rejection
The text states that such a person is obviously a fasiq, and the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted. Thus, verbal abuse constitutes fisq.
3
Distinguish the case of internal belief
The author explicitly says that if someone holds bad beliefs internally but does not express them, the person remains adil (upright) and his testimony is accepted.
4
Understand the Hanafi principle
This distinction reflects the Hanafi emphasis that fisq requires commission of a major sin or persistence on minor sins; mere belief (a'qida) without action does not render one fasiq unless accompanied by expression.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص صحابہ، تابعین اور ائمہ مجتہدین کو برا بھلا کہتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیوں کہ ایسے شخص کا فاسق ہونا ظاہر ہے اور فاسق کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے اور اگر اُن کے بارے میں برائیوں کا اعتقاد تو رکھتا ہو مگر ان کو ظاہر نہیں کرتا تو یہ شخص عادل اور مقبول الشہادت ہے۔
Sahib al-Quduri said: If a person speaks ill of the Companions, the Followers (tabi'un), and the mujtahid imams, his testimony will also not be accepted. Because it is obvious that such a person is a fasiq, and the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted. And if he only holds bad beliefs about them but does not express them, then this person is upright (adil) and acceptable of testimony.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between verbal abuse and mere belief. Reviling the Sahabah, Tabi'un, or imams is an act of fisq, disqualifying testimony. However, if one only holds bad beliefs internally without expressing, he remains upright. This aligns with the Hanafi principle that action is required for fisq, not mere belief.

Key Terms
صحابہ (sahabah): Companions of the Prophet; reviling them is a major sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His testimony is rejected
B) His testimony is accepted
C) He must repent first
D) It depends on the judge's opinion

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, disqualification from testimony due to reviling the Companions requires outward verbal abuse; internal belief without expression does not impair one's uprightness (adalah).

Testimony of People of Innovation (Ahl al-Ahwa')
Hanafi ruling on testimony of ahl al-ahwa' with Shafi'i disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of ahl al-ahwa', explain the reasoning (dalil), and distinguish the exception of Khattabiyyah.

Core Idea
Innovation in belief does not disqualify testimony; only those who permit false testimony are excluded.

The testimony of witnesses is crucial in Islamic courts. One key question is whether a person who holds heretical beliefs (ahl al-ahwa') can be a credible witness. This lesson examines the Hanafi view, which accepts their testimony except for the extreme Khattabiyyah, and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position. We will analyze the reasoning behind each school's stance and the practical implications for judges.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on ahl al-ahwa'
The Hanafi school accepts their testimony except for the Khattabiyyah. Identify the general rule and the exception.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Al-Shafi'i rejects all testimony from ahl al-ahwa' because innovation is the worst form of fisq.
3
Analyse the Hanafi counter-evidence
The Hanafi response distinguishes fisq in belief from fisq in action; the innovator's tadayyun makes him avoid lying.
Analogous to one who mistakenly believes a forbidden act is permissible.
4
Distinguish the exception of Khattabiyyah
The Khattabiyyah are excluded because they consider perjury permissible for their sect, so doubt prevails about their truthfulness.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A Hanafi judge accepts such testimony, a Shafi'i judge rejects it. This affects court outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوائے فرقہ خطابیہ کے اہل ہوا کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے
وتقبل شهادة اهل الأهواء الا الخطابية وقال الشافعي لا تقبل لانه اغلظ وجوه الفسق ولنا انه فسق من حيث الاعتقاد وما اوقعه فيه الا تدينه فيمتنع عن الكذب وصار كمن يشرب المثلث او يأكل متروك التسمية عامدا مستبيحا لذلك بخلاف الفسق من حيث التعاطى اما الخطابية فهم قوم من غلاة الروافض يعتقدون الشهادة لكل من حلف عندهم وقيل يرون الشهادة لشيعتهم واجبة فتمكنت
The testimony of people of innovation (ahl al-ahwa') is acceptable except the Khattabiyyah. And al-Shafi'i said: It is not accepted because it is the worst kind of fisq. Our proof is that it is fisq from the perspective of belief, and nothing leads him into it except his religious commitment (tadayyun), so he refrains from lying, and he becomes like one who drinks wine or eats meat over which the name of Allah has not been mentioned, deliberately, considering it permissible, unlike fisq in action. As for the Khattabiyyah, they are a group from the extreme Rafidah who believe that testimony is acceptable for anyone who swears an oath by them, and it is said they consider testifying for their sect as obligatory, so doubt prevails.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage deals with the testimony of ahl al-ahwa' (people of heretical innovations). The Hanafi position accepts their testimony, except the Khattabiyyah. Shafi'i rejects all because innovation is worse fisq. The Hanafi reasoning: their fisq is in belief, not action; because their sin stems from excessive religiosity, they are actually less likely to lie. They are like a person who drinks wine considering it halal due to ignorance. The Khattabiyyah are excluded because they consider perjury for their sect permissible.

Key Terms
اہل ہوا (ahl al-ahwa'): People of heretical innovations; those who hold theological views condemned by mainstream Sunnis but not necessarily engaged in sinful acts.
خطابیہ (khattabiyyah): An extreme Rafidi sect that considers testimony valid for anyone who swears by them or obligatory for their followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because all Muslims are considered upright
B) Because their innovation is in belief, not action, and they refrain from lying due to religious commitment
C) Because their testimony is coerced
D) Only if they repent

Key Takeaway
Testimony of ahl al-ahwa' is accepted in Hanafi fiqh unless they belong to an extreme sect like Khattabiyyah that deems false testimony permissible.

Testimony of Backgammon and Chess Players: Conditions and Ikhtilaf
Explaining conditions for testimony of backgammon and chess players

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of backgammon and chess players, identify the three conditions that disqualify a chess player, and explain why mere chess playing is not fisq due to ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Backgammon players are always rejected; chess players only when they gamble, miss prayers, or swear falsely.

The testimony of a witness is a cornerstone of Islamic justice, but not everyone may serve. This passage from Al-Hidayah examines three types of people whose involvement in certain activities raises questions about their uprightness (adala): the usurer, the backgammon player, and the chess player. While the rulings on usury and backgammon are straightforward, the case of chess introduces a subtle inter-madhhab dispute: does mere play constitute fisq? Let's unpack the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify each category and its ruling
Locate the three categories: usurer (rejected if notorious), backgammon player (rejected unconditionally), chess player (rejected only if three conditions met). State each ruling.
Only the chess player's ruling has conditions.
2
Examine the dalil for backgammon
Find the hadith about backgammon: 'Cursed is the one who plays backgammon.' Understand how this hadith renders the player non-upright (ghayr adl).
The hadith is explicit about the curse, so no further conditions needed.
3
List the three disqualifying conditions for chess
Read the three conditions that make the chess player's testimony rejected: playing for a stake, missing prayers due to engrossment, frequently swearing false oaths.
The author notes that the first two are most common.
4
Understand why mere chess is not fisq
Analyze the argument: because of ikhtilaf among scholars (Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i permit chess), the act of playing chess without the three conditions is not fisq. Hence, testimony is accepted.
This is the core inter-madhhab point.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario of a chess player, check if any of the three conditions are present. If not, testimony is accepted. If yes, rejected.
Remember that the default is acceptance unless a condition is met.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الہدایہ جلد - دہم كتاب الشهادة یعنی پیش آنا ایک بدیہی امر ہے۔ حالانکہ شریعت اسلام میں دقت اور حرج کو دور کیا گیا۔ لہذا اسی سود خور کی گواہی مردود ہو گی ۔ جو سود خوری میں مشہور ہو۔ اور نرد کے ساتھ کھیلنے والا بغیر شرط کے مردود الشہادت ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے ملعون من لعب بالنرد يعنى نزد کے ساتھ کھیلنے والا شخص ملعون ہے۔ اور ملعون شخص عادل کیسے ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس جب نزد کے ساتھ کھیلنے والا ملعون اور غیر عادل ہے تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ گواہی عادل کی قبول ہوتی ہے نہ غیر عادل کی نزد ایک قسم کا کھیل جس کو اردشیر بن بابک شاہ ایران نے ایجاد کیا تھا۔ اور شطرنج کے ساتھ کھیلنے والے کی گواہی اس وقت مردود ہوگی جبکہ تین باتوں میں سے ایک بات پائی جائے یا تو شطرنج کے ساتھ جو اکھیلتا ہو۔
۲۔ یا شطرنج میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے نماز فوت ہوتی ہے۔
- یا شطرنج کھیلنے میں جھوٹی قسمیں زیادہ کھاتا ہو۔
کیونکہ تینوں چیزیں کبائر میں سے ہیں۔ مصنف نے تیسری بات کا ذکر نہیں فرمایا ہے کیونکہ اول کی دو باتوں کا وقوع غالب ہے رہا محض شطرنج کھیلنا تو وہ فسق نہیں ہے اور جب فسق نہیں ہے تو مانع شہادت بھی نہ ہوگا اور بغیر مذکورہ تین باتوں کے محض شطرنج کھیلنا اس لئے فسق نہیں کہ علماء کا اس میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام مالک اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک شطرنج کھیلنا حلال اور جائز ہے پس جو چیز دو جلیل القدر علماء کے نزدیک حلال اور جائز ہو اس کا مرتکب فاسق کیسے ہو سکتا ہے اور جس چیز کا مرتکب فاسق نہ ہو اس کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے لہذا محض شطرنج کھیلنے والی کی گواہی قبول کیجائے گی۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Volume 10, Kitab al-Shahadah. Meaning: Appearing [as a witness] is an obvious matter. However, Islamic law has removed difficulty and hardship. Therefore, the testimony of the same usurer is rejected, who is notorious for usury. And the one who plays backgammon without a stake is rejected in testimony. Because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Cursed is the one who plays backgammon,' meaning playing with backgammon is cursed. And how can a cursed person be upright? So when the backgammon player is cursed and not upright, his testimony is also not accepted. Because testimony is accepted from an upright person, not from a non-upright person. Backgammon is a type of game invented by Ardashir ibn Babak, the king of Iran. And the testimony of a chess player is rejected only when one of three things occurs: (1) he plays chess with a stake, (2) he misses prayers due to being engrossed, (3) he often swears false oaths while playing. Because all three things are major sins. The author did not mention the third, because the occurrence of the first two is predominant. As for mere chess playing, it is not fisq, and when it is not fisq, it will not be a preventive of testimony. And chess playing without the three mentioned conditions is not fisq because scholars differed on it: indeed, according to Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, chess playing is halal and permissible. So how can one who commits an act that two great scholars consider halal and permissible be a fasiq? And the testimony of one who is not a fasiq is accepted. Therefore, the testimony of a mere chess player is accepted.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage discusses three categories of witnesses whose testimony may be rejected due to their involvement in sinful practices. First, the usurer (who is notorious for usury) is rejected because usury is a major sin and he is a fasiq. Second, the backgammon player is rejected without any condition because the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly cursed such players, rendering them non-upright (ghayr adl). Third, the chess player is rejected only if one of three conditions is met: (1) playing for a stake (gambling), (2) missing compulsory prayers due to being engrossed, or (3) frequently swearing false oaths during play. Mere chess playing without these is not considered fisq because there is ikhtilaf among scholars; Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i regard it as permissible. Thus, in the Hanafi school, the testimony of a chess player who does not engage in these three prohibited aspects is accepted.

Key Terms
نرد (nard): A game similar to backgammon, played with dice and tokens; its player is cursed by the Prophet (peace be upon him).
شطرنج (shatranj): Chess; the author rules that playing it without condition is not fisq because of scholarly disagreement.
فسق (fisq): Legal depravity; committing major sins or persisting on minor sins; grounds for rejecting testimony.
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony; legal evidence given by a witness in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the testimony of a chess player accepted?
A) Always accepted, regardless of any conditions
B) Accepted only if he does not play for a stake, does not miss prayers, and does not swear false oaths
C) Never accepted because chess is haram
D) Accepted only if he plays with a stake

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a chess player is accepted unless he engages in gambling, misses prayers, or swears false oaths; mere play is not fisq due to ikhtilaf.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Disqualifying Testimony: Lack of Dignity and Insulting the Companions
Ruling on disqualification of witnesses with ijma proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two grounds for rejecting a witness's testimony based on lack of muruwwah and insulting the Companions, and apply the reasoning to determine admissibility of testimony.

Core Idea
A witness who commits contemptible acts or insults the Companions is disqualified because shamelessness indicates a lack of truthfulness.

In this lesson, we examine two additional reasons that disqualify a witness in Hanafi law. The first is a lack of dignity (muruwwah) demonstrated by contemptible public acts, and the second is verbally insulting the Companions or early Muslims. The text from al-Quduri explains the reasoning and notes the consensus of the four Imams on these principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disqualifying acts
List the acts mentioned in the text that violate muruwwah: urinating or eating on the road, eating publicly in the market, and walking in minimal clothing according to Imam al-Karkhi. Also note the second ground: speaking ill of the Companions, Followers, and Mujtahid Imams.
The first set involves public behaviour; the second involves speech.
2
Trace the logical chain for muruwwah
Follow the reasoning: if a person is not ashamed of such acts, they will not be ashamed of lying. A suspected liar's testimony is rejected. Hence, such a person's testimony is not accepted.
This is a syllogistic argument based on moral character.
3
Note the ijma (consensus)
The text states that all four Imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Al-Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree on this ruling. This ijma strengthens the proof and makes it binding.
Ijma is a primary dalil in Hanafi usul.
4
Distinguish inner belief from outward expression
For insulting the Companions, only outward verbal abuse disqualifies. Holding bad beliefs in one's heart without expressing them does not make one a fasiq, so the testimony is accepted.
This distinction is crucial to avoid over-breadth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ جو شخص خفیف و حقیر حرکات کرتا ہو اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی جیسے راستہ پر پیشاب کرنا، راستہ پر کھانا ، اور بازار میں برسر عام کھانا اور بقول امام کرخی کے صرف تہبند یا پائجامہ پہن کر راستہ میں چلنا۔ کیونکہ ایسا آدمی مروت اور انسانیت کو ترک کر دیتا ہے اور جب وہ ایسے کاموں سے شرم نہیں کرتا تو جھوٹ بولنے سے بھی شرم نہیں کرے گا اور جو شخص جھوٹ بولنے سے نہ شرماتا ہو وہ اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہوگا اور جو شخص اپنی گواہی میں متہم ہو اس کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ اس مسئلہ میں چاروں ائمہ کا اتفاق ہے۔ صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اگر کوئی شخص صحابہ، تابعین اور ائمہ مجتہدین کو برا بھلا کہتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ کیوں کہ ایسے شخص کا فاسق ہونا ظاہر ہے اور فاسق کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے اور اگر اُن کے بارے میں برائیوں کا اعتقاد تو رکھتا ہو مگر ان کو ظاہر نہیں کرتا تو یہ شخص عادل اور مقبول الشہادت ہے۔
Sahib al-Quduri said: The testimony of a person who performs contemptible and lowly acts is not accepted, such as urinating on the road, eating on the road, and eating publicly in the market, and according to Imam al-Karkhi, walking on the road wearing only a wrap or trousers. Because such a person abandons dignity (muruwwah) and humanity. And when he is not ashamed of such acts, he will not be ashamed of lying either. And a person who is not ashamed of lying will be suspected in his testimony. And a person who is suspected in his testimony, his testimony is not accepted. Therefore, his testimony will also not be accepted. On this issue, the four Imams are in agreement. Sahib al-Quduri said: If a person speaks ill of the Companions, the Followers, and the Mujtahid Imams, then his testimony is also not accepted. Because such a person's being a fasiq is evident, and the testimony of a fasiq is not accepted. However, if he holds bad beliefs about them but does not express them, then this person is upright (adl) and his testimony is accepted.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents two additional grounds for rejecting a witness's testimony, both derived from the works of Imam al-Quduri. First, a person who habitually engages in acts that violate common decency and dignity (muruwwah) — like urinating or eating publicly in the street, or walking in minimal clothing — is not accepted as a witness. The reasoning is that such shamelessness in minor matters indicates a lack of moral restraint, making it likely that the person would lie without shame. Since a witness who is suspected of dishonesty is not accepted, such a person's testimony is rejected. The author notes that all four Imams (Abu Hanifa, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree on this principle, indicating ijma. Second, a person who verbally insults or reviles the Companions, the Followers, or the great Mujtahid Imams is clearly a fasiq, and therefore his testimony is rejected. However, if a person merely holds corrupt beliefs about them in his heart without expressing them, he is still considered upright (adl) and his testimony is accepted, because the sin is in the outward manifestation, not the inner belief as long as it does not constitute kufr.

Key Terms
مروت (muruwwah): Dignity, decency, social propriety; the quality that prevents a person from engaging in shameful acts publicly.
خفیف و حقیر حرکات (khafif wa haqir harakat): Contemptible and lowly actions that are considered beneath a person's dignity, such as public urination or eating.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, thus losing moral integrity. In this context, publicly insulting the Companions makes one a fasiq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the testimony of a person who holds bad beliefs about the Companions but never expresses them?
A) His testimony is rejected because inner belief is fisq
B) His testimony is accepted because he is still considered upright (adl)
C) His testimony is accepted only if he repents
D) His testimony is rejected by the Hanafi school but accepted by others

Key Takeaway
A witness who lacks public dignity (muruwwah) or verbally insults the Companions is disqualified because such conduct indicates a propensity to lie and violates the requirement of 'adalah.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' and the Khattabiyyah Exception
Inter-madhhab dispute with analogy and exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa', explain the exception for the Khattabiyyah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the qiyas analogy.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from heretical sects—except the Khattabiyyah—because their religious devotion keeps them from lying.

This passage addresses a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the admissibility of testimony from people of heretical beliefs (Ahl al-Ahwa'). The Hanafi position is based on a careful distinction between belief-based fisq and action-based fisq, supported by a powerful analogy. Understanding this ruling requires you to follow the legal reasoning and identify the precise exception for the Khattabiyyah sect.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What is the Hanafi ruling on testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa'? What is the exception?
The exception is the Khattabiyyah sect.
2
Identify the opponent's view
Which school(s) disagree, and what is their general ruling?
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik reject all such testimony.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
What is the Hanafi evidence? How does the analogy with the wine-drinker and meat-eater work?
Focus on the concept of tadayyun (religious devotion) preventing lying.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i counter-proof
What is the Shafi'i argument that i'tiqadi fisq is worse than amali fisq?
This is a deducing from a greater evil to a lesser.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
How does this dispute affect real-world acceptance of testimony?
Hanafis accept from most heretics; Shafi'is reject all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوائے فرقہ خطابیہ کے اہل ہوا کی گواہی قابل قبول ہے وتقبل شهادة اهل الأهواء الا الخطابية وقال الشافعى لا تقبل لانه اغلظ وجوه الفسق ولنا انه فسق من حيث الاعتقاد وما اوقعه فيه الا تدينه فيمتنع عن الكذب وصار كمن يشرب المثلث او يأكل متروك التسمية عامدا مستبيحا لذلك بخلاف الفسق من حيث التعاطى اما الخطابية فهم قوم من غلاة الروافض يعتقدون الشهادة لكل من حلف عندهم وقيل يرون الشهادة لشيعتهم واجبة فتمكنت التهمة فى شهادة لظهور فسقهم
ترجمہ سوائے فرقہ خطابیہ کے اہل ہوا کی گواہی قبول ہوگی امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قبول نہیں کی جائے گی کیوں کہ یہ فسق کے طریقوں میں سے سب سے زیادہ سخت ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص اعتقاد کے اعتبار سے فاسق ہے اس کو اس ہوا میں کسی چیز نے نہیں ڈالا مگر اس کے تدین نے پس وہ کذب سے باز رہے گا اور یہ اس شخص کے مانند ہو گیا جو مباح سمجھ کر شربت مثلث پیتا ہے یا اُس ذبحہ کو کھاتا ہے جس پر عدا اللہ کا نام ترک کر دیا گیا ہو۔ برخلاف ایسے فسق کے جو اعمال میں ہو۔ رہا خطابیہ فرقہ تو وہ غالی رافضیوں کا ایک فرقہ ہے۔ جو ہر اُس شخص کی شہادت پر اعتقاد رکھتے ہیں جو ان کے سامنے قسم کھائے اور بعض نے کہا کہ وہ اپنے گروہ کیواسطے گواہی کو واجب سمجھتے ہیں پس ان کی شہادت میں تہمت متمکن ہوگئی کیونکہ ان کا فسق ظاہر ہے۔
تشریح اہل ہوا وہ لوگ ہیں جو خواہشات نفسانی کیمطابق اعتقاد رکھتے ہیں یعنی نفس کی مطابعت اور سنت کی مخالفت کرتے ہیں۔ اہل ہوا کے بنیادی چھ فرقے ہیں: جبریہ، قدریہ، مشبہ، معتزلہ، خوارج، روافض۔ پھر میں سے ہر ایک کے بارہ بارہ فرقے ہیں تو اس طرح اہل ہوا کے کل فرقے بہتر ہوں گے اور ایک فرقہ اہل حق کا ہوگا یعنی اہل سنت والجماعت ۔ ان تمام کے عقائد اور ان میں باہمی اختلاف علم کلام کی کتابوں میں بشرط وبسط کیساتھ مذکور ہے۔ خطابیہ کے بارے میں تین قول ہیں۔ پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ خطابیہ روافض کا ایک غالی فرقہ ہے جو ابو الخطاب محمد بن ابی وہب اجدع کی طرف منسوب ہے ابوالخطاب کوفہ میں رہتا تھا اس کا عقیدہ تھا کہ حضرت علی الہ اکبر (بڑا خدا) ہے اور جعفر بن محمد صادق الہ اصغر (چھوٹا خدا) ہے جب اس کو جعفر صادق کی خدمت میں پیش کیا گیا تو جعفر نے اسے دھتکارا اور دربار سے باہر نکال دیا پس اس نے اپنے الہ (خدا) ہونے کا دعوی کیا اور اس کے مریدوں نے کہا کہ جعفر خدا ہے اور ابو الخطاب بڑا خدا ہے ۔ عیسی بن موسیٰ بن علی بن عبد اللہ بن عباس نے اس کے ساتھ محاربہ اور جنگ کر کے اس کو قتل کر دیا پھر عیسی نے اس کو سولی دیکر ساری دنیا کے لئے عبرت کا سامان پیدا کر دیا۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ فرقہ خطابیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فرقہ خطابیہ میں سے کوئی شخص کسی پر کسی چیز کا دعوی کرے تو اس گروہ کے باقی لوگوں پر اس کے حق میں گواہی دینا واجب ہے۔ خواہ اس کا دعوی سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو۔ اور تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ خطابیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ جو اس کے سامنے قسم کھا جائے اس کے حق میں گواہی دینا درست سمجھتے ہیں ۔ اس تفصیل کے بعد صاحب قدوری کی عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک اہل ہوا کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی لیکن اہل ہوا میں سے فرقہ خطابیہ کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اہل ہوا اہل بدع میں سے کسی کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک ہیں۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل ہوا کے اعتقادات فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے ان میں اعتقادی فسق ہے اور اعتقادی فسق عملی فسق سے بدتر ہے لہذا جب اعمال کے اعتبار سے فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی تو من حیث الاعتقاد فاسق کی گواہی بدرجہ اولی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
Except for the Khattabiyyah sect, the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' is acceptable. And the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' is accepted except for the Khattabiyyah. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not accepted because it is the gravest form of fisq. Our evidence is that this fisq is in terms of belief, and nothing caused him to fall into it except his religious devotion (tadayyun), so he will refrain from lying. He becomes like one who drinks wine or eats meat upon which Allah's name was deliberately omitted, considering it permissible. This is different from fisq in terms of action. As for the Khattabiyyah, they are a group of the extreme Rawafid; they believe in testifying for everyone who swears before them, and it is said they consider testimony for their followers obligatory, so suspicion in testimony is established due to the manifestation of their fisq. Translation: Except for the Khattabiyyah sect, the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' will be accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It will not be accepted, because it is the harshest form of fisq. Our evidence is that this person is a fasiq in terms of belief, and nothing caused him to fall into it except his religious devotion; thus he will refrain from lying, and he becomes like the one who drinks wine or eats meat upon which Allah's name was omitted, considering it permissible. Unlike fisq that is in actions. As for the Khattabiyyah, they are a sect of the extreme Rawafid. They hold the belief of testifying for everyone who swears before them, and some said they consider it obligatory to testify for their party. Therefore, suspicion became established in their testimony because their fisq is apparent. Explanation: Ahl al-Ahwa' are those who hold beliefs according to their desires, i.e., they follow the self and oppose the Sunnah. The basic six sects of Ahl al-Ahwa' are: Jabriyyah, Qadariyyah, Mushabbihah, Mu'tazilah, Khawarij, Rawafid. Then each has twelve sub-sects, so total sects of Ahl al-Ahwa' are seventy-two, and one sect of Ahl al-Haq, namely Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. Their beliefs and mutual differences are mentioned in detail in the books of Kalam. There are three sayings about the Khattabiyyah. The first saying is that Khattabiyyah is a ghali sect of the Rawafid, attributed to Abu al-Khattab Muhammad ibn Abi Wahb al-Ajda'. Abu al-Khattab lived in Kufa. He believed that Imam Ali (may Allah honor him) is the greater god (al-ilah al-akbar) and Ja'far al-Sadiq is the lesser god (al-ilah al-asghar). When he was brought before Ja'far al-Sadiq, Ja'far rebuked him and expelled him from his court. Then he claimed to be the god, and his followers said that Ja'far is god and Abu al-Khattab is the greater god. Isa ibn Musa ibn Ali ibn Abdullah ibn Abbas fought and killed him, then crucified him, making him a lesson for the whole world. The second saying is that the Khattabiyyah believe that if anyone from their sect claims something against someone, it is obligatory for the rest of the group to testify in his favor, whether his claim is true or false. The third saying is that they consider it correct to testify for anyone who swears before them. After this detail, the gist of Sahib al-Quduri's statement is that according to the Hanafis, the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' will be accepted, but among Ahl al-Ahwa', the testimony of the Khattabiyyah will not be accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the testimony of none of the Ahl al-Ahwa' (people of innovation) will be accepted. Imam Malik is also of this view. Imam al-Shafi'i's evidence is that due to their corrupt beliefs, they have i'tiqadi fisq (belief-based fisq), and i'tiqadi fisq is worse than amali fisq (action-based fisq). Therefore, when the testimony of a fasiq in actions is not accepted, then the testimony of a fasiq in beliefs is even more deserving of rejection.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive treatment of the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' (people of heretical desires and innovations). The Hanafi position, based on the statements of al-Quduri and the reasoning of the school, is that the testimony of such individuals is generally accepted, with the sole exception of the Khattabiyyah sect. The reason is that Ahl al-Ahwa', despite their corrupt beliefs, are motivated by religious devotion (tadayyun), which makes them refrain from lying. They are likened to a person who drinks wine or eats meat without basmalah, believing it to be permissible — such a person is still considered upright in testimony because his sin is in his belief, not in deliberate dishonesty. This is contrasted with fisq in actions, which indicates moral laxity and likelihood of lying. However, the Khattabiyyah are excluded because their beliefs lead to partiality: they are known to testify for anyone who swears before them or for their own party, making them suspect in their testimony. The text then defines Ahl al-Ahwa' and outlines the six main sects and their 72 sub-sects. It also details three historical accounts of the Khattabiyyah, including their extreme deification of Ali and Ja'far al-Sadiq. Finally, it presents the Shafi'i (and Maliki) opposing view: that all Ahl al-Ahwa' are rejected due to the severity of belief-based fisq, which is worse than action-based fisq. The Hanafi response is not explicitly repeated in this section, but the earlier argument stands: their tadayyun prevents them from lying, unlike those with action-based fisq.

Key Terms
اہل ہوا (ahl al-ahwa'): People who follow their desires in matters of belief, opposing the Sunnah; includes various sects of innovation.
خطابیہ (khattabiyyah): An extreme Rafidi sect that deified Ali and Ja'far al-Sadiq, and is known for partiality in testimony.
تدین (tadayyun): Religious devotion; the quality that makes a person adhere to his beliefs and refrain from lying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa' accepted despite their heretical beliefs?
A) Because their beliefs are not considered fisq
B) Because their religious devotion prevents them from lying
C) Because they repent before testifying
D) Because the Hanafi school always accepts testimony regardless of character

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from Ahl al-Ahwa' except the Khattabiyyah, due to their belief-based fisq not impairing truthfulness, based on the analogy with a person who commits a sin out of mistaken belief.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Position on Testimony of Ahl al-Hawa
Ruling and dispute on testimony of Ahl al-Hawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on testimony of Ahl al-Hawa and explain the distinction between i'tiqadi and amali fisq.

Core Idea
Testimony of Ahl al-Hawa is accepted because their sin is in belief, not action, and they avoid lying out of devotion.

This lesson explores the Hanafi view that people of bid'ah (Ahl al-Hawa) are valid witnesses, provided their sin is only in i'tiqad. The Shafi'i school disagrees, arguing that i'tiqadi fisq is worse. We will examine the Hanafi proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and the ruling
Read the opening of the passage: Hanafis accept Ahl al-Hawa testimony except Khitabiyya. Note the exception.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Imam al-Shafi'i rejects all Ahl al-Hawa testimony, arguing i'tiqadi fisq is worse than amali fisq.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The text compares Ahl al-Hawa to someone who drinks thuluth wine or eats basmalah-omitted meat considering it permissible—both are acts of mistaken devotion, not deliberate disobedience. Hence they avoid lying.
4
Distinguish i'tiqadi vs amali fisq
I'tiqadi fisq stems from erroneous belief but not a character flaw; such a person will refrain from falsehood. Amali fisq involves knowingly committing haram, indicating potential for lying.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in a Hanafi court, testimony of Ahl al-Hawa is valid; in a Shafi'i court, it is rejected.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشهادة
اشرف البدایہ جلد وہم

التهمة فى شهادة لظهور فسقهم
ترجمہ سوائے فرقہ خطابیہ کے اہل ہوا کی گواہی قبول ہوگی امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قبول نہیں کی جائے گی کیوں کہ یہ فسق کے طریقوں میں سے سب سے زیادہ سخت ہے اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص اعتقاد کے اعتبار سے فاسق ہے اس کو اس ہوا میں کسی چیز نے نہیں ڈالا ۔ مگر اس کے تدین نے پس وہ کذب سے باز رہے گا اور یہ اس شخص کے مانند ہو گیا جو مباح سمجھ کر شربت مثلث پیتا ہے یا اُس ذبحہ کو کھاتا ہے جس پر عدا اللہ کا نام ترک کر دیا گیا ہو۔ برخلاف ایسے فسق کے جو اعمال میں ہو۔ رہا خطابیہ فرقہ تو وہ غالی رافضیوں کا ایک فرقہ ہے۔ جو ہر اُس شخص کی شہادت پر اعتقاد رکھتے ہیں جو ان کے سامنے قسم کھائے اور بعض نے کہا کہ وہ اپنے گروہ کیواسطے گواہی کو واجب سمجھتے ہیں پس ان کی شہادت میں تہمت متمکن ہوگئی کیونکہ ان کا فسق ظاہر ہے۔
تشریح اہل ہوا وہ لوگ ہیں جو خواہشات نفسانی کیمطابق اعتقاد کھتے ہیں یعنی نفس کی مطابعت اور سنت کی مخالفت کرتے ہیں۔ اہل ہوا کے بنیادی چھ ر ہیں

معطله
پھر میں سے ہر ایک کے بارہ بارہ فرقے ہیں تو اس طرح اہل ہوا کے کل فرقے بہتر ہوں گے اور ایک فرقہ اہل حق کا ہوگا یعنی اہل سنت والجماعت ۔ ان تمام کے عقائد اور ان میں باہمی اختلاف علم کلام کی کتابوں میں یوری شرط وبسط کیساتھ مذکور ہے۔ خطابیہ کے بارے میں تین قول ہیں۔ پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ خطابیہ روافض کا ایک عالی فرقہ ہے جو ابو الخطاب محمد بن ابی وہب اجدع کی طرف منسوب ہے ابوالخطاب کوفہ میں رہتا تھا اس کا عقیدہ تھا کہ حضرت علی الہ اکبر ( بڑا خدا) ہے اور جعفر بن محمد صادق الہ اصغر ( چھوٹا خدا) ہے جب اس کو جعفر صادق کی خدمت میں پیش کیا گیا تو جعفر نے اسے دھتکارا اور دربار سے باہر نکال دیا پس اس نے اپنے الہ ( خدا ) ہونے کا دعوی کیا اور اس کے مریدوں نے کہا کہ جعفر خدا ہے اور ابو الخطاب بڑا خدا ہے ۔ عیسی بن موسیٰ بن علی بن عبد اللہ بن عباس نے اس کے ساتھ محاربہ اور جنگ کر کے اس کو قتل کر دیا پھر عیسی نے اس کو سولی دیکر ساری دنیا کے لئے عبرت کا سامان پیدا کر دیا۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ فرقہ خطابیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فرقہ خطابیہ میں سے کوئی شخص کسی پر کسی چیز کا دعوی کرے تو اس گروہ کے باقی لوگوں پر اس کے حق میں گواہی دینا واجب ہے۔ خواہ اس کا دعوی سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو۔ اور تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ خطابیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ جو اس کے سامنے قسم کھا جائے اس کے حق میں گواہی
دینا درست سمجھتے ہیں ۔ اس تفصیل کے بعد صاحب قدوری کی عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک اہل ہوا کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی لیکن اہل ہوا میں سے فرقہ خطابیہ کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اہل ہوا اہل بدع میں سے کسی کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک ہیں۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل ہوا کے اعتقادات فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے ان میں اعتقادی فسق ہے اور اعتقادی فست عملی فسق سے بدتر ہے لہذا جب اعمال کے اعتبار سے فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی تو من حیث الاعتقاد فاسق کی گواہی بدرجہ اولی قبول نہ ہوگی۔

اشرف الہدایہ جلد۔ و ہم

كتاب الشهادة
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل ہوا کا فاسق ہونا صرف اعتقاد کے اعتبار سے ہے مگر اس کا یہ اعتقاد اس کو حق سمجھ کر ہے یعنی یہ شخص اپنے خیال میں اسی کو حق تصور کرتا ہے پس اس کے خیال کے مطابق ایس کا اپنا عقیدہ ترین اور دینداری ہے نہ کہ ترک تدین۔ اور جو ص متدین اور دیندار ہوتا ہے وہ جھوٹ بولنے سے اجتناب کرتا ہے لہذا اہل ہوا بھی جھوٹ بولنے سے اجتناب کریگا اور جو شخص جھوٹ بولنے سے اجتناب کرتا ہے چونکہ وہ جھوٹ بولنے کے ساتھ معتم نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے لہذا اہل ہوا کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ جیسے اگر کسی شخص نے شراب ، مثلث کو مباح سمجھ کر پی لیا یا کسی شافعی نے متروک التسمیہ عامدا کو مباح سمجھ کر کھالیا تو وہ مردود الشہادت نہ ہو گا۔ شراب، مثلث انگور کا وہ شیرہ ہے جس کو اس قدر پکایا جائے کہ دو تہائی جل کر ایک تہائی باقی رہ جائے مگر نشہ آور نہ ہوا ہو تو یہ امام محمد کے نزدیک حرام ہے اور شیخین کے نزدیک اس کا پینا حلال ہے اور اگر کسی جانور کو مسلمان نے ذبح کیا ۔ مگر عمد ابسم اللہ ترک کر دیا تو امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس کا کھانا حلال ہے پس حنفی کا شراب مثلث کو حلال سمجھ کر پینا اور شافعی کا متروک التسمیہ عامدا کو حلال سمجھ کر کھانا چوں کہ ترین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اہل ہوا کا اعتقادان کے گمان میں چونکہ صحیح اور درست ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے خیال میں ان کا عقیدہ بھی تدین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہ ہوگا اور جب ان کا اعتقاد تدین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہیں ہے تو ان کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اس کے بر خلاف عملی فستق کہ اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ عملی فسق کسی نا جائز اور حرام فعل کو مباح سمجھ کر نہیں کرتا بلکہ اس کو حرام سمجھ کر کرتا ہے لہذا جب وہ حرام فعل کا ارتکاب کر سکتا ہے تو جھوٹ کا ارتکاب بھی کر سکتا ہے اور جو شخص جھوٹ بولنے کے ساتھ متہم ہوتا ہے۔ چونکہ اس کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی اس لئے عملی فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی رہا فرقہ خطابیہ تو ان کی گواہی احناف کے نزدیک بھی قبول نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ قول اول کی بناء پر خطابیہ کے لوگ کافر ہیں اور کفار کی گواہی مسلمانوں کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا ان کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی اور دوسرے اور تیسرے قول کی بناء پر ان کی شہادت میں جھوٹ بولنے کا شبہ ہے اس طور پر کہ وہ اپنے گروہ کے لوگوں کے حق میں گواہی دینا واجب سمجھتے ہیں خواہ ان کے گروہ کے لوگوں کا دعوی سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو یا جو ان کے پاس قسم کھائے اس کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز سمجھتے ہیں خواہ وہ اپنی قسم میں جھوٹا ہو یا سچا ہو۔ بہر حال یہ لوگ اپنی شہادت میں متہم بالکذب ہیں اور متہم بالکذب کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا ان کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Bidayah, volume 10. - The accusation in testimony due to appearance of their sinfulness. Translation: Except for the Khitabiyya sect, the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa will be accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said that it will not be accepted because this is the harshest of the ways of sin. Our proof is that this person is a sinner in terms of belief; nothing put him into this whim except his religious devotion. So he will refrain from falsehood, and he becomes like a person who drinks thuluth wine considering it permissible, or eats the slaughtered animal whose name of Allah has been intentionally omitted. Contrary to sin that is in actions. As for the Khitabiyya sect, they are a sect of extremist Rafidis who believe in the testimony of everyone who swears in their presence, and some said they consider testifying for their group obligatory. So their testimony is tainted because their sin is apparent. Explanation: Ahl al-Hawa are people who hold beliefs according to their base desires, i.e., they follow their souls and oppose the Sunnah. The basic six of Ahl al-Hawa are: Jabriyya, Rafida, Mushabbiha, Qadariyya, Khawarij, Mu'attila. Then each has twelve sub-sects, so total sects of Ahl al-Hawa become seventy-two, and one sect is of Ahl al-Haqq, i.e., Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. All their beliefs and differences are mentioned in books of kalam in detail. About Khitabiyya, there are three statements. First statement: Khitabiyya is an extremist sub-sect of Rafida, attributed to Abu al-Khattab Muhammad bin Abi Wahb al-Ajda'. Abu al-Khattab lived in Kufa. His belief was that Ali is the greater god and Ja'far bin Muhammad al-Sadiq is the lesser god. When he was brought to Ja'far al-Sadiq, he rejected him and expelled him. So he claimed divinity, and his disciples said Ja'far is god and Abu al-Khattab is the greater god. Isa bin Musa bin Ali bin Abdullah bin Abbas fought and killed him, then crucified him, making a lesson for the whole world. Second statement: The belief of Khitabiyya is that if a person from Khitabiyya claims something, testifying in his favor is obligatory on the rest of the group, whether his claim is true or false. Third statement: The belief of Khitabiyya is that they consider it permissible to testify for anyone who swears in their presence. After this detail, the purport of the author of al-Quduri's text is that according to the Hanafis, the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa will be accepted, but from among Ahl al-Hawa, the testimony of the Khitabiyya sect will not be accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the testimony of none of Ahl al-Hawa and Ahl al-Bida' will be accepted. Imam Malik holds the same. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: Ahl al-Hawa, due to their corrupted beliefs, have i'tiqadi fisq, and i'tiqadi fisq is worse than amali fisq. So when the testimony of a fasiq in actions is not accepted, then a priori the testimony of one who is fasiq in belief will not be accepted. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume 10, page 249. Book of Testimony. Our proof: The sinfulness of Ahl al-Hawa is only in terms of belief, but this belief is held as a right, i.e., this person considers it true. So according to his thought, his own belief is his religion and devotion, not neglect of religion. And a person who is religious and devout avoids lying. So Ahl al-Hawa will also avoid lying. And a person who avoids lying, since he is not accused of lying, his testimony is accepted. So the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa will be accepted. Like if a person drank thuluth wine considering it permissible, or a Shafi'i ate intentionally omitted basmalah animal considering it permissible, he will not be rejected in testimony. Thuluth wine is grape juice cooked until two-thirds evaporates and one-third remains, but not intoxicating. According to Imam Muhammad, it is haram, but according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) it is halal. And if a Muslim slaughtered an animal but intentionally omitted basmalah, according to Imam al-Shafi'i eating it is halal. So a Hanafi drinking thuluth wine considering it halal, and a Shafi'i eating meat with omitted basmalah considering it halal, since this is not against religion and devotion, their testimony is accepted. Similarly, Ahl al-Hawa's belief, since in their estimation it is correct and right, is not against devotion in their view, so their testimony is accepted. In contrast, amali fisq: his testimony will not be accepted because he does not commit a prohibited act considering it permissible, but he commits it knowing it is haram. So if he can commit a haram act, he can also commit falsehood. And a person accused of lying, his testimony is not accepted. So the testimony of a fasiq in actions will not be accepted. As for the Khitabiyya sect, their testimony will not be accepted even according to the Hanafis. Because based on the first statement, the Khitabiyya are disbelievers, and the testimony of disbelievers against Muslims is not accepted, so their testimony will not be accepted. Based on the second and third statements, there is suspicion of lying in their testimony: they consider testifying for their group members obligatory whether the claim is true or false, or they consider it permissible to testify for anyone who swears, whether truthfully or falsely. In any case, these people are accused of falsehood in their testimony, and the testimony of one accused of falsehood is not accepted, so their testimony will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the acceptance of testimony from Ahl al-Hawa (people of whims, followers of bid'ah). The Hanafi position, as stated by the author following al-Quduri, is that the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa is accepted, except for the Khitabiyya sect. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik reject all their testimony on the grounds that their i'tiqadi fisq (sinfulness in belief) is more severe than amali fisq (sinfulness in action). The Hanafis respond with an analogy: a person who commits a sin due to mistaken ijtihad (like drinking thuluth wine considering it halal) is not rejected as a witness because his action stems from religious devotion, not disregard for religion. Similarly, Ahl al-Hawa hold their beliefs out of misguided devotion, not a desire to lie; thus they will avoid falsehood. The text then details the sects of Ahl al-Hawa and provides three views on the Khitabiyya: (1) they are extreme Rafidis who consider Ali and Ja'far al-Sadiq as deities, making them kafir; (2) they consider testifying for their group obligatory regardless of truth; (3) they accept anyone who swears. Under all views, their testimony is rejected: under the first because they are kafir, under the second and third because they are accused of lying. The commentary emphasizes that Hanafis distinguish between i'tiqadi and amali fisq: i'tiqadi fisq does not automatically disqualify a witness if the person acts from religious conviction, while amali fisq involves knowingly committing haram and thus indicates a willingness to lie.

Key Terms
أهل الهوى (Ahl al-Hawa): People who follow their base desires in matters of belief, opposing the Sunnah; essentially the people of bid'ah and erroneous sects.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness or transgression. In this text, it is divided into i'tiqadi fisq (in belief) and amali fisq (in actions).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa accepted?
A) Because they are not sinful.
B) Because their sin is in i'tiqad and they avoid lying due to devotion.
C) Because the Shafi'i school agrees.
D) Because they repented.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis accept Ahl al-Hawa testimony because i'tiqadi fisq does not inherently make one a liar.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

The Khitabiyya Exception: Why Their Testimony is Rejected
Detailed explanation of Khitabiyya exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three views on the Khitabiyya sect and explain why their testimony is rejected in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Khitabiyya testimony is rejected either due to their kufr or their belief in obligatory false testimony.

The Hanafi school makes an exception for the Khitabiyya from the general acceptance of Ahl al-Hawa testimony. This lesson explores the three explanations for why their testimony is tainted, ranging from outright disbelief to a systematic disregard for truth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
The text states that among Ahl al-Hawa, only the Khitabiyya are excluded from valid testimony.
2
Review the three views on Khitabiyya
First view: they are extreme Rafidis who consider Ali and Ja'far al-Sadiq as gods (kufr). Second view: they consider testifying for their group obligatory even if false. Third view: they accept anyone who swears, true or false.
3
Determine the consequence for testimony
Under each view, their testimony fails: kufr makes them non-Muslim (testimony not accepted), obligatory false testimony makes them accused of lying, and accepting any swearer also makes them accused.
4
Connect to the general rule
The Khitabiyya are not covered by the Hanafi principle of accepting Ahl al-Hawa because they are either kuffar or blatantly untrustworthy.
5
Contrast with other Ahl al-Hawa
Other sects only have i'tiqadi fisq and avoid lying due to devotion; Khitabiyya go beyond that.
