پھر میں سے ہر ایک کے بارہ بارہ فرقے ہیں تو اس طرح اہل ہوا کے کل فرقے بہتر ہوں گے اور ایک فرقہ اہل حق کا ہوگا یعنی اہل سنت والجماعت ۔ ان تمام کے عقائد اور ان میں باہمی اختلاف علم کلام کی کتابوں میں یوری شرط وبسط کیساتھ مذکور ہے۔ خطابیہ کے بارے میں تین قول ہیں۔ پہلا قول یہ ہے کہ خطابیہ روافض کا ایک عالی فرقہ ہے جو ابو الخطاب محمد بن ابی وہب اجدع کی طرف منسوب ہے ابوالخطاب کوفہ میں رہتا تھا اس کا عقیدہ تھا کہ حضرت علی الہ اکبر ( بڑا خدا) ہے اور جعفر بن محمد صادق الہ اصغر ( چھوٹا خدا) ہے جب اس کو جعفر صادق کی خدمت میں پیش کیا گیا تو جعفر نے اسے دھتکارا اور دربار سے باہر نکال دیا پس اس نے اپنے الہ ( خدا ) ہونے کا دعوی کیا اور اس کے مریدوں نے کہا کہ جعفر خدا ہے اور ابو الخطاب بڑا خدا ہے ۔ عیسی بن موسیٰ بن علی بن عبد اللہ بن عباس نے اس کے ساتھ محاربہ اور جنگ کر کے اس کو قتل کر دیا پھر عیسی نے اس کو سولی دیکر ساری دنیا کے لئے عبرت کا سامان پیدا کر دیا۔ دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ فرقہ خطابیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فرقہ خطابیہ میں سے کوئی شخص کسی پر کسی چیز کا دعوی کرے تو اس گروہ کے باقی لوگوں پر اس کے حق میں گواہی دینا واجب ہے۔ خواہ اس کا دعوی سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو۔ اور تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ خطابیہ کا عقیدہ یہ ہے کہ جو اس کے سامنے قسم کھا جائے اس کے حق میں گواہی
دینا درست سمجھتے ہیں ۔ اس تفصیل کے بعد صاحب قدوری کی عبارت کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ احناف کے نزدیک اہل ہوا کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی لیکن اہل ہوا میں سے فرقہ خطابیہ کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ اہل ہوا اہل بدع میں سے کسی کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اسی کے قائل امام مالک ہیں۔
امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل ہوا کے اعتقادات فاسد ہونے کی وجہ سے ان میں اعتقادی فسق ہے اور اعتقادی فست عملی فسق سے بدتر ہے لہذا جب اعمال کے اعتبار سے فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہوتی تو من حیث الاعتقاد فاسق کی گواہی بدرجہ اولی قبول نہ ہوگی۔

اشرف الہدایہ جلد۔ و ہم

كتاب الشهادة
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اہل ہوا کا فاسق ہونا صرف اعتقاد کے اعتبار سے ہے مگر اس کا یہ اعتقاد اس کو حق سمجھ کر ہے یعنی یہ شخص اپنے خیال میں اسی کو حق تصور کرتا ہے پس اس کے خیال کے مطابق ایس کا اپنا عقیدہ ترین اور دینداری ہے نہ کہ ترک تدین۔ اور جو ص متدین اور دیندار ہوتا ہے وہ جھوٹ بولنے سے اجتناب کرتا ہے لہذا اہل ہوا بھی جھوٹ بولنے سے اجتناب کریگا اور جو شخص جھوٹ بولنے سے اجتناب کرتا ہے چونکہ وہ جھوٹ بولنے کے ساتھ معتم نہیں ہوتا اس لئے اس کی گواہی قبول کی جاتی ہے لہذا اہل ہوا کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ جیسے اگر کسی شخص نے شراب ، مثلث کو مباح سمجھ کر پی لیا یا کسی شافعی نے متروک التسمیہ عامدا کو مباح سمجھ کر کھالیا تو وہ مردود الشہادت نہ ہو گا۔ شراب، مثلث انگور کا وہ شیرہ ہے جس کو اس قدر پکایا جائے کہ دو تہائی جل کر ایک تہائی باقی رہ جائے مگر نشہ آور نہ ہوا ہو تو یہ امام محمد کے نزدیک حرام ہے اور شیخین کے نزدیک اس کا پینا حلال ہے اور اگر کسی جانور کو مسلمان نے ذبح کیا ۔ مگر عمد ابسم اللہ ترک کر دیا تو امام شافعی کے نزدیک اس کا کھانا حلال ہے پس حنفی کا شراب مثلث کو حلال سمجھ کر پینا اور شافعی کا متروک التسمیہ عامدا کو حلال سمجھ کر کھانا چوں کہ ترین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اہل ہوا کا اعتقادان کے گمان میں چونکہ صحیح اور درست ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے خیال میں ان کا عقیدہ بھی تدین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہ ہوگا اور جب ان کا اعتقاد تدین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہیں ہے تو ان کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اس کے بر خلاف عملی فستق کہ اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ عملی فسق کسی نا جائز اور حرام فعل کو مباح سمجھ کر نہیں کرتا بلکہ اس کو حرام سمجھ کر کرتا ہے لہذا جب وہ حرام فعل کا ارتکاب کر سکتا ہے تو جھوٹ کا ارتکاب بھی کر سکتا ہے اور جو شخص جھوٹ بولنے کے ساتھ متہم ہوتا ہے۔ چونکہ اس کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی اس لئے عملی فاسق کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی رہا فرقہ خطابیہ تو ان کی گواہی احناف کے نزدیک بھی قبول نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ قول اول کی بناء پر خطابیہ کے لوگ کافر ہیں اور کفار کی گواہی مسلمانوں کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا ان کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی اور دوسرے اور تیسرے قول کی بناء پر ان کی شہادت میں جھوٹ بولنے کا شبہ ہے اس طور پر کہ وہ اپنے گروہ کے لوگوں کے حق میں گواہی دینا واجب سمجھتے ہیں خواہ ان کے گروہ کے لوگوں کا دعوی سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو یا جو ان کے پاس قسم کھائے اس کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز سمجھتے ہیں خواہ وہ اپنی قسم میں جھوٹا ہو یا سچا ہو۔ بہر حال یہ لوگ اپنی شہادت میں متہم بالکذب ہیں اور متہم بالکذب کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا ان کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Bidayah, volume 10. - The accusation in testimony due to appearance of their sinfulness. Translation: Except for the Khitabiyya sect, the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa will be accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said that it will not be accepted because this is the harshest of the ways of sin. Our proof is that this person is a sinner in terms of belief; nothing put him into this whim except his religious devotion. So he will refrain from falsehood, and he becomes like a person who drinks thuluth wine considering it permissible, or eats the slaughtered animal whose name of Allah has been intentionally omitted. Contrary to sin that is in actions. As for the Khitabiyya sect, they are a sect of extremist Rafidis who believe in the testimony of everyone who swears in their presence, and some said they consider testifying for their group obligatory. So their testimony is tainted because their sin is apparent. Explanation: Ahl al-Hawa are people who hold beliefs according to their base desires, i.e., they follow their souls and oppose the Sunnah. The basic six of Ahl al-Hawa are: Jabriyya, Rafida, Mushabbiha, Qadariyya, Khawarij, Mu'attila. Then each has twelve sub-sects, so total sects of Ahl al-Hawa become seventy-two, and one sect is of Ahl al-Haqq, i.e., Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. All their beliefs and differences are mentioned in books of kalam in detail. About Khitabiyya, there are three statements. First statement: Khitabiyya is an extremist sub-sect of Rafida, attributed to Abu al-Khattab Muhammad bin Abi Wahb al-Ajda'. Abu al-Khattab lived in Kufa. His belief was that Ali is the greater god and Ja'far bin Muhammad al-Sadiq is the lesser god. When he was brought to Ja'far al-Sadiq, he rejected him and expelled him. So he claimed divinity, and his disciples said Ja'far is god and Abu al-Khattab is the greater god. Isa bin Musa bin Ali bin Abdullah bin Abbas fought and killed him, then crucified him, making a lesson for the whole world. Second statement: The belief of Khitabiyya is that if a person from Khitabiyya claims something, testifying in his favor is obligatory on the rest of the group, whether his claim is true or false. Third statement: The belief of Khitabiyya is that they consider it permissible to testify for anyone who swears in their presence. After this detail, the purport of the author of al-Quduri's text is that according to the Hanafis, the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa will be accepted, but from among Ahl al-Hawa, the testimony of the Khitabiyya sect will not be accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i said that the testimony of none of Ahl al-Hawa and Ahl al-Bida' will be accepted. Imam Malik holds the same. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: Ahl al-Hawa, due to their corrupted beliefs, have i'tiqadi fisq, and i'tiqadi fisq is worse than amali fisq. So when the testimony of a fasiq in actions is not accepted, then a priori the testimony of one who is fasiq in belief will not be accepted. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume 10, page 249. Book of Testimony. Our proof: The sinfulness of Ahl al-Hawa is only in terms of belief, but this belief is held as a right, i.e., this person considers it true. So according to his thought, his own belief is his religion and devotion, not neglect of religion. And a person who is religious and devout avoids lying. So Ahl al-Hawa will also avoid lying. And a person who avoids lying, since he is not accused of lying, his testimony is accepted. So the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa will be accepted. Like if a person drank thuluth wine considering it permissible, or a Shafi'i ate intentionally omitted basmalah animal considering it permissible, he will not be rejected in testimony. Thuluth wine is grape juice cooked until two-thirds evaporates and one-third remains, but not intoxicating. According to Imam Muhammad, it is haram, but according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) it is halal. And if a Muslim slaughtered an animal but intentionally omitted basmalah, according to Imam al-Shafi'i eating it is halal. So a Hanafi drinking thuluth wine considering it halal, and a Shafi'i eating meat with omitted basmalah considering it halal, since this is not against religion and devotion, their testimony is accepted. Similarly, Ahl al-Hawa's belief, since in their estimation it is correct and right, is not against devotion in their view, so their testimony is accepted. In contrast, amali fisq: his testimony will not be accepted because he does not commit a prohibited act considering it permissible, but he commits it knowing it is haram. So if he can commit a haram act, he can also commit falsehood. And a person accused of lying, his testimony is not accepted. So the testimony of a fasiq in actions will not be accepted. As for the Khitabiyya sect, their testimony will not be accepted even according to the Hanafis. Because based on the first statement, the Khitabiyya are disbelievers, and the testimony of disbelievers against Muslims is not accepted, so their testimony will not be accepted. Based on the second and third statements, there is suspicion of lying in their testimony: they consider testifying for their group members obligatory whether the claim is true or false, or they consider it permissible to testify for anyone who swears, whether truthfully or falsely. In any case, these people are accused of falsehood in their testimony, and the testimony of one accused of falsehood is not accepted, so their testimony will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the acceptance of testimony from Ahl al-Hawa (people of whims, followers of bid'ah). The Hanafi position, as stated by the author following al-Quduri, is that the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa is accepted, except for the Khitabiyya sect. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik reject all their testimony on the grounds that their i'tiqadi fisq (sinfulness in belief) is more severe than amali fisq (sinfulness in action). The Hanafis respond with an analogy: a person who commits a sin due to mistaken ijtihad (like drinking thuluth wine considering it halal) is not rejected as a witness because his action stems from religious devotion, not disregard for religion. Similarly, Ahl al-Hawa hold their beliefs out of misguided devotion, not a desire to lie; thus they will avoid falsehood. The text then details the sects of Ahl al-Hawa and provides three views on the Khitabiyya: (1) they are extreme Rafidis who consider Ali and Ja'far al-Sadiq as deities, making them kafir; (2) they consider testifying for their group obligatory regardless of truth; (3) they accept anyone who swears. Under all views, their testimony is rejected: under the first because they are kafir, under the second and third because they are accused of lying. The commentary emphasizes that Hanafis distinguish between i'tiqadi and amali fisq: i'tiqadi fisq does not automatically disqualify a witness if the person acts from religious conviction, while amali fisq involves knowingly committing haram and thus indicates a willingness to lie.

Key Terms
خطابية (Khitabiyya): An extremist Rafidi sect attributed to Abu al-Khattab, who held deification of Ali and Ja'far al-Sadiq. They are considered disbelievers or at least severely unreliable witnesses.
تہمت (tuhmah): Accusation or suspicion. In legal context, being accused of falsehood disqualifies a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a reason given for rejecting Khitabiyya testimony?
A) They consider Ali and Ja'far as gods.
B) They consider testimony obligatory for group members.
C) They only testify if the claimant swears.
D) They are known to be liars in all matters.

Key Takeaway
The Khitabiyya are excluded from the general acceptance due to extreme kufr or systematic falsehood.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Dhimmis Against Each Other
States Hanafi acceptance of dhimmi testimony against each other and refutes Shafi'i/Maliki

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dhimmi testimony against each other, contrast it with Shafi'i/Maliki views, and apply the distinctions (wilayah, spite) to determine admissibility.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's testimony is valid against another dhimmi due to wilayah and no spite, but not against Muslims.

This passage centers on a key inter-madhhab dispute: can a non-Muslim subject (dhimmi) testify against another dhimmi? The Hanafi school accepts it, even across different religions, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools reject it altogether. The Hanafis rely on a Prophetic hadith and a rational argument based on wilayah (guardianship) and the absence of spite among dhimmis. This lesson unpacks the proofs and limits of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the act (testimony of dhimmi against dhimmi) and its ruling: it is accepted (mubah to accept the testimony). Note that it applies even if the dhimmis differ in religion.
The source uses 'wa in ikhtalafat milaluhum' – even if their religions differ.
2
Identify the opponent's proof
Malik and al-Shafi'i argue that dhimmis are fasiq (sinners) by Quranic verse, so their testimony is unreliable, analogous to an apostate. They also note that dhimmi testimony against Muslims is rejected, so why accept it against each other?
Opposing dalil: Quran 'wa al-kafirun hum al-fasiqun'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis counter with two proofs: (a) a hadith where the Prophet allowed Christian testimony against each other; (b) rational argument: a dhimmi has wilayah over himself and his children, thus he is qualified to testify for his kind. Moreover, their kufr is i'tiqadi (belief-based) and they avoid what they believe is haram, including lying, which is prohibited in all religions.
The distinction with an apostate: the apostate has no wilayah. The distinction with testimony against a Muslim: no wilayah and potential spite.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafi courts accept dhimmi testimony against each other; Shafi'i/Maliki courts do not. This affects procedural justice for non-Muslim subjects.
This is the practical consequence of the ijtihad difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذمی کی ذمی کے حق میں گواہی معتبر ہے، اقوال فقہاء
قال و تقبل شهادة اهل الذمة بعضهم على بعض وان اختلفت مللهم و قال مالك والشافعي لا تقبل لانه فاسق قال الله تعالى والكافرون هم الفاسقون فيجب التوقف فى خبره ولهذا لا تقبل شهادته على المسلم فصار كالمرتد ولنا ان النبى عليه السلام اجاز شهادة النصارى بعضهم على بعض ولانه من اهل الولاية على نفسه وعلى اولاده الصغار فيكون من اهل الشهادة على جنسه و الفسق من حيث الاعتقاد غير مانع لانه يجتنب ما يعتقده محرم دينه والكذب محظور الاديان كلها بخلاف المرتد لانه لا ولاية له وبخلاف شهادة الذمى على المسلم لانه لا ولاية له بالاضافة اليه ولانه يتقول عليه لانه يغيظه قهره اياه وملل كفر وان اختلات فلا قهــر فـلا يــحــمــلهــم الــغـيـط عــلــى التـقــول
The testimony of a dhimmi in favor of a dhimmi is valid; statements of the jurists. He said: The testimony of Ahl al-Dhimmah is accepted, some of them against others, even if their religions differ. And Malik and al-Shafi'i said it is not accepted because he is a sinner. Allah said: 'And the disbelievers are the sinners.' So it is necessary to suspend judgment about his report. For this reason, his testimony is not accepted against a Muslim, so he becomes like an apostate. Our evidence: The Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the testimony of Christians against each other. And because he is a person of guardianship over himself and his young children, so he is eligible to testify about his species. And sin in terms of belief is not an obstacle because he avoids what he believes is forbidden in his religion, and lying is prohibited in all religions. Unlike an apostate because he has no guardianship. And unlike the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim because he has no guardianship with respect to him, and because he would fabricate against him, since his subjugation angers him. But the religions of disbelief, even if they differ, there is no subjugation, so anger does not drive them to fabrication.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the testimony of dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state) against each other. The Hanafi position is clear: the testimony of dhimmis is accepted against each other, even if they belong to different religions (e.g., Christian vs. Jew). Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i reject it on the grounds that dhimmis are disbelievers and thus fasiq (sinful) as per the Quranic verse 'And the disbelievers are the sinners.' They argue that since such a person's report is unreliable, his testimony is not accepted, similar to an apostate. The Hanafis respond with two proofs: First, a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) accepted the testimony of Christians against each other. Second, a rational argument: a dhimmi has wilayah (guardianship) over himself and his minor children, so he is qualified to testify about his own kind. Their kufr is a sin of belief, but they avoid what they believe is forbidden in their religion, and lying is prohibited in all religions, so they will not lie against their own kind. The text distinguishes two exceptions: (1) an apostate cannot testify even against his own kind because he has no wilayah; (2) a dhimmi cannot testify against a Muslim because he has no wilayah over Muslims and may be motivated by spite due to being subjugated. However, between dhimmis of different religions, there is no such subjugation or spite, so their testimony is accepted. The commentary highlights the Hanafi reliance on both naql (hadith) and aql (analogy of wilayah and avoidance of lying) and the precise limits of the ruling.

Key Terms
أهل الذمة (Ahl al-Dhimmah): Non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state who pay jizya and are protected.
ولاية (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship over oneself and dependents, which qualifies a person to testify for his kind.
تقول (taqawwul): Fabrication or false testimony, specifically motivated by spite or enmity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis accept the testimony of a dhimmi against another dhimmi but not against a Muslim?
A) Because dhimmis are reliable among themselves but biased against Muslims.
B) Because a dhimmi has wilayah over himself and his children, but no wilayah over Muslims, and may lie out of spite against Muslims.
C) Because the Quran prohibits accepting dhimmi testimony against Muslims.
D) Because dhimmis are considered fasiq only against Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts dhimmi testimony against each other based on wilayah and absence of spite, distinguishing it from apostates and from testimony against Muslims.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Testimony of Ahl al-Hawa: Accepted Due to Sincere Belief
Hanafi argument for accepting testimony of Ahl al-Hawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa and explain the rational proof that distinguishes them from practical sinners.

Core Idea
A person who sincerely believes his view is correct is not a liar, so his testimony is accepted.

In Hanafi fiqh, not all sinners are treated equally when it comes to testimony. While a practical sinner's word is rejected, a person with deviant beliefs (Ahl al-Hawa) may still be a valid witness—provided he is not accused of lying. This lesson unpacks the rational proof behind this ruling and clarifies how it applies to intra-madhhab differences and extreme sects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
Determine the ruling: testimony of Ahl al-Hawa is accepted unless they are proven liars. Note the distinction made between theoretical sin (belief) and practical sin (action).
The ruling is based on the principle that sincerity in belief leads to truthfulness.
2
Understand the rational proof (dalil aqli)
Trace the logic: Ahl al-Hawa believe their view is correct and thus consider themselves pious. Piety requires avoiding lying, so they are not accused of lying. Hence their testimony is accepted.
The proof hinges on the assumption that a person who thinks he is acting righteously will avoid sin, including lying.
3
Compare with practical sinners
Contrast: a practical sinner knowingly commits haram, so he is prone to lie. His testimony is rejected. The Khitabiyya sect is even worse—they may be kafir or systematic liars.
This distinction explains why testimony of a Hanafi drinking thuluth or a Shafi'i eating meat without basmala is accepted: they act on their madhhab.
4
Apply to analogous cases
Consider examples from the text: a Hanafi following Shaykhayn on thuluth, or a Shafi'i following his school on basmala omission. Their testimony is accepted, just like Ahl al-Hawa.
This shows the ruling is not limited to belief innovators but extends to anyone acting on sincere ijtihad.

شافعی کا متروک التسمیہ عامدا کو حلال سمجھ کر کھانا چوں کہ ترین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہیں ہے اس لئے ان کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح اہل ہوا کا اعتقادان کے گمان میں چونکہ صحیح اور درست ہے۔ اس لئے ان کے خیال میں ان کا عقیدہ بھی تدین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہ ہوگا اور جب ان کا عقیدہ تدین اور دینداری کے خلاف نہیں ہے تو ان کی گواہی بھی قبول کی جائے گی ۔ اس کے بر خلاف عملی فستق کہ اس کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کے حق میں گواہی دینا واجب سمجھتے ہیں خواہ ان کے گروہ کے لوگوں کا دعوی سچا ہو یا جھوٹا ہو یا جو ان کے پاس قسم کھائے اس کے لئے گواہی دینا جائز سمجھتے ہیں خواہ وہ اپنی قسم میں جھوٹا ہو یا سچا ہو۔ بہر حال یہ لوگ اپنی شہادت میں متہم بالکذب ہیں اور متہم بالکذب کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی لہذا ان کی گواہی بھی قبول نہ ہوگی ۔
Our proof is that the fasiq nature of Ahl al-Hawa is only with respect to belief, but this belief of his is based on considering it true, i.e., this person in his own view considers that [belief] as the truth. So according to his view, his own belief is piety and religiosity, not abandonment of religion. And one who is pious and religious refrains from lying; therefore Ahl al-Hawa will also refrain from lying. And since a person who refrains from lying is not accused of lying, his testimony is accepted. Therefore, the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa should also be accepted. For example, if a person drinks thuluth (a type of wine) considering it permissible, or a Shafi'i eats meat from an animal on which the basmala was deliberately omitted, considering it permissible, then he will not be rejected as a witness. Thuluth wine is grape juice boiled until two-thirds evaporates and one-third remains, but it is not intoxicating. According to Imam Muhammad it is forbidden, but according to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) it is permissible to drink. And if a Muslim slaughters an animal but deliberately omits the basmala, then according to Imam al-Shafi'i it is permissible to eat. So since a Hanafi drinking thuluth wine considering it permissible, and a Shafi'i eating meat without basmala considering it permissible, are not contrary to piety and religiosity, their testimony is accepted. Similarly, Ahl al-Hawa's belief, in their estimation, is correct and valid; therefore in their view their belief is not contrary to piety and religiosity, and since their belief is not contrary to piety and religiosity, their testimony will also be accepted. Conversely, a practical sinner's testimony will not be accepted because a practical sinner does not commit an impermissible act considering it permissible, but rather commits it knowing it is forbidden. Therefore, when he can commit a forbidden act, he can also commit lying. And a person who is accused of lying, since his testimony is not accepted, the testimony of a practical sinner will not be accepted. As for the Khitabiyya sect, their testimony is not accepted even according to the Hanafis, because based on the first opinion, the people of Khitabiyya are disbelievers, and the testimony of disbelievers is not accepted against Muslims, thus their testimony is not accepted. And based on the second and third opinions, there is suspicion of lying in their testimony, in that they consider it obligatory to testify in favor of people of their group, whether the claim of their group's people is true or false, or they consider it permissible to testify for one who takes an oath before them, whether he is lying or truthful in his oath. In any case, these people are accused of lying in their testimony, and the testimony of one accused of lying is not accepted, so their testimony is not accepted.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi ruling with proof (dalil aqli) regarding the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa (people of heretical desires/innovations). The Hanafi position is that their testimony is accepted, contrary to practical sinners and the Khitabiyya sect. The reasoning: Ahl al-Hawa are fasiq (sinner) only in belief, not in action; they believe their view is correct and thus are pious in intention. Since piety necessitates avoiding lying, they are not accused of lying, so their testimony is accepted. The text provides examples: a Hanafi drinking thuluth wine (permissible in the view of the Shaykhayn) or a Shafi'i eating meat without basmala (permissible in their madhhab) are not considered sinners in practice, so their testimony is accepted. In contrast, a practical sinner (fasiq bi'l-fi'l) knowingly commits haram, so he is prone to lie; his testimony is rejected. The Khitabiyya sect is treated separately: according to one opinion they are kafir (testimony rejected), and according to others they are suspected of lying because they believe in testifying for their group regardless of truth. Thus, their testimony is also rejected. The key distinction: Ahl al-Hawa are not accused of lying because they believe their position is religiously correct, so they are like any Muslim who follows his madhhab.

Key Terms
اہل ہوا (Ahl al-Hawa): People who follow heretical desires/innovations (bid'ah) in matters of belief, but act according to their sincere conviction.
عملی فسق (Amali Fiqh (actually 'Amali Fiqh' is a typo; should be 'Amali Fisaq' or 'عملی فسق')): Practical sinning: committing forbidden acts while knowing they are forbidden.
شراب مثلث (Sharab al-Thuluth): Wine made from grapes boiled to reduce by two-thirds, leaving one-third; not intoxicating according to some.
خطابیہ (Khitabiyya): A sect that believes it is obligatory or permissible to lie to protect their group, and thus their testimony is rejected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of Ahl al-Hawa (people of desires) accepted according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they are considered Muslims regardless of their beliefs.
B) Because they refrain from lying due to their sincere belief that their actions are pious.
C) Because their testimony is needed more than that of practical sinners.
D) Because they have taqwa (piety) that overcomes their sinful beliefs.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony of Ahl al-Hawa because their sincerity in belief prevents them from lying, unlike practical sinners.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Dhimmis Against Each Other is Accepted
Hanafi position accepting Dhimmi testimony inter se, with disputes from Malik, Shafi'i, and Ibn Abi Layla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dhimmi testimony against each other, explain the proofs, and distinguish it from the positions of Malik, Shafi'i, and Ibn Abi Layla.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's testimony against another dhimmi is accepted because he has wilayah and lying is forbidden in all religions.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute over whether non-Muslim citizens (dhimmis) can testify against each other. While Malik and Shafi'i reject it outright, and Ibn Abi Layla restricts it to same religion, the Hanafi school adopts a broader acceptance. Understanding the reasoning reveals how Hanafi usul differentiates between sins of belief and practical sins, and how the concept of wilayah (guardianship) underlies witness capacity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State precisely what the Hanafi school accepts: testimony of dhimmis against each other, even if their religions differ.
This is the core ruling from al-Quduri and al-Hidayah.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the two proofs: the hadith of the Prophet permitting Christian testimony, and the reasoning based on wilayah (guardianship) over self and minor children.
Wilayah is a prerequisite for testimony in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Contrast with opposing proofs
Understand the Maliki/Shafi'i argument from the Qur'anic verse that disbelievers are fasiq, and the analogy to apostates. Then see the Hanafi response distinguishing fisq i'tiqadi from fisq amali.
The Hanafi response argues that fisq in belief does not necessarily lead to lying.
4
Understand the practical difference
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf: how this dispute affects court proceedings in each school.
In Hanafi courts, dhimmi testimony is accepted; in Maliki/Shafi'i courts, it is not, causing practical difficulties.

ذمی کی ذمی کے حق میں گواہی معتبر ہے، اقوال فقہاء
قال و تقبل شهادة اهل الذمة بعضهم على بعض وان اختلفت مللهم و قال مالك والشافعي لا تقبل لانه فاسق قال الله تعالى والكافرون هم الفاسقون فيجب التوقف فى خبره ولهذا لا تقبل شهادته على المسلم فصار كالمرتد ولنا ان النبى عليه السلام اجاز شهادة النصارى بعضهم على بعض ولانه من اهل الولاية على نفسه وعلى اولاده الصغار فيكون من اهل الشهادة على جنسه و الفسق من حيث الاعتقاد غير مانع لانه يجتنب ما يعتقده محرم دينه والكذب محظور الاديان كلها بخلاف المرتد لانه لا ولاية له وبخلاف شهادة الذمى على المسلم لانه لا ولاية له بالاضافة اليه ولانه يتقول عليه لانه يغيظه قهره اياه وملل كفر وان اختلات فلا قهــر فـلا يــحــمــلهــم الــغـيـط عــلــى التـقــول
ترجمہ اور ذمیوں کی گواہی آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے خلاف قبول کی جائے گی اگر چہ ان کے ادیان جدا جدا ہوں اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ذمیوں کی باہم گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ وہ فاسق ہیں اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا کہ کافر ہی فاسق ہے۔ پس اس کی خبر میں توقف کرنا واجب ہے اسی وجہ سے اس کی شہادت مسلمانوں کے خلاف قبول نہ ہو گی۔ لہذا وہ مرتد کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے نصرانیوں کی گواہی ایک کی دوسرے کے خلاف جائز قرار دی ہے اور اس لئے کہ ذمی اپنی ذلت پر اور اپنی اولادصغار پر ولایت رکھتا ہے پس اس کو اپنی جنس پر شہادت کی ولایت بھی ہوگی ۔ اور فسق من حیث الاعتقاد مانع شہادت نہیں ہے کیوں کہ جس چیز کو وہ اپنے دین میں حرام سمجھتا ہے اس سے پر ہیز کرے گا اور جھوٹ بولنا تمام ادیان میں حرام ہے۔ بر خلاف مرتد کے اس لئے کہ اس کے واسطے کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے اور برخلاف مسلمان پر ذمی کے گواہی دینے کے کیوں کہ ذمی کو مسلمان کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ ذمی مسلمان پر بہتان باندھے گا کیوں کہ مسلمان کا اس کو مشہور اور مغلوب کرنا اس کو غیظ میں مبتلا کرتا ہے اور کفر کی مانتیں اگر چہ مختلف ہیں لیکن کسی نے کسی کو مقہور نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس ان کو غصہ، بہتان باندھنے پر آمادہ نہ کرے گا۔
تشریح ذمی وہ غیر مسلم ہے جو امیر المومنین سے اجازت لیکر دار الاسلام میں رہتا ہو صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ ذمیوں میں سے بعض کی شہادت بعض کے خلاف قبول کر لیجائے گی یعنی اگر ایک ذمی دوسرے ذمی کے خلاف گواہی دے تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی اگر چدان کے ادیان مختلف ہوں مثلا یہودی کا نصرانی کے خلاف اور نصرانی کا یہودی کے خلاف گواہی دینا جائز ہے امام مالک اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ذمیوں کی گواہ؟ آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے خلاف مطلقاً قبول نہ ہو گی خواہ ان کی مانتیں متفق ہوں یا مختلف ہوں۔ ابن ابی لیلی نے فرمایا کہ اگر شاہد اور مشہود علیہ دونوں کا دین ایک ہو تو گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی ورنہ نہیں۔ ابن ابی لیلی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: لا شهادة لاهل ملة على اهل ملة اخرى الا المسلمين فشهادة متهم ابی مقبولة على اهل الملل یعنی ایک ملت کے ماننے والے کی شہادت دوسری ملت کے ماننے والے کے خلاف قبول نہ ہوگی۔ مگر مسلمان کہ ان کی شہادت تمام ادیان والوں کے خلاف مقبول ہے۔
امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کافر فاسق ہے۔ چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے و الكافرون هم الظالمون کا فرہی ظالم ہیں اور ظالم فاسق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا کا فر فاسق ہوا۔ اور فاسق کی خبر فورا قبول نہیں کی جاتی ، بلکہ اس میں تو قف کرنا واجب ہے چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے ان جاء کم فاسق بنباء فتبينوا اگر کوئی فاسق تمہارے پاس خبر لے کر آئے تو اس کی تحقیق کر لو۔ یعنی فورا قبول نہ کرو بلکہ توقف کرو ۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ فاسق کی خبر اور شہادت قبول نہیں ہوتی اور کافر بھی چونکہ فاسق ہے لہذا اس کی شہادت بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اس فاسق ہونے کی وجہ سے کافر کی شہادت مسلمان کے خلاف قبول نہیں ہوتی پس کافر مرتد کے مانند ہو گیا۔ یعنی جس طرح مرتد کی گواہی مرتد اور غیر مرتد کے حق میں اور ان کے خلاف قبول نہیں ہوتی ۔ اسی طرح کافر کی گواہی کا فر اور غیر کا فردونوں کے حق میں قبول ہوگی نہ دونوں کے خلاف قبول ہوگی۔ ہدایہ کے اکثر نسخوں میں والكافرون هم الفاسقون ہے حالانکہ قرآن پاک میں والكافرون هم الظالمون ہے۔ اس کی تصحیح کرتے ہوئے صاحب فتح القدیر نے فرمایا ہے کہ نہایہ میں یہ عبارت اس طرح ہے للكافرين هم الفاسقون یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے کافروں کے لئے فرمایا ہے کہ وہ فاسق ہیں اور فاسق اس
The testimony of a dhimmi against a dhimmi is valid; statements of jurists.
He said: And the testimony of the people of dhimma is accepted, some against others, even if their religions differ. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: It is not accepted because he is a fasiq. Allah said: 'And the disbelievers are the fasiqun.' So it is obligatory to pause (withhold acceptance) regarding his report, and for this reason his testimony is not accepted against a Muslim, so he becomes like an apostate.
And our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the testimony of Christians against each other; and because he (the dhimmi) has guardianship over himself and his young children, so he is qualified to give testimony concerning his own kind. And fisq due to belief is not a preventer, because he refrains from what he believes is forbidden in his religion, and lying is prohibited in all religions. Unlike an apostate, because he has no guardianship; and unlike the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim, because he has no guardianship relative to him, and because he would slander him, since the Muslim's dominance over him angers him. And the religions of disbelief, even if they differ, none has domination over the other; thus anger does not impel them to slander.
Translation: And the testimony of dhimmis among themselves, one against another, will be accepted even if their religions are separate. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i said: The testimony of dhimmis against each other will not be accepted at all because they are fasiqs; Allah said: 'The disbelievers are the fasiqun.' So it is obligatory to pause concerning his report; for this reason his testimony is not accepted against Muslims. Thus he becomes like an apostate.
And our proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) permitted the testimony of Christians against each other; and because the dhimmi has guardianship over himself and his young children, so he will have guardianship to testify concerning his own kind. And fisq due to belief is not a preventer of testimony, because he will refrain from what he considers forbidden in his religion, and lying is prohibited in all religions. Unlike an apostate, because he has no guardianship; and unlike a dhimmi testifying against a Muslim, because the dhimmi has no guardianship relative to the Muslim, and because he would slander him, since the Muslim's dominance over him angers him. And the religions of disbelief, even if they differ, none has domination over the other; so anger does not impel them to slander.
Explanation: A dhimmi is a non-Muslim who lives in Dar al-Islam with permission from the Amir al-Mu'minin. Sahib al-Quduri said: The testimony of some dhimmis against others will be accepted. That is, if one dhimmi gives testimony against another dhimmi, his testimony is accepted even if their religions differ; e.g., a Jew against a Christian and a Christian against a Jew is permissible. Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i said: The testimony of dhimmis among themselves, one against another, is absolutely not accepted, whether their religions agree or differ. Ibn Abi Layla said: If both the witness and the adverse party have the same religion, then the testimony will be accepted; otherwise not. The proof of Ibn Abi Layla is the hadith: 'There is no testimony for the people of one religion against the people of another religion except Muslims; so the testimony of an accused (?) is acceptable against people of religions.' Meaning: The testimony of a follower of one religion is not accepted against a follower of another religion, except Muslims, for their testimony is accepted against all people of religions.
The proof of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i is that a disbeliever is a fasiq. Thus Allah said: 'And the disbelievers are the wrongdoers (zālimūn)' and a wrongdoer is a fasiq. Therefore a disbeliever is a fasiq. And the report of a fasiq is not immediately accepted; rather, it is obligatory to pause. As Allah said: 'If a fasiq comes to you with news, then verify.' Meaning: do not accept immediately but pause. The summary is that the report and testimony of a fasiq are not accepted, and since a disbeliever is also a fasiq, his testimony will not be accepted. Because of this fisq, the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, so the disbeliever becomes like an apostate. That is, just as the testimony of an apostate is not accepted either for or against an apostate or a non-apostate, similarly the testimony of a disbeliever will not be accepted either for or against a disbeliever or a non-disbeliever? In most copies of Hidayah it is 'wal-kāfirūna hum al-fāsiqūn' whereas in the Qur'an it is 'wal-kāfirūna hum al-zālimūn'. Correcting this, the author of Fath al-Qadir said that in al-Nihayah the phrase is 'lil-kāfirīna hum al-fāsiqūn', i.e., Allah said regarding the disbelievers that they are the fasiqun, and the fasiq is...
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the testimony of dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of an Islamic state) against each other. The Hanafi position, as stated by al-Quduri and al-Hidayah, is that such testimony is accepted even if the dhimmis belong to different religions (e.g., Jew vs. Christian). The proof is twofold: (1) The Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted Christians to testify against each other; (2) a dhimmi has guardianship (wilayah) over himself and his minor children, which makes him qualified to testify concerning his own kind (ahl al-dhimma). The text argues that fisq due to belief (kufr) does not prevent testimony because a dhimmi refrains from what he believes is forbidden in his religion, and lying is prohibited in all religions. Thus, they are not accused of lying in the same way as a practical sinner or an apostate. The opposing views: Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i reject it absolutely, arguing that all disbelievers are fasiq (sinful/disobedient) based on the Qur'anic verse 'wa al-kāfirūna hum al-fāsiqūn' (or al-zālimūn), and the report of a fasiq is not accepted (reference to Surah al-Hujurat: 6). They analogize dhimmis to apostates, whose testimony is rejected entirely. Ibn Abi Layla takes an intermediate position: testimony is accepted only if the witness and the defendant share the same religion. His evidence is a hadith (interpreted) that restricts testimony to one's own religious community except for Muslims. The Hanafi response counters: the fisq of disbelief does not automatically make one a liar; moreover, among dhimmis there is no religious domination or animosity that would impel them to slander each other, unlike the case of a dhimmi testifying against a Muslim (where anger from subjugation might cause slander). Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands: dhimmis can testify against each other.

Key Terms
ذمی (Dhimmi): A non-Muslim who lives permanently in an Islamic state with a covenant of protection (dhimmah), paying jizyah and accepting Islamic authority.
ولایت (Wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship. In this context, a dhimmi has wilayah over himself and his minor children, which qualifies him to be a witness for his community.
فسق اعتقادی (Fisq I'tiqadi): Sinfulness due to erroneous belief (disbelief), as opposed to practical sin (fisq amali). The text distinguishes between the two, arguing that fisq i'tiqadi does not necessarily lead to lying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the testimony of a dhimmi against another dhimmi of a different religion?
A) It is not accepted because dhimmis are fasiqs.
B) It is accepted only if the witness and the defendant share the same religion.
C) It is accepted regardless of difference in religion.
D) It is accepted only in criminal cases, not in financial matters.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the testimony of dhimmis against each other regardless of religious difference, based on prophetic hadith and the principle that fisq of belief does not undermine reliability.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony of Dhimmis Against Each Other: Hanafi Acceptance Across Religions
Inter-madhhab dispute on testimony of dhimmis with different religions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhimmi testimony, explain the two main Hanafi proofs, and evaluate the opposing arguments by Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's testimony against another dhimmi is accepted even if their religions differ — ideological sin does not disqualify, and wilaya over oneself qualifies.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents a well-known inter-madhhab dispute: can dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state) testify against each other when their religions differ? The Hanafi school, following a prophetic hadith and the concept of wilaya, answers yes. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i reject it entirely, while Ibn Abi Layla accepts only within the same religion. This lesson walks through the proofs and the Hanafi responses, clarifying why Hanafis distinguish between ideological sin (fisq i'tiqadi) and practical sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State exactly what the Hanafis rule regarding dhimmi testimony: it is admissible even if the witness and defendant have different religions.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Examine the Hanafi proofs
Identify the two main proofs: the hadith of the Prophet permitting Christian testimony against each other, and the argument from wilaya (the dhimmi has guardianship over himself and his children).
Also note the secondary proof that fisq i'tiqadi does not bar testimony.
3
Understand the opposing view
State the position of Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i: dhimmi testimony is absolutely inadmissible because disbelievers are fasiq.
They cite Quranic verses and analogize to apostates.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafis rebut the opposing proofs: distinguish fisq i'tiqadi from fisq 'amali, point out that the apostate analogy fails because apostates lack wilaya, and note that the hadith specifically addresses dhimmis.
Also mention the response to the Ibn Abi Layla position.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafis accept dhimmi testimony against other dhimmis; Malik and Shafi'i do not accept it at all; Ibn Abi Layla accepts only within the same religion.
This difference affects how courts handle disputes among non-Muslim citizens.

اشرف الہدایہ جلد وام
ترجمہ اور ذمیوں کی گواہی آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے خلاف قبول کی جائے گی اگر چہ ان کے ادیان جدا جدا ہوں اور امام مالک اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ذمیوں کی باہم گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی کیوں کہ وہ فاسق ہیں اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا کہ کافر ہی فاسق ہے۔ پس اس کی خبر میں توقف کرنا واجب ہے اسی وجہ سے اس کی شہادت مسلمانوں کے خلاف قبول نہ ہو گی۔ لہذا وہ مرتد کے مانند ہو گیا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے نصرانیوں کی گواہی ایک کی دوسرے کے خلاف جائز قرار دی ہے اور اس لئے کہ ذمی اپنی ذلت پر اور اپنی اولاد صغار پر ولایت رکھتا ہے پس اس کو اپنی جنس پر شہادت کی ولایت بھی ہوگی۔ اور فسق من حیث الاعتقاد مانع شہادت نہیں ہے کیوں کہ جس چیز کو وہ اپنے دین میں حرام سمجھتا ہے اس سے پرہیز کرے گا اور جھوٹ بولنا تمام ادیان میں حرام ہے۔ بر خلاف مرتد کے اس لئے کہ اس کے واسطے کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے اور برخلاف مسلمان پر ذمی کے گواہی دینے کے کیوں کہ ذمی کو مسلمان کی طرف نسبت کرتے ہوئے کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے اور اس لئے کہ ذمی مسلمان پر بہتان باندھے گا کیوں کہ مسلمان کا اس کو مشہور اور مغلوب کرنا اس کو غیظ میں مبتلا کرتا ہے اور کفر کی مانتیں اگر چہ مختلف ہیں لیکن کسی نے کسی کو مقہور نہیں کیا ہے۔ پس ان کو غصہ، بہتان باندھنے پر آمادہ نہ کرے گا۔
تشریح ذمی وہ غیر مسلم ہے جو امیر المومنین سے اجازت لیکر دار الاسلام میں رہتا ہو صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ ذمیوں میں سے بعض کی شہادت بعض کے خلاف قبول کر لیجائے گی یعنی اگر ایک ذمی دوسرے ذمی کے خلاف گواہی دے تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی اگر چہ ان کے ادیان مختلف ہوں مثلا یہودی کا نصرانی کے خلاف اور نصرانی کا یہودی کے خلاف گواہی دینا جائز ہے امام مالک اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ ذمیوں کی گواہی آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے خلاف مطلقاً قبول نہ ہو گی خواہ ان کی مانتیں متفق ہوں یا مختلف ہوں۔ ابن ابی لیلی نے فرمایا کہ اگر شاہد اور مشہود علیہ دونوں کا دین ایک ہو تو گواہی قبول کر لی جائے گی ورنہ نہیں۔ ابن ابی لیلی کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے: لا شهادة لاهل ملة على اهل ملة اخرى الا المسلمين فشهادة متهم ابی مقبولة على اهل الملل یعنی ایک ملت کے ماننے والے کی شہادت دوسری ملت کے ماننے والے کے خلاف قبول نہ ہوگی۔ مگر مسلمان کہ ان کی شہادت تمام ادیان والوں کے خلاف مقبول ہے۔
امام مالک اور امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ کافر فاسق ہے۔ چنانچہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے و الكافرون هم الظالمون کافر ہی ظالم ہیں اور ظالم فاسق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا کافر فاسق ہوا۔ اور فاسق کی خبر فورا قبول نہیں کی جاتی، بلکہ اس میں توقف کرنا واجب ہے چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے ان جاء کم فاسق بنباء فتبينوا اگر کوئی فاسق تمہارے پاس خبر لے کر آئے تو اس کی تحقیق کر لو۔ یعنی فورا قبول نہ کرو بلکہ توقف کرو۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ فاسق کی خبر اور شہادت قبول نہیں ہوتی اور کافر بھی چونکہ فاسق ہے لہذا اس کی شہادت بھی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اس فاسق ہونے کی وجہ سے کافر کی شہادت مسلمان کے خلاف قبول نہیں ہوتی پس کافر مرتد کے مانند ہو گیا۔ یعنی جس طرح مرتد کی گواہی مرتد اور غیر مرتد کے حق میں اور ان کے خلاف قبول نہیں ہوتی۔ اسی طرح کافر کی گواہی کافر اور غیر کافر دونوں کے حق میں قبول ہوگی نہ دونوں کے خلاف قبول ہوگی۔ ہدایہ کے اکثر نسخوں میں والكافرون هم الفاسقون ہے حالانکہ قرآن پاک میں والكافرون هم الظالمون ہے۔ اس کی تصحیح کرتے ہوئے صاحب فتح القدیر نے فرمایا ہے کہ نہایہ میں یہ عبارت اس طرح ہے للكافرين هم الفاسقون یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے کافروں کے لئے فرمایا ہے کہ وہ فاسق ہیں اور فاسق اس

کتاب الشهادة
اشرف الہدایہ جلد دہم لئے ہیں کہ قرآن میں کفار کو ظالم کہا گیا ہے۔ چنانچہ فرمایا و الكافرون هم الظالمون اور ظالم فاسق ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا کافر بھی فاسق ہوگا۔
ہماری دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان النبی اجاز شهادة النصارى بعضهم على بعض یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے نصاری کی شہادت بعض کی بعض کے خلاف جائز قرار دی ہے احناف کی طرف سے بیان کردہ اس دلیل پر یہ اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ دلیل دعوئی کے مطابق نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ دعوی یہ ہے کہ ذمیوں میں بعض کی شہادت بعض کے خلاف جائز ہے اگر چہ انکی ملتیں مختلف ہوں اور دلیل میں جو حدیث ذکر کی گئی ہے اس میں شاہد اور مشہود علیہ دونوں کی ملت ایک ہے یعنی نصرانیت، اگر صاحب ہدایہ نصاری کی جگہ اہل الکتاب کا لفظ ذکر کرتے اور یوں فرماتے ان النبی اجاز شهادة اهل الكتاب تو دلیل دعوی کے موافق ہو جاتا۔ ابن ماجہ میں جابر بن عبد اللہ کے طریق سے یہ حدیث مذکورہ الفاظ سے موجود بھی ہے چنانچہ جابر بن عبد اللہ سے روایت ہے ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اجاز شهادة اهل الكتاب بعضهم على بعض
احناف کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ کافر کو اپنی ذات پر بھی ولایت حاصل ہے اور اپنی نابالغ اولاد پر بھی اور جس شخص کو ولایت اپنی اور حاصل ہوتی ہے وہ شہادت کا بھی اہل ہوتا ہے لہذا کافر، شہادت کا اہل ہوگا۔ البتہ کافر کی گواہی اس کی جنس (کافر) کے خلاف تو قبول کر لی جائے گی لیکن اس کی جنس کے علاوہ (مسلمانوں) کے خلاف قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے لن يجعل الله للكافرین علی المؤمنین سبیلا یعنی ہرگز نہ دے گا اللہ کافروں کو مسلمانوں پر غلبہ کی راہ اور مسلمانوں کے خلاف گواہی دینے میں چونکہ کفار کا غلبہ ہے اس لئے مسلمانوں کے خلاف کفار کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔ اور رہا امام شافعی اور امام مالک کا یہ کہنا کہ کافر فاسق ہے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کافر کا فسق اعتقادی ہے اور سابق میں گزر چکا ہے کہ فسق اعتقادی مانع شہادت نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا کافر کا فسق اعتقادی مانع شہادت نہ ہوگا۔ اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ انسان جس چیز کو اپنے دین میں حرام سمجھتا ہے اس سے پرہیز کرتا ہے اور جھوٹ تمام ادیان میں ممنوع اور حرام ہے لہذا کافر بھی جھوٹ کے ممنوع ہونے کی وجہ سے اس سے پرہیز کرے گا۔ اور کافر جب جھوٹ سے پرہیز اور اجتناب کرے گا تو وہ جھوٹ کے ساتھ متہم بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب کافر جھوٹ کے ساتھ متہم نہیں ہے تو اس کی گواہی بھی قبول ہو جائے گی۔
بخلاف المرتد.... الخ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مرتد کو نہ اپنی ذات پر ولایت ہوتی ہے اور نہ اپنی اولاد صغار پر۔ پس جب مرتد کو نہ اپنی ذات پر ولایت حاصل ہے اور نہ اپنی اولاد پر تو کسی دوسرے پر کس طرح ولایت حاصل ہوگی اور جب مرتد کو بالکل ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے تو اس کو شہادت کا بھی حق حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شہادت کا حق اس کو حاصل ہوتا ہے جس کو ولایت کا حق حاصل ہے۔
بخلاف شهادة الذمي على المسلم ... الخ سے امام شافعی کے دوسرے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مسلمان کے خلاف ذمی کی شہادت قبول نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذمی کو مسلمان پر کوئی ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد لن يجعل الله للكافرين على المؤمنين سبيلا اس پر شاہد ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذمی
Book of Testimony. Ashraf al-Hidaya Volume 10. Translation: The testimony of dhimmis against each other is accepted even if their religions are separate. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said that the testimony of dhimmis among themselves is not accepted because they are sinners (fasiq). Allah said: 'The disbelievers are the sinners.' So it is obligatory to pause in accepting their report. For this reason their testimony against Muslims is not accepted. Thus he becomes like an apostate. Our proof is that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, permitted the testimony of Christians against each other, and because the dhimmi has guardianship over his own person and his minor children, so he also has guardianship of testimony against his own kind. And sin from the aspect of belief does not prevent testimony because he will abstain from what he considers forbidden in his religion, and lying is forbidden in all religions. Contrary to the apostate because he has no guardianship, and contrary to the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim because the dhimmi has no guardianship in relation to a Muslim, and because the dhimmi would slander the Muslim as the Muslim's superiority and domination over him enrages him. But among disbeliefs, even if they differ, none has subjugated the other, so anger will not impel them to slander. Explanation: A dhimmi is a non-Muslim who lives in Dar al-Islam with permission from the Amir al-Mu'minin. Sahib al-Quduri said: The testimony of some dhimmis against others is accepted, i.e., if one dhimmi testifies against another dhimmi, his testimony is accepted even if their religions differ, e.g., a Jew against a Christian and a Christian against a Jew is permissible. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i said: The testimony of dhimmis against each other is absolutely not accepted, whether their beliefs agree or differ. Ibn Abi Layla said: If the witness and the defendant have the same religion, the testimony is accepted; otherwise not. Ibn Abi Layla's proof is the hadith: 'No testimony of people of one religion against people of another religion except Muslims; the testimony of a Muslim is accepted against all religions.' Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i's proof is that the disbeliever is a sinner. Thus Allah said: 'And the disbelievers are the wrongdoers.' And a wrongdoer is a sinner. So the disbeliever is a sinner. The report of a sinner is not immediately accepted; rather, it is obligatory to pause. Thus the command of Allah: 'If a sinner comes to you with news, verify it.' Meaning do not accept immediately but pause. Summary: The news and testimony of a sinner are not accepted, and since the disbeliever is a sinner, his testimony is also not accepted. Because of this sinfulness, the testimony of a disbeliever against a Muslim is not accepted, so the disbeliever becomes like an apostate. Just as the testimony of an apostate is not accepted for or against apostates and non-apostates, similarly the testimony of a disbeliever will not be accepted for or against disbelievers and non-disbelievers. In most copies of al-Hidayah there is 'wa al-kafirun hum al-fasiqun' while in the Quran it is 'wa al-kafirun hum al-zalimun'. Correcting this, Sahib Fath al-Qadir said that in al-Nihayah the phrase is 'li al-kafirina hum al-fasiqun', i.e., Allah said regarding the disbelievers that they are sinners, and a sinner... Page 82: ...they said that in the Quran disbelievers are called wrongdoers. Thus He said: 'And the disbelievers are the wrongdoers' and a wrongdoer is a sinner, so the disbeliever is also a sinner. Our proof is the hadith: 'The Prophet permitted the testimony of Christians against each other.' This proof presented by the Hanafis was objected to: that the proof does not match the claim. Because the claim is that the testimony of dhimmis against each other is permissible even if their religions differ, but the hadith cited mentions that both witness and defendant belong to the same religion, i.e., Christianity. If the author of al-Hidayah had said 'the People of the Book' instead of 'Christians' and said 'The Prophet permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other', then the proof would match the claim. In Ibn Majah, via Jabir ibn Abdullah, this hadith exists with those exact words: Jabir ibn Abdullah narrated that the Prophet permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other. The second Hanafi proof is that the disbeliever has guardianship over himself and over his minor children, and whoever has guardianship over himself is also qualified for testimony. Hence the disbeliever is qualified for testimony. However, his testimony is accepted against his own kind (disbelievers) but not against others (Muslims), because Allah said: 'Allah will never grant the disbelievers a way over the believers.' In testifying against Muslims, there is dominance of disbelievers over believers, so it is not accepted. As for Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik's saying that the disbeliever is a sinner, the response is that the disbeliever's sin is in belief, and it has passed that sin in belief does not prevent testimony. Therefore the disbeliever's sin in belief will not prevent testimony. The reason is that a person refrains from what he considers forbidden in his religion, and lying is prohibited and forbidden in all religions, so the disbeliever will also refrain from lying due to its prohibition. When the disbeliever refrains from lying, he will not be accused of lying. And when he is not accused of lying, his testimony will be accepted. 'Contrary to the apostate...' from this is the response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The gist of the response is that the apostate has no guardianship over himself nor over his minor children. So when the apostate has no guardianship over himself nor over his children, how can he have guardianship over others? And when the apostate has absolutely no guardianship, he will have no right to testimony. Because the right to testimony is given to one who has the right of guardianship. 'Contrary to the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim...' from this is the response to Imam Shafi'i's second analogy. The gist of the response is that the reason the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim is not accepted is that the dhimmi has no guardianship over the Muslim. Thus the command of Allah: 'Allah will never grant the disbelievers a way over the believers' testifies to this. The second reason is that the dhimmi...
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the admissibility of testimony given by dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state) against one another. The Hanafi position, as articulated by Imam Abu Hanifa and recorded in works like al-Hidayah and al-Quduri, is that such testimony is accepted even if the dhimmis belong to different religions (e.g., a Jew testifying against a Christian). The key Hanafi proofs are: (1) a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) permitted the testimony of Christians against each other; (2) the principle that a dhimmi has legal guardianship (wilaya) over himself and his minor children, which qualifies him to testify against others of his own kind; and (3) that disbelief constitutes sin from an ideological perspective (fisq i'tiqadi), which does not prevent testimony because lying is forbidden in all religions, and dhimmis, like Muslims, avoid open falsehood. The opposing view, held by Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i, is that the testimony of dhimmis is absolutely inadmissible against anyone, Muslim or fellow dhimmi, because disbelievers are considered fasiq (sinners) based on Quranic verses like 'wa al-kafirun hum al-zalimun' (the disbelievers are the wrongdoers) and the command to verify news from a fasiq. They analogize dhimmis to apostates (murtadd), whose testimony is rejected entirely. A third position, attributed to Ibn Abi Layla, accepts dhimmi testimony only when both witness and defendant share the same religion. The Hanafi responses refute the opposing proofs: they distinguish fisq i'tiqadi from fisq 'amali (practical sin), arguing that ideological sin does not automatically disqualify a witness in a dhimmi's case because witness reliability depends on abstention from lying, which is universal. Regarding the hadith, they clarify that a version in Ibn Majah explicitly mentions 'Ahl al-Kitab' (People of the Book), supporting their inclusive ruling. Furthermore, they explain why dhimmi testimony against Muslims is prohibited: the Quranic verse 'lan yaj'ala Allahu lil-kafirina 'ala al-mu'minin sabila' (Allah will never grant disbelievers a way over believers) precludes giving disbelievers authority over believers, and enmity might lead to slander. However, among dhimmis themselves, no such dominance exists, so testimony is accepted. This nuanced position reflects the Hanafi school's reliance on istihsan (juristic preference) and the purpose behind legal rulings.

Key Terms
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of the Islamic state, having a covenant (dhimma) with the Muslim ruler.
فسق اعتقادی (fisq i'tiqadi): Sin or transgression due to disbelief or ideological error, as opposed to sinful acts (fisq 'amali).
ولایت (wilaya): Legal guardianship or authority; the capacity to act on one's own behalf or over others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim not accepted?
A) Because dhimmis are always fasiq and their testimony is never accepted.
B) Because Allah said 'lan yaj'ala Allahu lil-kafirina 'ala al-mu'minin sabila'.
C) Because dhimmis have no wilaya over Muslims.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, dhimmi testimony against fellow dhimmis is accepted regardless of religious difference, based on hadith, wilaya, and the distinction of fisq i'tiqadi, but testimony against Muslims is prohibited to prevent dominance.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Testimony of Disbelievers Against Each Other is Acceptable
Argument for accepting testimony of disbelievers against each other with proofs and refutation of objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of disbelievers against each other, identify the proofs (Quran, hadith, and rational), and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i/Maliki arguments.

Core Idea
A disbeliever's testimony is accepted against another disbeliever due to mutual wilayah, but not against Muslims as per Quran.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute: Can a non-Muslim testify against another non-Muslim in an Islamic court? The Hanafi school says yes, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools say no. The debate hinges on concepts of fisq (sinfulness), wilayah (legal authority), and the interpretation of specific Quranic verses and hadith. By the end, you will understand the Hanafi case and how they rebut the opposing arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact claim: testimony of a disbeliever is acceptable against another disbeliever (even from a different sect) but not against a Muslim.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik reject all testimony of disbelievers, equating them with fasiqs whose testimony is invalid.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their proofs: (1) A disbeliever is a fasiq, and fasiq testimony is rejected. (2) Qiyas to an apostate (murtad) who has no wilayah. (3) Qiyas to a dhimmi testifying against a Muslim.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: The fisq of a disbeliever is i'tiqadi (doctrinal), not 'amali (practical), and doctrinal fisq does not disqualify testimony because all religions prohibit lying. Apostates have no wilayah at all, so the analogy fails. A dhimmi has no wilayah over a Muslim, but a kafir does have wilayah over another kafir.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: In Hanafi courts, dhimmis (and other non-Muslims) can testify against each other. In Shafi'i/Maliki courts, such testimony is rejected entirely.

بخلاف المرتد.... الخ سے امام شافعی کے قیاس کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مرتد کو نہ اپنی ذات پر ولایت ہوتی ہے اور نہ اپنی اولادصغار پر۔ پس جب مرتد کو نہ اپنی ذات پر ولایت حاصل ہے اور نہ اپنی اولاد پر تو کسی دوسرے پر کس طرح ولایت حاصل ہوگی اور جب مرتد کو بالکل ولایت حاصل نہیں ہے تو اس کو شہادت کا بھی حق حاصل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ شہادت کا حق اُس کو حاصل ہوتا ہے جس کو ولایت کا حق حاصل ہے۔

ابن ابی پہلی کی پیش کردہ حدیث لا شهادة لاهل ملة على اهل ملة اخرى .... الحدیث حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ حدیث باری تعالیٰ کے قول والذين كفروا اولیاء بعض کے مخالف ہے کیونکہ آیت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کفار آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے ولی ہیں اور ان کو آپس میں ولایت کا حق حاصل ہے اور حدیث سے اس کی نفی ہوتی ہے پیس کتاب اللہ کے مقابلہ میں حدیث متروک ہو جائے گی۔
We [Hanafis] say: In the Quran, disbelievers are called oppressors. Thus He said: 'And the disbelievers, they are the oppressors' and an oppressor is a fasiq. Therefore a disbeliever is also a fasiq. Our proof is this hadith: 'The Prophet allowed the testimony of Christians some against others' meaning the Messenger of Allah allowed the testimony of Christians some against others. An objection was raised against this proof presented by the Hanafis: that the proof does not match the claim. Because the claim is that testimony of dhimmis some against others is allowed even if their religious sects are different, but in the hadith mentioned, both the witness and the one against whom testimony is given are of the same religion, i.e., Christianity. If the author of al-Hidayah had used the word 'Ahl al-Kitab' instead of 'Christians' and said 'the Prophet allowed the testimony of the People of the Book', then the proof would match the claim. In Ibn Majah, through Jabir ibn Abdullah, this hadith exists with the mentioned wording: narrated from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Prophet allowed the testimony of the People of the Book some against others. The second proof of the Hanafis is that a disbeliever has wilayah over himself and over his minor children, and whoever has wilayah over himself and [his children] is also qualified for testimony. Therefore a disbeliever is qualified for testimony. However, the testimony of a disbeliever will be accepted against his own kind (disbelievers) but not against others (Muslims). Because Allah said: 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers.' And in giving testimony against Muslims, there is dominance of disbelievers, so their testimony is not accepted against Muslims. As for Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik saying that a disbeliever is a fasiq, the answer is that the fisq of a disbeliever is i'tiqadi (doctrinal), and it has passed earlier that i'tiqadi fisq does not prevent testimony. Therefore the i'tiqadi fisq of a disbeliever will not prevent testimony. The reason is that a person refrains from what he considers forbidden in his religion, and lying is prohibited and forbidden in all religions. Hence a disbeliever will also refrain from lying due to its prohibition. And when a disbeliever refrains from lying, he will not be accused of lying. And when a disbeliever is not accused of lying, his testimony will be accepted. 'As for the apostate...' etc. is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's analogy. The gist of the answer is that an apostate has neither wilayah over himself nor over his minor children. So when an apostate has no wilayah over himself or his children, how can he have wilayah over anyone else? And when an apostate has no wilayah at all, he will have no right to testimony, because the right to testimony belongs to one who has the right of wilayah. 'As for the testimony of a dhimmi against a Muslim...' etc. is the answer to Imam Shafi'i's second analogy. The gist of the answer is that the reason a dhimmi's testimony is not accepted against a Muslim is that a dhimmi has no wilayah over a Muslim. The saying of Allah 'Allah will never give the disbelievers a way over the believers' is evidence of this. The second reason is that a dhimmi would slander a Muslim, because the Muslim's keeping him downtrodden and subjugated keeps him in rage and anger. So the dhimmi, to remove his rage, might slander the Muslim, and in the presence of such possibility, the question of accepting testimony does not arise. And although the sects of disbelief are different, in Dar al-Islam a disbeliever of one sect cannot dominate and subjugate a disbeliever of another sect, so there is no malice among them. And when there is no rage and anger among them, they will not slander each other. And when the possibility of mutual slander is removed, their testimony against each other will be accepted. The hadith presented by Ibn Abi Shayba: 'لا شهادة لاهل ملة على اهل ملة اخرى' (No testimony of one religious community against another religious community) is answered by saying that this hadith contradicts the saying of Allah: 'And those who disbelieve are allies of one another.' Because the verse indicates that disbelievers are each other's allies and they have the right of wilayah among themselves, and the hadith negates it. So in opposition to the Book of Allah, the hadith is abandoned.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the testimony of disbelievers. The Hanafi position is that a disbeliever's testimony is acceptable against another disbeliever, even if they belong to different sects (e.g., Christian vs. Jew). The proof includes a hadith where the Prophet allowed testimony of Christians against each other, and an argument from wilayah (authority): a disbeliever has wilayah over himself and his children, so he is qualified for testimony. However, against Muslims, it is not accepted due to the Quranic verse 'لن يجعل الله للكافرين على المؤمنين سبيلا'. The response to Shafi'i and Maliki who consider kafir as fasiq is that their fisq is doctrinal (i'tiqadi), not practical, and doctrinal sin does not disqualify testimony because all religions prohibit lying. The text refutes two analogies by Shafi'i: (1) Comparison with an apostate (murtad) who lacks wilayah entirely, so his testimony is rejected. (2) Comparison with a dhimmi testifying against a Muslim, which is rejected due to lack of wilayah and fear of slander. The text also refutes the hadith 'لا شهادة لاهل ملة على اهل ملة اخرى' by stating it contradicts the Quran (Surah Al-Anfal: 73) that declares disbelievers are allies of one another, so the hadith is deemed abandoned.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahadah): Testimony given in court; the act of bearing witness.
ولاية (wilayah): Legal authority or guardianship; in this context, the capacity to have authority over oneself and others.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness or deviation from religious obedience.
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of an Islamic state, paying jizyah.
مرتد (murtad): An apostate from Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason a disbeliever's testimony is rejected against a Muslim?
A) Disbelievers are fasiqs and therefore untrustworthy.
B) The Quran says 'لن يجعل الله للكافرين على المؤمنين سبيلا', indicating no authority over Muslims.
C) The Prophet forbade disbelievers from testifying against Muslims in a specific hadith.
D) Muslims are inherently superior and disbelievers cannot bear witness in any case.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a disbeliever's testimony is valid against another disbeliever due to mutual wilayah, but invalid against a Muslim to prevent non-Muslim dominance over believers.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony of a Harbi Musta'min Against a Dhimmi is Not Accepted
Ruling on harbi musta'min testimony against dhimmi with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a harbi musta'min against a dhimmi and explain the two rational proofs: lack of wilayah and difference in status.

Core Idea
A harbi musta'min cannot testify against a dhimmi because difference of dar severs wilayah and the dhimmi's higher status prevents it.

In this passage, the Hanafi school presents a specific ruling on testimony across different legal jurisdictions. The key issue is whether a temporary resident from enemy territory (harbi musta'min) can provide valid testimony against a permanent protected resident (dhimmi) in a Hanafi court. The ruling is negative, and the reasoning reveals foundational principles of Hanafi testimony law: the requirement of wilayah (authority) and the consideration of relative status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exact parties involved
Note that the harbi in question is specifically a musta'min (one who entered dar al-Islam with aman), not any harbi. The ruling applies only to this category.
Al-Hidayah clarifies this specification to avoid confusion.
2
Understand the concept of wilayah in testimony
Wilayah (authority/guardianship) is a prerequisite for the validity of testimony in Hanafi law. The witness must have some form of authority over the person against whom they testify.
This condition is unique to the Hanafi school among the four major madhahib.
3
Apply the 'difference of dar' principle
The harbi musta'min belongs to dar al-harb, while the dhimmi belongs to dar al-Islam. This difference in jurisdiction severs any potential wilayah.
Dar al-harb and dar al-Islam are distinct legal territories.
4
Consider the status hierarchy
The dhimmi is considered higher in status than the harbi musta'min because the dhimmi has accepted jizya and enjoys protected blood. A lower-status person cannot testify against a higher-status person.
This principle is analogous to the rule that a slave cannot testify against a free person.
5
Conclude the ruling
Due to both the absence of wilayah and the status difference, the testimony of a harbi musta'min against a dhimmi is not accepted in the Hanafi school.
The proof is based on istihsan (rational preference) and the general legal objectives.

قال ولا تقبل شهادة الحربي على الذمى اراد به والله اعلم المستامن لانه لا ولاية له عليه لان الذمى من اهل دارنا وهو اعلى حالا منه
ترجمہ اور ذمی کے خلاف حربی کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی واللہ اعلم اس سے مراد وہ حربی ہے جو امان لے کر دار الاسلام میں آیا ہو ۔ اس لئے کہ حربی کو ذمی پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ذمی ہمارے دار کا رہنے والا ہے اور وہ حربی سے اچھی حالت میں ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے فرمایا کہ حربی کی شہادت ذمی کے خلاف قبول نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا کہ حربی سے مراد وہ حربی ہے جو امان لے کر دار الاسلام میں آیا ہو یعنی حربی مستامن کی گواہی ذمی کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ حربی مستامن کو ڈمی پر کوئی ولایت نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے کہ حربی مستامن دارالحرب کا باشندہ ہے اور ذمی دار الاسلام کا رہنے والا ہے۔ اور حکما دارین کا ختلاف ولایت کو منقطع کر دیتا ہے۔ یعنی دار الحرب اور دار الاسلام میں سے ایک دار کے رہنے والے کو دوسرے دار کے رہنے والے پر ولایت کا حق حاصل نہیں ہوتا ۔ پس جب حربی مستامن کو ڈمی پر ولایت کا حق حاصل نہیں ہے تو حربی مستامن کی گواہی ذمی کے خلاف قبول نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ شہادت کا اہل وہی ہوتا ہے جو اہل ولایت میں سے ہو۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ ذمی کی حالت تربی مستامن سے بدرجہا بہتر ہے یعنی ذمی اہل اسلام سے زیادہ قریب ہے۔ اور ذمی اہل اسلام سے زیادہ قریب اس لئے ہے کہ ذمی نے اسلام کا خلیفہ یعنی جزیہ قبول کر لیا ہے اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ مسلمان کی طرح ذمی کا خون محفوظ ہو گیا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مسلمان نے کسی ذمی کو ناحق عمد اقتل کر دیا تو مسلمان کو قصاص میں قتل کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر مسلمان کسی حربی مستامن کو قتل کر ڈالے تو اس کے قصاص میں مسلمان کو قتل نہیں کیا جاتا۔ بہر حال ذمی کی حالت ، حربی مستامن سے بہت بہتر ہے اور اسلام ے قریب ہونے میں اعلیٰ حال والے کے خلاف ادنیٰ حال والے کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جاتی ۔ لہذاذمی کے خلاف حربی مستامن کی گواہی قبول نہ ہوگی۔
فوان صاحب ہدایہ نے حربی سے حربی مستامن اس لئے مراد لیا ہے کہ حربی غیر مستامن کی گواہی ناممکن ہے کیونکہ شہادت کے لئے قاضی کی مجلس ضروری ہے اور قضاء کے لئے دار اسلام میں مصر اور شہر کا ہونا شرط ہے پس حربی غیر مستامن جو دار الحرب میں مقیم ہے وہ اس . شرط کو کس طرح پورا کر سکتا ہے۔ اور اگر حربی دار الاسلام میں بغیر امان کے داخل ہو کر مجلس قضاء میں حاضر ہو گیا تو اس کو چونکہ قبر اور غلبہ پکڑا جائے گا اس لئے وہ غلام ہو گا اور غلام کی گواہی نہ کسی کے حق میں قبول کی جاتی ہے اور نہ کسی کے خلا قبول کی جاتی ہے۔
Testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not accepted. He (al-Quduri) meant, and Allah knows best, the musta'min, because he has no wilayah over him, because the dhimmi is from the people of our dar and he is in a higher state than him. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri said that the testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not accepted. Sahib al-Hidayah said that by harbi is meant the one who entered dar al-Islam under aman, i.e., the harbi musta'min. The proof is that the harbi musta'min has no wilayah over the dhimmi, because the harbi musta'min is a resident of dar al-harb and the dhimmi is a resident of dar al-Islam. Rationally, difference of dar severs wilayah. So when he has no right of wilayah, his testimony is not accepted because only those who have wilayah are qualified for testimony. Also, the dhimmi's state is far better than the musta'min's; he is closer to Islam because he has accepted jizya and his blood is protected like a Muslim's. Al-Marghinani specified that by 'harbi' is meant the musta'min because testimony of a harbi who has no aman is impossible, as he cannot appear before the qadi in dar al-Islam, and if he enters without aman he becomes a slave, and a slave's testimony is not accepted.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi. The author states the ruling: the testimony of a harbi is not accepted against a dhimmi. Al-Hidayah clarifies that 'harbi' here means the harbi musta'min (one who entered dar al-Islam with a safe-conduct). The reasoning is twofold: First, there is no wilayah (authority/guardianship) between them because of the difference in dar (territory) — the musta'min belongs to dar al-harb and the dhimmi to dar al-Islam. Second, the dhimmi is in a higher state, being closer to Islam (by accepting jizya and enjoying protected status), and the testimony of a lower-status person against a higher-status person is not accepted. The author also explains why they interpret 'harbi' as musta'min: a harbi without aman cannot physically appear before the qadi in dar al-Islam, and if he enters without aman he is captured and becomes a slave, and a slave's testimony is universally rejected. Thus, the ruling applies specifically to the musta'min. This is a clear Hanafi position based on rational proofs and the principle of wilayah.

Key Terms
حربی (harbi): A person from dar al-harb, enemy territory; in this context, the harbi who enters dar al-Islam under aman (musta'min).
ذمی (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living in dar al-Islam under a pact of protection (dhimma), paying jizya.
مستامن (musta'min): A harbi who enters dar al-Islam with a temporary safe-conduct (aman) for trade or other purpose.
ولایت (wilayah): Authority or guardianship; a condition for testimony in Hanafi law — the witness must have some form of authority over the parties.

D) Because the dhimmi is a non-Muslim and the harbi is also a non-Muslim, so their testimonies are equal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the testimony of a harbi musta'min against a dhimmi is invalid due to lack of wilayah and the dhimmi's superior status.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Testimony of a Dhimmi Against a Harbi and Musta'mins' Mutual Testimony
Rulings on dhimmi and musta'min testimony with proof from wilaya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on dhimmi and musta'min testimony, and explain the role of wilaya 'amma and ikhtilaf al-darayn in these rulings.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's testimony is accepted against a harbi due to general wilayah; musta'mins must share a country for their testimony to stand.

This lesson examines two related rulings from the Hanafi school on the acceptance of testimony involving non-Muslims in dar al-Islam. The first concerns a dhimmi (non-Muslim subject) testifying against a harbi (enemy non-Muslim). The second addresses testimony among musta'mins (temporary residents) from different territories. The key concepts of wilaya 'amma (general authority) and ikhtilaf al-darayn (difference of abodes) determine the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and note the two separate rulings: (1) testimony of a dhimmi against a harbi is accepted, (2) testimony of musta'mins against each other is accepted only if they are from the same country (dar).
The passage also contrasts the dhimmi with the musta'min to highlight why the ruling differs.
2
Understand the proof for dhimmi testimony
The rationale is that the dhimmi has a higher status due to his residence in dar al-Islam, giving him a general wilayah (wilaya 'amma) that extends to testifying against outsiders.
This is an istihsan based on the analogy with a Muslim's testimony against a harbi.
3
Understand the condition for musta'min testimony
Musta'mins from different countries lack mutual wilayah because difference of territory (ikhtilaf al-darayn) severs legal ties. Hence, their testimony against each other is not accepted.
This principle also blocks inheritance between residents of different dars.
4
Resolve the apparent contradiction
A question arises: if ikhtilaf al-darayn severs wilayah, why is a dhimmi's testimony accepted against a harbi from another dar? The answer: the dhimmi's general wilayah comes from dar al-Islam itself, not from a personal tie to the harbi.
Thus, the dhimmi's testimony is an exception due to the nobility of dar al-Islam.
